801 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Herron


No. 1-09-0663


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


965 N.E.2d 1263; 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 101; 2012 IL App (1st) 090663; 358 Ill. Dec. 784



February 14, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 07 CR 21144. Honorable Timothy Joseph Joyce Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; remanded for resentencing on the conviction for aggravated kidnapping.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which found him guilty of intimidation, home invasion, armed robbery, and aggravated kidnapping, 720 ILCS 5/10-2(a)(6) (2006).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed: (1) the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he was involved in any of the offenses due to deficiencies in the witnesses' identifications; (2) his sentence for aggravated kidnapping violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution (Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 (1970)); and (3) his sentence for aggravated kidnapping should be vacated. The appeals court found a rational trier of fact could have found defendant guilty of intimidation, home invasion, armed robbery and aggravated kidnapping beyond a reasonable doubt, as the witnesses had ample opportunity to view him during the crime. The State conceded the 15-year enhancement on his sentence for aggravated kidnapping violated the proportionate penalties clause and was therefore unconstitutional. Due to the enhancement, the sentencing range for aggravated kidnapping was greater than the sentencing range for the similar offense of armed violence predicated on kidnapping. Following Gibson, the appeals court found the trial court had the opportunity to view and weigh the significance of all the evidence and thus was in a better position to impose a sentence for aggravated kidnapping.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for intimidation, home invasion, armed robbery, and aggravated kidnapping were affirmed. The sentence for aggravated kidnapping was vacated, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for resentencing on the conviction for aggravated kidnapping.

 

802 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Oshana


No. 2-10-1144


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


965 N.E.2d 1174; 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 99; 2012 IL App (2d) 101144; 358 Ill. Dec. 695



February 9, 2012, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 23, 2012.
Appeal denied by People v. Oshana, 968 N.E.2d 1070, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 829, 360 Ill. Dec. 317 (Ill., May 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 09-CF-1166. Honorable Timothy Q. Sheldon, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) convicting him of two counts of workers' compensation fraud under 820 ILCS 305/25.5(a) (2006), sentencing him to 24 months' probation, and ordering him to pay $ 22, 594 in restitution to the administrator of workers' compensation benefits for defendant's employer to reimburse it for the costs of investigating defendant's workers' compensation claim and its attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The evidence was insufficient to support defendant's conviction under count I because nothing in his initial application for workers' compensation benefits or the 820 ILCS 305/19(b) (2006) petition required him to state whether he was totally disabled from working, and therefore his failure to disclose his temporary light-duty work did not render his workers' compensation claim false or fraudulent. However, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction under count II because the evidence showed that defendant consistently represented to his treating physician that his level of pain was a nine or ten, leading the physician to conclude that he 85 percent or more disabled but contrary to those representations, defendant had been working light duty at two construction sites for 27 days. The court held that 820 ILCS 305/25.5 was not unconstitutionally vague because the terms "false or fraudulent" and "material representation" were within the daily vocabulary of ordinary people and therefore did not have to be defined in the statute.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction on count II was affirmed, but his conviction on count I was reversed. The order of restitution was reduced to $ 12,923. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

803 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jackson


No. 1-10-0398


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


965 N.E.2d 623; 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 83; 2012 IL App (1st) 100398; 358 Ill. Dec. 552



February 7, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Jackson, 968 N.E.2d 1069, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 782, 360 Ill. Dec. 316 (Ill., May 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 07 CR 1061. Honorable Lawrence Edward Flood, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of two aggravated criminal sexual assault counts and one criminal sexual abuse count. On appeal, he primarily challenged the constitutionality of that part of the Illinois Juvenile Court Act of 1987 directing automatic transfer of a juvenile age 15 or over to adult criminal court based on being charged with certain Class X felonies.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly sexually assaulted the young victim over more than a one-year time period at the place where he resided. Pursuant to the automatic transfer provision of the Illinois Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 ILCS 405/5-130 et seq. (2006) (Juvenile Court Act), his case proceeded in criminal court because he was statutorily excluded from the jurisdiction of juvenile court for being at least 15-years-old and accused of aggravated criminal sexual assault. A jury found him guilty on two counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault and one count of criminal sexual abuse. On appeal, he primarily claimed that the automatic transfer provision was unconstitutional. He also challenged evidentiary rulings and the sufficiency of the evidence. The appellate court found that the automatic transfer provision violated neither his substantive nor procedural due process rights since it was rationally related to handling specific violent crimes by young offenders and only applied to 15-year-olds and 16-year-olds who committed them. It also found that he did not show reversible error regarding the evidentiary rulings or that the evidence was insufficient to support the guilty verdict.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

804 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Spencer


No. 1-10-2094


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


2012 IL App (1st) 102094; 965 N.E.2d 1135; 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 82; 358 Ill. Dec. 656



February 6, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Spencer, 2014 Ill. LEXIS 36 (Ill., Jan. 29, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 09 CR 06736. Honorable Nicholas Ford, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of unlawful use of a weapon in violation of 720 ILCS 5/24-1.1 (2008) and sentenced him to serve three years in the Illinois Department of Corrections, with a recommendation for boot camp. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after a bench trial of unlawful use of a weapon in violation of 720 ILCS 5/24-1.1 (2008). After sentencing, he claimed on appeal that the State had not proven his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt and that 720 ILCS 5/24-1.1 (2008) violated his Second Amendment right to bear arms. The appellate court found that a rational trier of fact could have found that he constructively possessed the revolver and ammunition recovered at the time police searched his residence and that the State had proven the essential elements of that offense, committed by a felon, beyond a reasonable doubt. As to the constitutional claim, it first found that he could raise that claim on appeal because a constitutional challenge to a statute could be raised at anytime. It also found an intermediate level of scrutiny applied, which meant that the challenged statutory provision had to serve a significant, substantial, or important governmental interest, and the fit between the challenged law and the asserted objective had to be reasonable. It then found that under that test, the statute was constitutional because defendant as a convicted felon was not protected by the Second Amendment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and sentence.

 

805 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nichols


No. 2-10-0028


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


964 N.E.2d 1190; 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 37; 2012 IL App (2d) 100028; 358 Ill. Dec. 168



January 18, 2012, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 2, 2012.
Appeal denied by People v. Nichols, 968 N.E.2d 1070, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 739, 360 Ill. Dec. 317 (Ill., May 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 08-CF-3797. Honorable George Bridges, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) of two counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault and sentenced to the statutory minimum of 32 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the mandatory consecutive sentencing statute, 730 ILCS 5/5-8-4, was unconstitutional as applied to him and violated Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court duly noted the substantial testimony at sentencing that defendant was a good person and that the crime was out of character for him. The trial court went on, however, to note reports of defendant's poor behavior while incarcerated. First, defendant was expelled from a GED class for his poor efforts and horseplay. Second, defendant was placed in isolation for using vulgar language toward staff, making sexually explicit comments to a therapist, and being noncompliant. The court inferred from those reports that defendant was indeed capable of acting "outside of his character." The sex offender evaluator found that defendant was at a "moderate" risk to reoffend, based on his young age and other factors, including potential for psychopathy and unrealistic plans and negative attitude toward intervention. At the time of sentencing, defendant had taken few steps that showed definite rehabilitative potential.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

806 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Tri-Power Res., Inc. v. City of Carlyle


NO. 5-11-0075


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


2012 IL App (5th) 110075; 967 N.E.2d 811; 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 11; 359 Ill. Dec. 781; 84 A.L.R.6th 663



January 6, 2012, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 25, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Clinton County. No. 05-MR-91. Honorable William J. Becker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Clinton County, Illinois, granted the motion filed by appellant company to certify a question for interlocutory appeal pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 308, in the proceeding with appellee city. The certified question was whether a non-home-rule unit had the authority to prohibit or bar the drilling or operation of an oil or gas well within its municipal limits?


OVERVIEW: The city was a non-home-rule unit of government. The company entered into an oil and gas lease with the owners of the mineral interests in a 67-acre parcel of land. The company argued that the city had the limited authority to regulate the drilling or operation of an oil or gas well within its municipal limits, but it was not authorized to bar or prohibit such activity. The company claimed that as a non-home-rule unit of government, the city lacked the authority to prohibit the drilling or operation of an oil or gas well within its municipal limits. The appellate court ruled that a non-home-rule unit of government could prohibit the drilling or operation of an oil or gas well within its municipal limits. 225 ILCS 725/13 provided a city the power to prohibit the operation of an oil or gas well within its municipal limits. 65 ILCS 5/11-56-1 (2004) provided local units of government the power to regulate and permit local oil and gas mining. Pursuant to 225 ILCS 725/13, a municipality could block the Illinois Department of Natural Resources' issuance of a permit to operate an oil or gas well within its municipal limits.


OUTCOME: The certified question was answered in the affirmative, and the case was remanded.

 

807 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Robinson


No. 1-10-0078


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


964 N.E.2d 551; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1321; 2011 IL App (1st) 100078; 357 Ill. Dec. 872



December 30, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Robinson, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 1042 (Ill., Sept. 26, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 09 CR 03878. Honorable Joseph M. Claps, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, convicting him of unlawful use of a weapon by a felon (UUW), 720 ILCS 5/24-1.1(a) (2008).


OVERVIEW: The parties stipulated that a.38-caliber bluesteel revolver was found by police in the stove in the kitchen of the apartment and that a box containing 50 live rounds of.32-caliber ammunition was recovered from a kitchen cabinet. Defendant argued that the appellate court should declare the UUW statute unconstitutional and vacate his conviction under that statute, because it violated his right to bear arms as embodied by the Second Amendment to the United States Constitution. The appellate court ruled that the UUW statute did not, on its face, violate the Second Amendment, and the UUW statute did not require the State to show any improper purpose for the felon's possession of a firearm. Because the UUW statute constituted a valid exercise of the government's right to protect the health, safety and general welfare of its citizens, the UUW statute was a constitutionally permissible restriction of the Second Amendment right to bear arms. The restriction served a substantial governmental interest and was proportional to the interest served. There was a longstanding prohibition on the possession of firearms by felons.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Alvarado


No. 1-08-2957


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 082957; 964 N.E.2d 532; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1322; 357 Ill. Dec. 853



December 30, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by, Vacated by People v. Alvarado, 2014 Ill. LEXIS 19, 378 Ill. Dec. 740, 4 N.E.3d 1112 (Ill., 2014)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by People v. Alvarado, 2014 IL App (1st) 082957-UB, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1482 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 07 CR 398. The Honorable Mary Margaret Brosnahan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (AUUW) in violation of 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6(a)(1), (a)(3)(C) (2006) and sentencing him to two years of probation.


OVERVIEW: The court vacated one of defendant's two convictions for AUUW under the one act, one crime rule because both convictions were based on the same, single act of possession of the same revolver. The court held that defense counsel was not ineffective for allegedly eliciting testimony that suggested that the offense was gang-related because counsel's challenged actions were reasonable and consistent with the strategy to discredit the testimony of the State's witnesses that the officers saw defendant in the street carrying the gun. The court held that 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6(a)(1), (a)(3)(C) was constitutional under the Second Amendment because, under intermediate scrutiny, the fit between the statute and its substantial and important goal of reducing the armed violence and illegal activity of street gangs, was reasonable. The statute did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because it did not burden a fundamental right, as it did not impinge on conduct at the core of the Second Amendment right. Defendant cited no case law showing that he had a fundamental right to carry on or about his person a handgun when he was not on his own land or in his abode or fixed place of business.


OUTCOME: One of defendant's conviction for AUUW was vacated. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

People v. M.I. (In re M.I.)


No. 1-10-0865


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


964 N.E.2d 72; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1293; 2011 IL App (1st) 100865; 357 Ill. Dec. 709



December 23, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by People v. M.I. (In re M.I.), 968 N.E.2d 82, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 603, 360 Ill. Dec. 3 (Ill., Mar. 28, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 09 JD 1621. Honorables Paul Stralka and Terrence V. Sharkey, Judges Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) adjudicated respondent juvenile delinquent after finding him guilty of aggravated discharge of a firearm and aggravated unlawful use of a weapon. It then sentenced him to an indeterminate term in the Juvenile Department of Corrections, and pursuant to the extended jurisdiction juvenile statute, he received an adult sentence to be stayed pending successful completion of his juvenile sentence. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was adjudicated delinquent after the trial court found him guilty of three counts of aggravated discharge of a firearm and two counts of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon. The trial court sentenced him to an indeterminate term in the Juvenile Department of Corrections, to end no later than his 21st birthday, and pursuant to the extended juvenile jurisdiction (EJJ) statute, he received an adult sentence to be stayed pending successful completion of his juvenile sentence. On appeal, he argued that: (1) the State did not prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of aggravated discharge of a firearm; (2) the trial court failed to timely conduct an EJJ hearing; and (3) the EJJ statue was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court found that the State provided sufficient evidence to prove the juvenile guilty of 720 ILCS 5/24-1.2(a)(3) (2008) aggravated discharge of a firearm, that 705 ILCS 405/5-810(2) (2008) regarding the time for holding an EJJ hearing was directory, not mandatory, and that he lacked standing to challenge 705 ILCS 405/5-810(6) (2008)'s constitutionality regarding imposition of adult sentences, as he had not yet been affected by that statute.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Williams


No. 1-09-1667


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 091667-B; 962 N.E.2d 1148; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1264; 357 Ill. Dec. 247



December 15, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 08 CR 16364. Honorable Kenneth J. Wadas, Judge Presiding.
People v. Williams, 953 N.E.2d 933, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1324, 352 Ill. Dec. 252 (Ill., 2011)
People v. Williams, 405 Ill. App. 3d 958, 940 N.E.2d 95, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1284, 346 Ill. Dec. 95 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of two counts of unlawful use of a weapon by a felon and six counts of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (AUUW). At sentencing, all counts were merged into one AUUW conviction and defendant was sentenced to five years in prison, with 308 days' credit for the time he served awaiting trial. Defendant was also assessed costs totaling $715. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found to be in possession of a handgun and ammunition while standing on a public street, thus negating any possible application of the holding concerning possession of handguns in the home. Because 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6(a)(1), (a)(3)(A) (2008) of the AUUW statute applied to the situation in which defendant found himself, being in a public place with a handgun, he could not argue for relief based on the possibility that the AUUW might be unconstitutional as applied to a felon in possession of a handgun in his own home. Judgments of conviction were entered for defendant, and the fact that those convictions were not among those enumerated by 55 ILCS 5/5-1103 (2008) for imposition of a court services fee of $25 without entry of conviction did not void the assessment. Further, because 730 ILCS 5/5-4-3 mandated that a convicted felon submit a DNA sample and pay the analysis fee, the appellate court presumed the circuit court followed the law and assessed the fee on defendant as part of either of the sentences imposed on his prior felony convictions and that fee was not imposed again in the current case.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, vacated the judgment in part, and remanded the case with directions to modify the mittimus to accord with the findings regarding the imposition of certain costs and the application of pretrial incarceration credit.

Hubbard St. Lofts LLC v. Inland Bank


No. 1-10-2640


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 102640; 963 N.E.2d 262; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1255; 357 Ill. Dec. 309



December 13, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Hubbard St. Lofts LLC v. Inland Bank, 968 N.E.2d 81, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 545, 360 Ill. Dec. 2 (Ill., Mar. 28, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 09 CH 49410. Honorable Mary Anne Mason, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff debtor filed a class action against defendants, a bank and its successor-in-interest (collectively, the lender), alleging, inter alia, violations of the Illinois Interest Act (Interest Act), 815 ILCS 205/1 et seq. (2010), and the Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Practices Act (Consumer Fraud Act), 815 ILCS 505/1 et seq. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the lender's motion to dismiss with prejudice. The debtor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The debtor, a limited liability company and an individual, obtained a loan from the lender. The promissory note identified the 365/360 method as the applicable method for computing interest. A dispute arose out of the lender's use of the 365/360 method. The debtor claimed that interest had to be calculated pursuant to 815 ILCS 205/4, 9, and 10 of the Interest Act. However, 815 ILCS 205/4 did not apply to corporations and 815 ILCS 205/9 and 10 were gap-filling provisions that only applied when no time period for calculation of interest appeared anywhere in the instrument in question. Furthermore, there was no action under the Consumer Fraud Act because the terms used in the note were clearly unambiguous and nothing in the record indicated deception. Therefore, in the light most favorable to the debtor, the allegations of the complaint were insufficient to state a cause of action upon which relief could have been granted, and the trial court correctly granted the lender's motion to dismiss with prejudice, pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-615 (2010).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Shachter v. City of Chicago


No. 1-10-3582


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 103582; 962 N.E.2d 586; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1229; 356 Ill. Dec. 901



December 5, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Shachter v. City of Chicago, 968 N.E.2d 88, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 675, 360 Ill. Dec. 9 (Ill., Mar. 28, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 09 MI 450812. Honorable William G. Pileggi, Judge Presiding.
Shachter v. City of Chi., 2013 IL App (1st) 120986-U, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 3384 (Mar. 25, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which upheld a decision of defendants, the city, a municipal corporation, the department of administrative hearings, and the department of streets and sanitation, finding that the property owner had violated Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code §§ 7-28-120(a), 10-32-050, involving the care of his property and the parkway outside his home.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by denying the property owner's petition for substitution of the judge because he could not establish a violation of 735 ILCS 5/2-1001 (2008) as the petition was premised upon the trial court's handling of his written specification of errors and defendants' written response thereto. In addition, the property owner was not prejudiced, as his petition contained no assertions of any extrajudicial source of bias or prejudice. The court rejected the property owner's contention that the administrative proceedings were void under 65 ILCS 5/1-2.1-4(d) (2008) because he did not challenge the fact that both he and the administrative law officer had copies of the notice of ordinance violation at the administrative hearing, a copy of the notice had been properly served on the property owner, and a copy of the document appeared in the administrative record. The court rejected the property owner's claim that he did not receive proper notice of the administrative proceeding against him under Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 2-14-074(b) because it contained all of the information necessary to determine the issuing officer's identity.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

814 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Crawford


No. 2-10-0533


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


961 N.E.2d 447; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1203; 2011 IL App (2d) 100533; 356 Ill. Dec. 351



November 21, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 6, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 09-CF-3041. Honorable Kathryn E. Creswell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, Illinois, which sentenced him to five years of imprisonment after a conviction for forgery under 720 ILCS 5/17-3(a)(2) (2008).


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that imposing probation in this case would have depreciated the seriousness of the offense, so a five year prison term was imposed under 730 ILCS 5/5-6-1(a) (2008). Defendant then sought review, arguing that this violated the decision in Apprendi v. New Jersey. In affirming, the appellate court determined that, since defendant was found guilty of a Class 3 felony, an appropriate sentence included a term of imprisonment, which could not have exceeded five years. Therefore, although the sentence in this case was the maximum, it was still appropriate for a Class 3 felony. There was nothing suggesting that probation was the maximum sentence. Deciding whether probation or imprisonment was appropriate for defendant after considering the circumstances of the offense and defendant's individual characteristics was the type of decision that judges routinely made in sentencing. The jury did not have to be involved in that decision. Moreover, not every fact with a bearing on sentencing had to be determined by a jury.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

815 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Salas


No. 1-09-1880


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 091880; 961 N.E.2d 831; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1195; 356 Ill. Dec. 442



November 21, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Salas, 968 N.E.2d 87, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 631, 360 Ill. Dec. 8 (Ill., 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Salas v. Illinois, 133 S. Ct. 276, 184 L. Ed. 2d 163, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 6379 (U.S., 2012)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Salas, 2015 IL App (1st) 132280-U, 2015 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1032 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 07 CR 21201. Honorable Marcus R. Salone, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, that convicted him of first-degree murder, arguing that the automatic transfer statute, 705 ILCS 405/5-130 (2008), violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII, that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on self-defense, and that his counsel was ineffective in failing to request a jury instruction on the lesser offense of involuntary manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the automatic transfer statute, 705 ILCS 405/5-130 (2008), which required that 15- and 16-year-old defendants charged with first-degree murder be prosecuted in adult court and not juvenile court, did not violate the Eighth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VIII, because it did not impose any penalty but merely provided the forum where guilt would be adjudicated. The trial court did not err in failing to instruct on self-defense because defendant never admitted killing the victim and failed to present evidence that he reasonably believed deadly force was necessary to prevent death or great bodily harm to himself. Where defendant denied using any force against the victim, he could not claim to have acted in self-defense. Further counsel did not err in failing to request an involuntary manslaughter instruction. The State presented evidence that defendant intentionally killed the victim by a shot to the back of the head, defendant denied shooting and killing the victim, but there was no evidence that defendant recklessly killed the victim. In the absence of evidence of recklessness, defendant was not entitled to an involuntary manslaughter instruction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

816 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gay


NO. 4-10-0009


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


960 N.E.2d 1272; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1197; 2011 IL App (4th) 100009; 356 Ill. Dec. 149



November 18, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Gay, 968 N.E.2d 84, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 433, 360 Ill. Dec. 5 (Ill., 2012)
Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Gay, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 807, 2012 IL App (4th) 100369-U (2012)
Related proceeding at People v. Gay, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 856, 2012 IL App (4th) 100360-U (2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gay v. Ill., 133 S. Ct. 270, 184 L. Ed. 2d 147, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 6175 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. No. 03CF172. Honorable Robert M. Travers, Judge Presiding.
People v. Gay, 376 Ill. App. 3d 796, 878 N.E.2d 805, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1171, 316 Ill. Dec. 83 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Livingston County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed defendant's amended postconviction petition filed in his aggravated battery case involving him striking a prison guard in the face with a liquid substance that had a urine-like odor. It did so after a second-stage nonevidentiary hearing upon finding he had not made a substantial showing that his constitutional rights were violated. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed defendant's amended postconviction petition following a second-stage nonevidentiary hearing. He claimed on appeal that he made substantial showings that: (1) his aggregate sentence in the present case and other unconsolidated cases violated the constitutional prohibition against cruel and unusual punishments; (2) the State subverted his constitutional rights to due process and a speedy trial by engaging in tactical preindictment delay; (3) he received ineffective assistance of appellate counsel by counsel not arguing that the ordering of a fitness hearing circumvented defendant's speedy-trial request; and (4) the Department of Corrections citation issued to him insufficiently advised him. The appellate court found that: (1) defendant's aggregated 97-year sentence on his 16 felony convictions was not a de facto life sentence without parole; (2) any preindictment delay had no effect on his due process or speedy-trial rights; (3) collateral estoppel barred reconsideration of the ineffective assistance argument; and (4) he did not show the criminal offense or the disciplinary proceedings inadequately informed him as to the offense he committed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

817 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Montyce H.


No. 1-10-1788


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 101788; 959 N.E.2d 221; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1184; 355 Ill. Dec. 193



November 18, 2011, Decided 
November 18, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 11, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 09 JD 3959. Honorable Carl Anthony Walker, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a 15-year-old juvenile, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, that adjudicated him delinquent for having committed aggravated unlawful use of a weapon under 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6(a) (2008), arguing that the aggravated unlawful use of a weapon statute, which criminalized the possession of a loaded, uncased, and accessible firearm outside the home, violated his constitutional right to bear arms.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile asserted a facial challenge to the aggravated unlawful use of a weapon statute, contending that it violated his constitutional right to bear arms. Noting that it had considered this identical argument on several occasions and found that the statute constitutional, the court applied the intermediate scrutiny analysis and again determined that the statute survived a constitutional challenge. Specifically, the statute served an important governmental objective; its overall purpose was to protect the public and police enforcement officers from the inherent dangers or threats to safety posed by any person carrying in public a loaded and accessible firearm on his person or in his vehicle. Further, the means employed were substantially related to the objective. The statute did not impose a blanket prohibition on carrying firearms outside of the home but was limited to prevent the carrying of loaded, uncased, and accessible firearms in public on the street. The prohibition was justified by the potential deadly consequences to innocent members of the general public when someone carrying a loaded and accessible gun was mistaken about his need for defense or was just a poor shot.


OUTCOME: The adjudication of delinquency was affirmed.

People v. Donelson

Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Donelson, 2014 IL App (1st) 140295-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2930 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) dismissed the pro se petition for relief from judgment defendant filed pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-1401(f) (2008) in a case where defendant was convicted of first degree murder, home invasion, and aggravated criminal sexual assault, and he ultimately received concurrent sentences of 50 years, 30 years, and 30 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to charges of first-degree murder, aggravated criminal sexual assault, and home invasion. Pursuant to a guilty plea, he was convicted of first degree murder, home invasion, and aggravated criminal sexual assault. He received concurrent sentences of 50 years, 30 years, and 30 years. A mittimus was eventually issued reflecting a sentence of 50 years for the murder and 30 years for the home invasion. The trial court then dismissed his pro se motion for relief from judgment that he filed and in which he challenged various aspects of his guilty plea rather than his concurrent sentencing. On appeal, he challenged the concurrent sentences as being void. The appellate court found that since he was challenging the sentences as being void, under the law he could raise that challenge at any time. It also found that an aggravated criminal sexual assault conviction under 720 ILCS 5/12-14 (1998) triggered mandatory consecutive sentences due to defendant's convictions on multiple offenses regardless of whether a single course of conduct or multiple courses of conduct were involved, and resentencing had to be within the plea agreement and the relevant, applicable statutes.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated defendant's sentences and remanded for resentencing consistent with both the plea agreement and relevant statutes.

Carr v. Koch


NO. 4-11-0117


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


960 N.E.2d 640; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1121; 2011 IL App (4th) 110117; 355 Ill. Dec. 758



October 28, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Carr v. Koch, 963 N.E.2d 244, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 94, 357 Ill. Dec. 291 (Ill., 2012)
Affirmed by Carr v. Koch, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 1529, 2012 IL 113414 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 10MR169. Honorable Patrick J. Londrigan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) that dismissed their action against defendants, education superintendent, board of education, and governor, in which they sought a declaration that the Illinois education funding system found in 105 ILCS 5/18-8.05 (2010) in violation of the equal-protection clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers claimed the state's education funding system had the effect of requiring taxpayers in school districts with low property values to pay property taxes to fund local public schools at a higher rate than similarly situated taxpayers--that is, taxpayers owning similarly valued real property--in school districts with high property values, which violated § 2. The appellate court found, inter alia, that the state neither rewarded nor punished the taxpayers' school districts for exceeding the statutory tax rates on which the state based its aid calculation. Any injury incurred by higher tax rates could not be fairly traceable to defendants' actions. Moreover, a declaration that the state's funding scheme was unconstitutional would not redress the taxpayers' claimed injury. Therefore, the taxpayers did not allege an actual or threatened injury. Since their claim of higher tax rates could not be fairly traceable to the defendants' actions, they lacked standing to challenge § 18-8.05. Consequently, the trial court did not err in granting the defendants' motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Lara


NO. 4-08-0983


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


958 N.E.2d 719; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1078; 2011 IL App (4th) 080983-B; 354 Ill. Dec. 787



September 29, 2011, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Woodford County. No. 08CF55. Honorable John B. Huschen, Judge Presiding.
People v. Lara, 402 Ill. App. 3d 257, 932 N.E.2d 1052, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 688, 342 Ill. Dec. 591 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, the Circuit Court of Woodford County (Illinois) convicted defendant of predatory criminal sexual assault 720 ILCS 5/12-14.1(a)(1) (2006). He was sentenced to 12 years in prison. The judgment was affirmed on appeal. Based on a supervisory opinion from the Illinois Supreme Court, the appeal was reopened.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that 725 ILCS 5/115-10 (2006) was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the reliability requirement in 725 ILCS 5/115-10(b)(1) did not affect the constitutionality of the statute because hearsay testimony still had to satisfy Crawford's constitutional requirements, in addition to the statutory requirement of reliability. Further, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the video recording of the interview between the officer and the victim pursuant to 25 ILCS 5/115-10 because the officer did not direct the child victim's answers in the interview. He asked open-ended questions, which she answered. She described conduct with which a typical four- or five-year-old child would not and should not be familiar. Not only did she describe what defendant did, she also described how it felt. Finally, because the victim was available for cross-examination, trial counsel's performance was not deficient for failing to argue that the victim's testimony at trial made her unavailable as a witness. She was present and she answered all of the questions posed by defense counsel.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

People v. Lacy


NO. 5-10-0347


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


2011 IL App (5th) 100347; 958 N.E.2d 351; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1016; 354 Ill. Dec. 608



September 20, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Lacy, 963 N.E.2d 248, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 126, 357 Ill. Dec. 295 (Ill., 2012)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by People v. Lacy, 2013 IL 113216, 2013 Ill. LEXIS 847 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County. No. 09-CF-86. Honorable E. Dan Kimmel & Honorable Ronald R. Eckiss, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jackson County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed the first-degree murder charge filed against defendant and discharged him from custody because defendant was not brought to trial within the statutory speedy trial period. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with first-degree murder. He remained in custody throughout the proceedings. He requested and was granted several continuances, tolling the running of the speedy trial period. Six days before trial was scheduled to begin, the State sought a continuance and an extension of the speedy trial period pursuant to 725 ILCS 5/103-5(c) (2010). The State's motion was granted over defendant's objection, and the trial was rescheduled. Thereafter, the State filed a second motion for continuance under 735 ILCS 5/103-5(c) (2010) to procure the presence of a witness at trial. Defendant objected, but the motion was granted. A different judge then concluded that defendant's speedy trial right had been violated by granting the second continuance because the trial was set outside the speedy trial period. Accordingly, the charge was dismissed and defendant was dismissed from state custody. The appellate court found that dismissal of the charge and discharge was appropriate because 725 ILCS 5/103-5(c) (2010) permitted only one 60-day continuance and the State had other options for trying defendant if it wanted to do so, but it did not use any of those options.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Yoselowitz


Docket No. 4-10-0764


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


2011 IL App (4th) 100764; 960 N.E.2d 564; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1109; 355 Ill. Dec. 682



September 20, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Yoselowitz, 963 N.E.2d 251, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 130, 357 Ill. Dec. 298 (Ill., 2012)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at, Motion granted by People v. Yoselowitz, 2014 IL App (4th) 130212-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1278 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Rule 23 Order Filed September 20, 2011. Appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, No. 09-CF-416; the Hon. Robert L. Freitag, Judge, presiding.
People v. Yoselowitz, 2011 IL App (4th) 100764-U, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2233 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of McLean County, Illinois, which accepted a guilty plea to unlawful possession of more than 5,000 grams of cannabis with intent to deliver, in violation of 720 ILCS 550/5(g) (2008), a Class X felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought to declare 720 ILCS 550/5(g) unconstitutional based on scientific studies relating to cannabis. After defendant was sentenced to 12 years in prison, his motion for reconsideration was denied. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that, even though Ill. Const. art. I, § 11 placed some restraint on the right of the Illinois Legislature to establish penalties for crimes, courts were reluctant to invalidate penalties prescribed by the Legislature. Defendant failed to show that punishing him as a Class X offender by imposing a 12-year prison term was cruel, degrading, or so wholly disproportionate to the offense that it shocked the moral sense of the community. The sentence was not excessive since this was defendant's third drug-related conviction, and the sentence was at the lower end of the potential range. Defendant failed to show an equal protection violation based on the scientific studies, which were more properly given to the Illinois Legislature. There was a rational basis for classifying the crime based on the Legislature's stated and unchanged purpose in enacting the Illinois Cannabis Control Act, 720 ILCS 550/1 (2008).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Moore


Appeal No. 3-09-0993


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


2011 IL App (3d) 090993; 957 N.E.2d 555; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1074; 354 Ill. Dec. 239



September 2, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing October 6, 2011. Released for Publication November 16, 2011.
Rehearing denied by People v. Moore, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1189 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., Oct. 6, 2011)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by People v. Moore, 2015 IL App (3d) 120757-U, 2015 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 13 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois, Circuit No. 09-CF-497. Honorable Chris L. Frederickson and James E. Shadid, Judges, Presiding.
People v. Moore, 2011 IL App (3d) 090993, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 959 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and vacated; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 10th Judicial Circuit Court, Peoria County (Illinois), granted the State's motion to transfer defendant's case of armed robbery from the juvenile court to the criminal court for trial as an adult. After a bench trial, defendant was convicted of the armed robbery charge. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was 13-years-old, was arrested after committing an armed robbery of a bank with an unloaded handgun. Initially, he was charged by juvenile petition. The State then moved to transfer the case from juvenile court to criminal court for him to be tried as an adult. The juvenile court considered the factors under the discretionary transfer provision of the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 ILCS 405/5-805(3)(b) (2008), and after orally pronouncing findings, granted the State's motion to transfer. Defendant was then convicted of armed robbery following a bench trial and was sentenced. The appellate court found that the juvenile court failed to adequately address certain factors. First, it found that no evidence was presented as to the availability and advantages of treatment services in the juvenile system, which was one statutory factor. Also, it determined that the evidence presented at the transfer hearing failed to establish that defendant possessed a deadly weapon, another statutory factor. Too, it found that the juvenile court failed to consider the nonstatutory element of his potential sentence as an adult. As a result, it found the transfer order had to be vacated.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment of conviction, vacated the decision to transfer defendant's case to the criminal court to be tried as an adult, and remanded the case to the juvenile court for further proceedings.

People v. Peters


No. 1-09-2839


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


955 N.E.2d 640; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 901; 2011 IL App (1st) 092839; 353 Ill. Dec. 173



August 22, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 08 CR 16590. Honorable James B. Linn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; mittimus corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child and criminal sexual assault. Defendant was sentenced to natural life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his sentence was violative of the proportionate penalties clause under Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The court of appeals disagreed. The victim testified defendant inserted his penis into her vagina two or three times a week for three years, starting when she was 10 years old, and that defendant threatened to hurt her mother if she ever told anyone what he had done. The victim testified to how defendant inserted his penis into her anus after he discovered she had been writing about the incidents in her diary. The victim testified defendant caused her pain when he rubbed her vaginal area with baby oil prior to the first time he inserted his penis into her vagina, and she also testified he caused her pain when he inserted his penis into her anus. Defendant's repeated sexual assaults of the victim physically harmed her and caused both her and her family severe emotional harm. Further, other victims similarly testified that when defendant was dating their mother he sexually assaulted them for approximately two years, beginning when they were 14 years old and 8 years old.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the mittimus was corrected.

Vlastelica v. Brend

Appeal dismissed by Vlastelica v. Brend, 2014 IL App (1st) 133025-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 883 (2014)
Decision reached on appeal by Vlastelica v. Brend, 2015 IL App (1st) 142524, 2015 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 930 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 10 L 001908. Honorable Kathy M. Flanagan, Judge Presiding.
In re Marriage of Chehaiber, 394 Ill. App. 3d 690, 917 N.E.2d 5, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 909, 334 Ill. Dec. 408 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2009)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted the 735 ILCS 5/2-619 (2010) motion to dismiss filed by defendants, a child representative and his law firm, after plaintiff mother, individually and as next friend of her son, sued them for legal malpractice, intentional breach of fiduciary duty, and intentional interference with her custody rights, related to the child representative's appointment in a divorce action. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: In an underlying divorce action involving the mother, father, and son, visitation and other issues not addressed by the dissolution judgment remained open. In connection with those issues, the trial court appointed the child representative for the son. The child representative remained in that capacity until the dissolution of marriage action was fully adjudicated and became final. Thereafter, the mother filed a three-count complaint against the child representative and his law firm, alleging legal malpractice, intentional breach of fiduciary duty and intentional interference with her custody rights, all related to his representation of the son in the underlying divorce proceeding. The trial court granted the child representative and law firm's 735 ILCS 5/2-619 (2010) motion to dismiss upon finding that they were absolutely immune for his work performed as a child representative in that case. The appellate court found that the child representative had absolute immunity under 750 ILCS 5/506(a) (2010) for work performed within his court-appointed duties. It also found that the law firm as a principal could not be liable since the agent, the child representative, was not liable.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Rivera v. City of Chicago Electoral Bd.


No. 1-11-0283


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


956 N.E.2d 20; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 811; 2011 IL App (1st) 110283; 353 Ill. Dec. 500



July 29, 2011, Decided 
July 29, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 2, 2011.
Appeal denied by Rivera v. City of Chic. Electoral Bd., 962 N.E.2d 489, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 2106, 356 Ill. Dec. 804 (Ill., Nov. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 2011 COEL 12. The Honorable Susan Fox Gillis, Judge Presiding.
Rivera v. City of Chic. Electoral Bd., 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1592 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed; appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed petitioner prospective candidate's petition for administrative review of a decision finding that his candidacy for election as a city alderman was invalid after the trial court found that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction over his cause. The prospective candidate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prospective candidate filed nomination papers to become a candidate in a city aldermanic election. Respondent objectors filed objections. The cause proceeded before a hearing officer pursuant to an order from respondent Board. The hearing officer eventually submitted a recommendation to the Board that the objections be sustained, that his candidacy be declared invalid, and that his name not be printed on the election ballot. The Board issued a written decision that affirmed the recommendation. Although the prospective candidate timely mailed his petition for review of the Board's decision, his petition violated 10 ILCS 5/10-10.1 (2010) because it was not sent registered or certified mail and it was mailed to the relevant parties' attorneys rather than, as that section required, the parties themselves. Although he tried to correct the problems by properly serving the parties, the service was beyond that statute's time limits. The trial court dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The appellate court then found that because the trial court lacked jurisdiction due to his noncompliance with the Illinois Election Code, it lacked jurisdiction to hear his appeal.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment and dismissed the prospective candidate's appeal.

People v. Peterson


Appeal Nos. 3-10-0513, 3-10-0514, 3-10-0515, 3-10-0546, 3-10-0550 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


952 N.E.2d 691; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 774; 2011 IL App (3d) 100513; 351 Ill. Dec. 899



July 26, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 30, 2011. Counsel Amended April 18, 2012.
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Peterson, 958 N.E.2d 284, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1974, 354 Ill. Dec. 541 (Ill., 2011)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by People v. Peterson,968 N.E.2d 204, 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 269, 360 Ill. Dec. 125, 2012 IL App (3d) 100514B (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. Circuit No. 09-CF-1048. Honorable Stephen D. White, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 3-10-0514, Dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. Nos. 3-10-0515 and 3-10-0550, Affirmed; cause remanded. Nos. 3-10-0513 and 3-10-0546, Affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed orders of the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois, that denied its motions in limine to limit certain hearsay statements under the common law doctrine of forfeiture and to admit other crimes evidence and that excluded portions of the proposed testimony of one of its expert witnesses. Defendant moved to dismiss the State's appeal as untimely.


OVERVIEW: In a murder case in which defendant was charged with murdering his estranged third wife in 2004 after his fourth wife disappeared in 2007, the circuit court did not err in precluding the State's expert witness from testifying what the judge in the divorce case would have ultimately ruled at the marital property distribution proceeding had the victim lived or what defendant's attorney in the divorce case would have advised him to expect to occur because experts were not permitted to testify as to statutory interpretation or legal conclusion and were not permitted to offer testimony that was based upon speculation or conjecture. Further, the circuit court did not err in precluding defendant's son from his first marriage, the victim's sister, and defendant's second wife from testifying about instances of domestic violence to show defendant's propensity to commit such crimes because the evidence was too remote in time; although the prior incidents shared some factual similarities to the charged conduct and were arguably relevant to show motive, intent, and propensity, all of the incidents occurred many years before the charged offense, some as many as 22 years earlier.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to dismiss was granted as to those issues for which the State's notice of appeal was untimely filed under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(a)(1). As to the remaining issues, the circuit court's rulings on the admissibility of the evidence was affirmed.

 

828 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Harris


No. 1-09-2251


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 092251; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 779



July 22, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by People v. Harris, 2012 IL App (1st) 092251, 968 N.E.2d 90, 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 297, 360 Ill. Dec. 11 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 04 CR 23182 (01). Honorable Stanley J. Sacks, Judge Presiding.
People v. Harris, 384 Ill. App. 3d 1086, 973 N.E.2d 1087, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 4353, 362 Ill. Dec. 691 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of armed robbery while armed with a firearm and two counts of aggravated kidnaping while armed with a firearm. The trial court sentenced defendant to 20 years' imprisonment for armed robbery and 20 years for aggravated kidnaping, to run concurrently. After defendant's motion for postconviction relief was summarily dismissed, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his sentences violated the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court declined to impose the 15-year add-on penalty to either of defendant's sentences, and his 20-year sentences were, therefore, proper. However, the trial court stated that the reason why it declined to add the 15-year enhancement was that the State did not give proper notice to defendant that it would seek the enhancement, and not that it had any doubts as to whether the add-on penalty was valid. Accordingly, while the sentence imposed by the trial court was proper, the appropriate remedy was to remand for sentencing in accordance with the statute as it existed before it was amended, in order to allow the trial court to determine defendant's sentence for each offense while taking into account the totality of his sentence. However, since the truth-in-sentencing provision under 730 ILCS 5/3-6-3 did not affect the sentencing range imposed for the offenses of aggravated kidnaping and armed violence, but only the manner in which the sentence was carried out, it did not violate the proportionate penalties clause.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for resentencing. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Dupree v. Hardy


No. 4-10-0351


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


960 N.E.2d 1; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 986; 2011 IL App (4th) 100351; 355 Ill. Dec. 558



July 20, 2011, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County No. 09MR55. Honorable Jennifer H. Bauknecht, Judge Presiding.
Dupree v. Hardy, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1715, 2011 IL App (4th) 100351-U (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a petition for a writ of mandamus, alleging that appellees, the warden, the acting warden, and the Director of the Department of Corrections (DOC), acted unlawfully by depriving him of certain property, exercise privileges, and administrative action. The Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois) dismissed the inmate's petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the trial court erred by dismissing his mandamus petition. The appellate court held that the petition for a writ of mandamus was properly dismissed under 735 ILCS 5/2-615 (2008) because the inmate did not have a "right" to access the prison's exercise yard. Also, Ill. Admin. Code tit. 20, § 504.670 gave appellees the discretionary authority to place restrictions on the inmate's exercise-yard privileges. The inmate claimed only that his access to the yard was restricted whenever he received an inmate disciplinary report (IDR). Without more, his claim failed to set forth every material fact required to demonstrate that he is entitled to mandamus relief. Further, the DOC director could delegate the review of the inmate's grievance appeal because he was not required to personally review such appeals. And, the inmate did not allege material facts relating to the "legal and personal property" at issue, nor the circumstances under which appellees purportedly confiscated that property. Prison officials could establish regulations regarding the property inmates could retain in their cells. Finally, he did not have a constitutional right to the appointment of counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Hughes


No. 2-09-0992


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


953 N.E.2d 1017; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 764; 2011 IL App (2d) 090992; 352 Ill. Dec. 336


April 19, 2011, Assigned, Submitted 
July 19, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 2, 2011.
Appeal granted by People v. Hughes, 962 N.E.2d 485, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1887, 356 Ill. Dec. 800 (Ill., 2011)
Affirmed by People v. Hughes, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 1527, 2012 IL 112817 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 99-CF-2426. Honorable Victoria A. Rossetti, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Hughes (In re Hughes), 346 Ill. App. 3d 637, 805 N.E.2d 725, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 214, 282 Ill. Dec. 106 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that denied defendant's motion to vacate a guilty plea he entered to one count of aggravated criminal sexual abuse in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-16 (1998). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After defendant pled guilty to one count of aggravated criminal sexual abuse, he moved to vacate that plea. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, he contended his plea was void because, before he entered it, the State had nol-prossed that charge. He also argued that his plea was not voluntary because he had not been informed it could be the basis for filing a petition to have him civilly committed as a sexually violent person. The appellate court rejected both claims. It noted the State had nol-prossed the charge, but found that the trial court had reacquired jurisdiction over it through the doctrine of revestment because he and the State participated in later proceedings regarding the charge that were inconsistent with that disposition, and without objection. As to plea voluntariness, the appellate court found the petition that the State filed to have him declared to be a sexually violent person was a collateral consequence that the trial court did not have to admonish him about before accepting his plea. It also added that it would not apply the United State Supreme Court's recent Padilla decision regarding deportation to the civil commitment context before it.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Blanton


NO. 4-08-0120


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


955 N.E.2d 92; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 691; 2011 IL App (4th) 080120; 352 Ill. Dec. 916



June 30, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at People v. Blanton, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2148, 2012 IL App (4th) 110998-U (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 07CF488. Honorable Harry E. Clem, Judge Presiding.
People v. Blanton, 396 Ill. App. 3d 230, 925 N.E.2d 703, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1101, 338 Ill. Dec. 847 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Champaign County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of armed robbery. It then sentenced defendant to 25 years in prison on that conviction and noted 15 years was required to be added to his sentence under the mandatory enhancement statute related to the use of firearms. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of armed robbery in violation of 720 ILCS 5/18-2(a)(2) (2006) for holding up a college student with a firearm. The trial court then sentenced defendant to 25 years in prison on that conviction, including 15 years added on under the mandatory enhancement statute related to the use of firearms, 720 ILCS 5/18-2(b) (2006). On appeal, he contended that (1) the trial court violated Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 431(b) by not informing jurors that his failure to testify could not be used against him; (2) his sentence violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution; and (3) the trial court improperly considered as an aggravating sentencing factor. The appellate court found that he was not entitled to plain-error review relief, as even though the trial court erred in instructing the jurors under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 431(b), he did not show that a biased jury had been seated. It also found that the 15-year sentence enhancement violated the proportionate penalties clause of the Illinois Constitution, meaning he had to be resentenced without that enhancement and that he waived the sentencing factor challenging by raising for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of armed robbery. However, it vacated his 25-year sentence and remanded his case to the trial court for resentencing without the imposition of the 15-year firearm enhancement.

People v. Gutierrez


No. 1-09-3499


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


954 N.E.2d 365; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 717; 2011 IL App (1st) 093499; 352 Ill. Dec. 505



June 30, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 20, 2011. Released for Publication August 8, 2011.
Appeal denied by People v. Gutierrez, 962 N.E.2d 485, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1891, 356 Ill. Dec. 800 (Ill., 2011)
Habeas corpus proceeding at United States ex rel. Lazaro Gutierrez #r-57154 v. Pfister, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 5544 (N.D. Ill., Jan. 14, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 CR 999201. Honorable Nicholas Ford, Judge Presiding.
People v. Gutierrez, 229 Ill. 2d 678, 900 N.E.2d 1121, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 1688, 326 Ill. Dec. 874 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that denied defendant's request for leave to file a successive postconviction petition. In the underlying case, he had pled guilty to one count of first-degree murder. In denying his request for leave, the trial court assessed court costs and fees, which included a $ 50 State's Attorney fee. Defendant appealed the denial of his request and imposition of the State's Attorney fee.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot another man to death. He decided to plead guilty to one count of first degree murder. The trial court extensively admonished him about his rights. Defendant said he understood everything and the State presented a factual basis for the plea. The trial court then found him guilty. Later, it dismissed his pro se postconviction petition. It also imposed court costs and fees, which included a $ 50 State's Attorney fee. Thereafter, it denied his request for leave to file a successive postconviction petition. The appellate court found that denial of his leave request was proper since he could not show the cause and prejudice required by 725 ILCS 5/122-1(f) (2006) allowing him to file it. It did so upon finding he could not have prevailed at trial given the overwhelming evidence against him. It also rejected his argument that he was not informed of the possible immigration consequences of his plea, as required by 725 ILCS 5/113-8 (2006), because that was not a required constitutional claim. However, it found the State's Attorney fee imposed under 55 ILCS 5/4-2002.1(a) (2006) had to be vacated since the State had not been involved in his first postconviction petition.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied defendant leave to file his successive postconviction petition, but vacated the $ 50 State's Attorney fee that the trial court imposed.

People v. Span


No. 1-08-3037


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


955 N.E.2d 100; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 700; 2011 IL App (1st) 083037; 352 Ill. Dec. 924



June 30, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 8, 2011.
Appeal denied by People v. Span, 968 N.E.2d 1071, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 692, 360 Ill. Dec. 318 (Ill., May 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 06-12551. Honorable John J. Scotillo, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after it found guilty of attempted armed robbery and aggravated battery. It then imposed concurrent prison sentences of 25 years on the attempted armed robbery conviction and five years on the aggravated battery conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered the store carrying a bludgeon, struck the store cashier, attempted to open the store's cash register, and then struck the cashier again. His conduct was caught on a surveillance video. An investigating police officer recognized him from the video. Too, defendant's fingerprints were obtained from a potato chip bag he had handled. Following a bench trial, he was convicted of attempted armed robbery and aggravated battery. The appellate court found, inter alia, that: (1) the evidence sufficiently supported his convictions, as the State proved beyond a reasonable doubt that he committed the crimes; (2) defendant waived his right to proceed pro se; (3) a proper foundation was laid to admit the potato chip bag into evidence; (4) the offenses for which he was convicted involved multiple separate acts and, thus, did not violate the one-act, one-crime doctrine; and (5) his 25-year sentence for attempted armed robbery violated Ill. Const. art. I, § 11's proportionate penalties clause because it was disproportionate to the sentence for attempted armed violence, which had the same elements, and meant that he had to sentenced for the offense of attempted armed violence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for aggravated battery, but vacated his conviction and sentence for attempted armed robbery. It then remanded the case to the trial court for sentencing based on the offense of attempted armed violence.

People v. Neal


No. 1-09-2814


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 092814; 954 N.E.2d 358; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 697; 352 Ill. Dec. 498



June 29, 2011, Decided 
June 29, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 8, 2011.
Appeal denied by People v. Neal, 2013 Ill. LEXIS 313 (Ill., Mar. 27, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 09 CR 2798. Honorable John P. Kirby, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance. Defendant contended that the police lacked probable cause to arrest him for violating a municipal ordinance prohibiting the solicitation of unlawful business, thereby requiring suppression of the heroin recovered in his postarrest search.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested in a high gang and narcotics area for yelling "blows," in violation of Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 10-8-515, which prohibited the solicitation of unlawful business. He was taken to the police station, where a custodial search revealed seven packets of heroin. Contrary to defendant's argument, the court held that police did not lack probable cause to arrest him for violating the ordinance as the evidence showed that defendant solicited the sale of heroin on a public way in Chicago, thus allowing a conclusion that the officers witnessed defendant violate the ordinance and that they had probable cause to arrest defendant. While defendant argued that the word "blows" had meanings other than heroin, the existence of possible innocent explanations for the individual circumstances did not negate probable cause. The officer's belief that defendant was soliciting the sale of heroin was based on knowledge from 15 years' police service and hundreds of narcotics arrests that "blows" referred to the sale of heroin.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

People v. Kun Lee


No. 2-10-0205


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


954 N.E.2d 338; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 696; 2011 IL App (2d) 100205; 352 Ill. Dec. 478



June 29, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 12, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 09-CF-928. Honorable George Bridges, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Lee, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 5371 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Dec. 19, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted defendant's motion to dismiss an indictment on the ground of prosecutorial vindictiveness after the State charged defendant with residential arson, dismissed that charge after he was convicted of other offenses, and refiled the residential arson charge after the appellate court reversed the judgments of conviction on the other charges and remanded them for a new trial. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated criminal sexual assault and unlawful restraint for attacking his wife. In a separate case, he was also indicted for residential arson for setting fire to her house 13 days after the alleged attack on her. The first case proceeded to trial, and a jury convicted him of aggravated criminal sexual assault and unlawful restraint. After he was sentenced, the State dismissed the residential arson indictment. On appeal, the appellate court reversed defendant's convictions and remanded for a new trial. The State subsequently reindicted him for residential arson. He moved to dismiss the indictment on the ground of prosecutorial vindictiveness. The trial court held that the State did not meet its burden of establishing that it was not being vindictive; therefore, it granted his motion. The appellate court found that the State's decision to reindict him for residential arson after he had successfully appealed in a separate case his convictions of aggravated criminal sexual assault and unlawful restraint did not trigger a presumption of prosecutorial vindictiveness. It then found that he did not prove that the State engaged in actual vindictiveness.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.
