People v. Land


No. 1-10-1048


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 101048; 955 N.E.2d 538; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 659; 353 Ill. Dec. 71



June 24, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 3, 2011.
Appeal denied by People v. Land, 962 N.E.2d 486, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1972, 356 Ill. Dec. 801 (Ill., Nov. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 09 CR 3945. Honorable Thomas P. Fecarotta, Jr., Judge Presiding.
People v. Land, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1403 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 29, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting her of aggravated cruelty to a companion animal in violation of 510 ILCS 70/3.02 (2006).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the trial court's error in failing to instruct the jury that the State had to prove a specific intent by defendant to injure her dog was not plain error because the evidence on that element was not closely balanced, as the jury could have found that defendant specifically intended to cause her dog injury at a point in time after the tow chain broke through the skin and during the four to six weeks it took for the chain to become seriously embedded in the dog's neck. The court could not find that delivering an agreed-to non-pattern jury instruction, when no such instruction was available and the given instruction tracked the statute, challenged the integrity of the judicial process. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in responding to the jury's note regarding whether defendant's failure to remove the chain could qualify as an "act" as the statute required because defendant's claimed distinction between an "act" and an "omission" had no legal basis in Illinois criminal law. The jury's verdict could have been based on defendant's omissions or on her affirmative actions.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. The fees imposed were vacated.

People v. Mimes


No. 1-08-2747


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 082747; 953 N.E.2d 55; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 644; 352 Ill. Dec. 119



June 20, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 3, 2011.
Vacated by, Withdrawn by publisher People v. Mimes, 2014 Ill. LEXIS 18, 378 Ill. Dec. 742, 4 N.E.3d 1114 (Ill., 2014)
Decision reached on appeal by People v. Mimes, 2014 IL App (1st) 082747-B, 2014 Ill. App. LEXIS 467, 382 Ill. Dec. 809, 13 N.E.3d 222 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 CR 28199. Honorable Kenneth J. Wadas, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after it found defendant guilty of attempted first degree murder, aggravated battery with a firearm, and two counts of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon. It then sentenced him and ordered that he be responsible for various fines, fees, and costs. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 19-year-old youth, robbed the victim, who was a 17-year-old youth selling heroin in a public housing building. Later the same day, the victim went into a second building and saw defendant, who shot and gravely wounded the victim. Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of attempted first degree murder, aggravated battery with a firearm, and two counts of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (AUUW). He was sentenced to 45 years in prison on the attempted murder charge and had fees imposed against him. The appellate court found, inter alia, that (1) the trial court did not improperly assume the role of prosecutor by considering the the earlier robbery, as it only did so to assess the victim's ability to identify defendant regarding the current offenses; (2) his sentence for attempted murder was not excessive; (3) his convictions for aggravated battery with a firearm and one AUUW count violated the one-act, one-crime rule; (4) the AUUW statute, 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6 (2004), did not violate the Second Amendment or Ill. Const. art. I, § 22 right to bear arms; and (5) a $ 50 court system fee could be permissibly imposed under 55 ILCS 5/5-1101(c) (2004).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction and sentences, except for convictions and sentences for aggravated battery with a firearm offense and the second aggravated unlawful use of a weapon offense, which had to be vacated. It also affirmed imposition of a $ 50 court system fee, vacated the imposition of the other challenged fees totaling $ 160, and offset the fines totaling $ 15 with accrued presentence credit.

People v. Grant


No. 1-09-1107


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 091107; 951 N.E.2d 1153; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 645; 351 Ill. Dec. 489



June 17, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 25, 2011.
Appeal granted by People v. Grant, 955 N.E.2d 475, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1599, 353 Ill. Dec. 8 (Ill., 2011)
Reversed by People v. Grant, 2013 IL 112734, 2013 Ill. LEXIS 266 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 09 CR 0398. The Honorable Maureen Slattery Boyle, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, which convicted him of Class 4 possession of cocaine. Specifically, defendant challenged the denial of his motion to quash his arrest and suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed at a known narcotics sales spot yelling "dro, dro" at a passing vehicle. He was arrested for violating Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 10-8-515 (1998), which prohibited the solicitation of an unlawful business on a public way. A motion to quash the arrest and suppress evidence in a search incident to arrest was denied, and defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine. This appeal followed. In reversing, the appellate court determined, had a complaint been filed against defendant based upon what was observed and heard at the time of the arrest, such a complaint charging solicitation of unlawful business in the language of Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 10-8-515 (1998) would have been insufficient under 725 ILCS 5/111-3(a) (2008) because the phrase "unlawful business" did not describe specific conduct. Moreover, the term "dro" did not qualify as a common term for cannabis such that a complaint defining the term would have satisfied the requirement that an ordinance violation be charged with reasonable certainty. The facts known in this case amounted to no more than reasonable suspicion under Terry, and probable cause did not exist to arrest defendant.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed, and the sentence was vacated.

Hope Clinic for Women Ltd. v. Adams


No. 1-10-1463, 1-10-1576 (cons.)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 101463; 955 N.E.2d 511; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 649; 353 Ill. Dec. 44



June 17, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 8, 2011.
Appeal granted by Hope Clinic for Women, Ltd. v. Adams, 962 N.E.2d 481, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1870, 356 Ill. Dec. 796 (Ill., 2011)
Appeal granted by Hope Clinic for Women, Ltd. v. Adams, 962 N.E.2d 481, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1872, 356 Ill. Dec. 796 (Ill., 2011)
Motion granted by Hope Clinic for Women, Ltd. v. Adams, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 23 (Ill., Jan. 9, 2012)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Hope Clinic for Women, Ltd. v. Flores, 2013 IL 112673, 991 N.E.2d 745, 2013 Ill. LEXIS 846, 372 Ill. Dec. 255 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 09 CH 38661. Honorable Daniel A. Riley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) dismissed plaintiff medical providers' complaint with prejudice that challenged the constitutionality of the Parental Notice of Abortion Act of 1995, 750 ILCS 70/1 et seq. (2008), under the Illinois constitution alone. It also denied the proposed intervenors' petition to intervene. The medical providers appealed the dismissal; the proposed intervenors appealed the denial of their petition.


OVERVIEW: The medical care providers filed an action to challenge the Parental Notice of Abortion Act of 1995, 750 ILCS 70/1 et seq. (2008), under the Illinois constitution alone. The trial court granted judgment on the pleadings against them. It held that their equal protection and due process claims were barred by collateral estoppel, and that their privacy law claim had to be dismissed because federal privacy law would require dismissal. The appellate court found that their equal protection claim was not barred by collateral estoppel because the federal opinion was not decided on equal protection grounds, and that their due process claim was not barred by collateral estoppel because the federal court was presented with only a very narrow question not at issue in the present case. It also found state and federal constitutional clauses could be considered coextensive when the two clauses were worded the same, but that logic did not apply when the Illinois Constitution had an express clause, such as a right to privacy clause, which the federal constitution did not. Too, it found that the proposed intervenors, whose petition to intervene was denied, had not shown inadequate representation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the complaint with prejudice and affirmed the trial court's order denying the petition to intervene. Too, it remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Farmer


No. 1-08-3185


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


2011 IL App (1st) 083185; 949 N.E.2d 770; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 544; 350 Ill. Dec. 978



June 1, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 12, 2011.
Appeal denied by People v. Farmer, 955 N.E.2d 474, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1630, 353 Ill. Dec. 7 (Ill., Sept. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. No. 02-1213446. HONORABLE ANTHONY A. IOSCO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, convicting him of falsely representing himself to be the parent, legal guardian or other relation of a minor child to a public employee, a police officer, and sentencing him to 364 days in the county department of corrections.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the child's mother testified that her daughter had ran away in March 2002, when she was 12-years old. In June 2002, defendant was observed with the child at a shopping mall. Defendant proclaimed to the police that the child was his cousin. The mother had reported the child missing, and testified she did not know defendant, she had not given him permission to care for her daughter, and he was not related to her or her daughter. Defendant argued that the statute under which he was convicted was unconstitutionally overbroad and criminalized constitutionally protected speech. The appellate court ruled that 720 ILCS 5/32-5.3 (2002) was not unconstitutionally overbroad. A construction of 720 ILCS 5/32-5.3 that required the false statement be given knowingly and with the intent of deceiving the relevant public official or employee advanced the State's interest in protecting minors, while limiting the punishment of speech to cases where a person knowingly deceives a public official or employee to frustrate the operations of government in the protection of minors. Also, defendant failed to show ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

842 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Larimer


No. 1-10-0116


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


409 Ill. App. 3d 827; 949 N.E.2d 303; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 466; 350 Ill. Dec. 815



May 13, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 22, 2011.
Appeal denied by People v. Larimer, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1353 (Ill., Sept. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 08 MC 25611. The Honorable Marguerite Quinn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) summarily dismissing her post-conviction petition. On appeal, defendant contended that her petition stated the gist of an actual innocence claim and an ineffective assistance of counsel claim.


OVERVIEW: Before reaching the merits of defendant's case, the appellate court had to first determine whether defendant, who was convicted of a misdemeanor and received a disposition of supervision, had standing to proceed under the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 ILCS 5/122-1 et seq., before the supervision was complete. The trial court placed defendant on supervision, which did not, as a matter of law, constitute a disposition following a judgment of conviction. As defendant had not yet received a judgment of conviction and sentence when she filed her petition under the Act, defendant's petition was premature. No exception existed to the rule that there had to be a final judgment to challenge under the Act. Also, defendant had another avenue available to raise her claims as Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(b) provided for a direct appeal. Further, the fact that defendant contended that there were serious collateral consequences that resulted from the entry of supervision in a criminal case did not change the fact that her petition was premature. Thus, the circuit court did not err in dismissing her post-conviction petition as premature.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

People v. Tolentino


No. 1-09-1388


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


409 Ill. App. 3d 598; 949 N.E.2d 1167; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 417; 351 Ill. Dec. 72



May 10, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 22, 2011.
Appeal denied by People v. Tolentino, 955 N.E.2d 479, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1720, 353 Ill. Dec. 12 (Ill., 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Tolentino v. Illinois, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 1244 (U.S., Feb. 21, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 06 CR 1204. The Honorable Thomas V. Gainer, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; cause remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after it found defendant guilty of attempted first degree murder of a peace officer, being an armed habitual criminal, and aggravated discharge of a firearm. It then sentenced him. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after a bench trial of attempted first degree murder of a peace officer, being an armed habitual criminal, and aggravated discharge of a firearm. He was then sentenced to, inter alia, 20 years in prison as a sentence enhancement for personally discharging a firearm, as well as for the armed habitual criminal and aggravated discharge of a firearm convictions. On appeal, he alleged the sentence enhancement was improper, his armed habitual criminal conviction was an ex post facto violation, his conviction for aggravated discharge of a firearm violated the one-act, one-crime rule, and his mittimus should be corrected. The appellate court found that: (1) allowing addition of a firearm enhancement to a sentence given pursuant to 720 ILCS 5/8-4(c)(1)(A) (2006) addressed the legislature's desire both to deter intentional peace officer killings and to discourage the use of firearms in the commission of felonies; (2) the armed habitual criminal statute did not violate constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto legislation; (3) his convictions were not improperly based on a single physical act of firearm possession; and (4) his mittimus needed to be corrected.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction and remanded the case to the trial court for correction of the mittimus.

People v. Coleman


No. 1-09-0417


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


409 Ill. App. 3d 869; 948 N.E.2d 795; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 408; 350 Ill. Dec. 515



April 29, 2011, Decided 
April 29, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 8, 2011.
Rehearing denied by People v. Coleman, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 622 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., May 27, 2011)
Appeal denied by People v. Coleman, 955 N.E.2d 473, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1323, 353 Ill. Dec. 6 (Ill., 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Coleman v. Illinois, 132 S. Ct. 1866, 182 L. Ed. 2d 652, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 2548 (U.S., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 06 CR 28145. Honorable John A Wasilewski, Judge Presiding.
People v. Coleman, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 220 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; mittimus corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, that convicted him of violating the armed habitual criminal statute, 720 ILCS 5/24-1.7 (2006), arguing that the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he violated the statute because the name on one of the certified copies of conviction entered as evidence of a prior offense did not match his name.


OVERVIEW: At the trial of defendant, whose first name was Jesse, the State, in order to prove that defendant had a criminal record, introduced a certified copy of a 1997 conviction for unlawful use of a weapon by a felon for an individual with the same surname but with the first name of "Jessie." Defendant did not object but challenged such evidence on appeal and contended that the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the certified copy reflected his prior conviction rather than the conviction of an individual with a similar name. On review, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because the record indicated that defendant's criminal history report named defendant as "Jessie" and listed defendant's use of "Jessie" as an alias at least eight times between 1975 to 2002, as well as four convictions under the name "Jessie." Further, the armed habitual criminal statute was a constitutionally permissible restriction of the right to bear arms under the Second Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. II, as a valid exercise of government's right to protect the health, safety, and general welfare of its citizens.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

In re Merrilee M.


No. 2-10-0103


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


409 Ill. App. 3d 983; 949 N.E.2d 1146; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 402; 351 Ill. Dec. 51



April 28, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 10, 2011.
Appeal denied by People v. Merrilee M. (In re Merrilee M.), 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1778 (Ill., Sept. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 09-MH-172. Honorable Susan Clancy Boles, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Merrilee M. (In re Merrilee), 409 Ill. App. 3d 377, 950 N.E.2d 1162, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 355, 351 Ill. Dec. 334 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Kane County, Illinois, which entered an order of involuntarily admission.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the patient was subject to involuntary admission for 90 days, and this appeal followed. In vacating, the appellate court first noted that the appeal was moot because the time period in the order had expired. However, the collateral consequences exception applied in this case because of the suspension of the patient's nursing licence and the necessity of seeking the reinstatement of that license. The State was put on notice that the patient was challenging her involuntary admission on the basis that she was reasonably expected to engage in dangerous conduct. Moreover, a posttrial motion was not required. Next, the involuntary admission was vacated as void because the trial court relied upon a standard that had been held to be unconstitutionally vague. The definition of dangerous conduct was unconstitutionally vague; because 405 ILCS 5/1-119(1), (3) (2008) required a finding that the patient was reasonably expected to engage in dangerous conduct as defined in the unconstitutional 405 ILCS 5/1-104.5 (2008), the admission could not have been sustained.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated.

People v. Hawkins


1-09-0221


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


409 Ill. App. 3d 564; 948 N.E.2d 676; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 396; 350 Ill. Dec. 396



April 26, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 8, 2011.

As Corrected May 2 , 2011.
Motion granted by People v. Hawkins, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1234 (Ill., Sept. 23, 2011)
Appeal denied by People v. Hawkins, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 2158 (Ill., Nov. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 07 CR 22774. Honorable Stanley Sacks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentencing him to seven years in prison for each of his three convictions of aggravated criminal sexual assault under 720 ILCS 5/12-14(a)(4) (2008), to be served consecutively, for a total of 21 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: The mandatory consecutive sentences for defendant's aggravated criminal sexual assault convictions did not violate the proportionate sentencing provision of Ill. Const. art. I, §11 because the elements for aggravated criminal sexual assault and aggravated kidnapping were not identical as charged in the indictment, the proportionate penalties clause was not implicated. To prove aggravated kidnapping as charged, the State only needed to prove the elements of kidnapping plus the commission of criminal sexual assault and the use of force or threat of force, but not aggravated criminal sexual assault. The seven-year sentences for each count fell within the statutory sentencing range of six to 30 years, and the imposition of the seven-year sentences as a consecutive sentence affected only the manner by which the sentence was carried out and did not constitute an increase in penalty.


OUTCOME: Sentences affirmed.

 

847 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Agolf, LLC v. Vill. of Arlington Heights


No. 1-10-1599


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


409 Ill. App. 3d 211; 946 N.E.2d 1123; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 357; 349 Ill. Dec. 627



April 15, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 17, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Agolf, LLC v. Vill. of Arlingtion Heights, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1353 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Apr. 26, 2011)
Appeal denied by Agolf, LLC v. Vill. of Arlington Heights, 955 N.E.2d 468, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1769, 353 Ill. Dec. 1 (Ill., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 06 CH 18560. The Honorable Nancy J. Arnold, Judge Presiding.
Agolf, LLC v. Village of Arlington Heights, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 212 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an Illinois limited liability company (LLC), brought suit against defendant village. a municipal corporation, seeking declaratory judgment and injunctive relief involving a redevelopment project. It later filed an amended complaint which added constitutional claims. The village moved for summary judgment based on res judicata, and the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted its motion. The LLC appealed.


OVERVIEW: The LLC purchased a shopping center in the village. The village announced that it would be implementing a tax increment financing (TIF) district as part of the redevelopment project. A tenant in the shopping center filed suit, challenging the implementation of the TIF district. This action was unsuccessful. When the LLC later filed its action challenging the TIF district, the trial court found it was barred by res judicata. The LLC contended that the trial court erred in granting summary judgment because res judicata was inapplicable and inequitable in the instant cause. The appeals court disagreed. Each of the elements of res judicata had been met: the tenant brought a suit against the village to final adjudication, that suit clearly involved an identity of the same cause of action as the suit the LLC subsequently filed against the village, and the tenant and the LLC stood in privity with regard to the same set of operative facts. To allow the LLC to pursue its suit would essentially condemn the village to relitigate issues already decided in all potential suits filed by anyone with a property interest in the shopping center. This was what res judicata was meant to prevent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Fields


No. 3-08-0829


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


409 Ill. App. 3d 398; 948 N.E.2d 290; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 354; 350 Ill. Dec. 221



April 14, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 2, 2011.
Appeal granted by People v. Fields, 955 N.E.2d 474, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1740, 353 Ill. Dec. 7 (Ill., 2011)
Reversed by People v. Fields, 2012 IL 112438, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 1003 (2012)
Appeal after remand at, Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Fields, 2013 IL App (3d) 080829, 2013 Ill. App. LEXIS 748 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 14th Judicial Circuit, Henry County, Illinois, No. 07-CF-37. Honorable Larry S. Vandersnick, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Fields, 235 Ill. 2d 595, 924 N.E.2d 458, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 123, 338 Ill. Dec. 252 (2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for the 14th Judicial Circuit, Henry County, Illinois, convicting him of two counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child under 720 ILCS 5/12-14.1(a)(1) (2006), three counts of criminal sexual assault under 720 ILCS 5/12-13(a)(1), (a)(3) (2006), and two counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse under 720 ILCS 5/12-16(b) (2006).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with sex offenses against a child. At trial, the State called another witness to testify concerning defendant's sexual assault against her that led to his conviction of aggravated criminal sexual abuse in another county. Defendant's appointed counsel had represented the witness in a previous juvenile proceeding as guardian ad litem. The Appellate Court of Illinois held that defense counsel was laboring under a per se conflict of interest under the Sixth Amendment, because he had a previous association with an entity assisting the State. Counsel's prior representation of the witness was never disclosed to the trial court or waived on the record by defendant. Defendant's conviction had to be reversed, because counsel's representation might have been restrained by his prior commitments to the witness. For example, any information protected by the attorney-client privilege could have impacted his ability to effectively cross-examine the witness or attack her credibility.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for a new trial with new trial counsel.

People v. Davis


1-09-1973


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


408 Ill. App. 3d 747; 947 N.E.2d 813; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 298; 349 Ill. Dec. 799



March 31, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Davis, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1399 (Ill., Sept. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 09 CR 3042. Honorable Michael J. Howlett, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, convicting him of seven counts of unlawful use of a weapon by a felon (UUWF), 720 ILCS 5/24-1.1(a) (2008), and four counts of violating the armed habitual criminal statute, 720 ILCS 5/24-1.7(a) (2008).


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence showing that he possessed firearms and that he had prior felony convictions. Defendant argued that his convictions must be reversed because both the armed habitual criminal statute and the UUWF statute violated his constitutional right to bear arms. The appellate court ruled that the armed habitual criminal statute and the UUWF statute did not, on their faces, violate the Second Amendment, and the State was permitted to ban felons from possessing firearms. The restrictions fit proportionally with the interests the statutes served. Also, the armed habitual criminal statute did not violate the constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto laws. The armed habitual criminal statute did not punish defendant for his prior convictions, but rather for a new and separate subsequent crime. However, simultaneous possession of four weapons could support only one conviction for violation of the armed habitual criminal statute.


OUTCOME: The mittimus was modified to reflect only one conviction for violation of the armed habitual criminal statute, and in all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

People v. Nash


No. 2-09-0833


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


409 Ill. App. 3d 342; 947 N.E.2d 350; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 311; 349 Ill. Dec. 713



March 31, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 20, 2011.
Appeal denied by People v. Nash, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1341 (Ill., Sept. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 09-CM-2933. Honorable John J. Scully, Judge, Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence located after a police officer stopped defendant's vehicle because she was driving without a seatbelt, the officer learned her driving privileges had been suspended and that she could not produce an insurance card, and the officer located contraband when he conducted an inventory search as the vehicle was being prepared for impoundment. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped defendant's car because she was not wearing a seat belt. The officer then learned that her driving privileges had been suspended and that she could not produce an insurance card. The officer arrested her. A tow truck was called so that the vehicle could be impounded. While the officer waited for the tow truck, he conducted an inventory search. Under the driver's seat, he found evidence that defendant unlawfully possessed a controlled substance. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress the evidence found. The appellate court found that once the officer learned that defendant had a suspended license and did not have an insurance card, the officer had a mandatory obligation under 625 ILCS 5/6-303(e) (2008) to impound the vehicle because it could not be operated until proof of insurance was shown. It then added that the officer was not required to determine whether a teenage passenger with defendant at the time of the arrest could have driven the vehicle away and that the officer's inventory search conducted pursuant to police department policy furthered a "community caretaking" function, making the search reasonable under the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the suppression order and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Christian Assembly Rios De Agua Viva v. City of Burbank


No. 1-10-3822


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


408 Ill. App. 3d 764; 948 N.E.2d 251; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 299; 350 Ill. Dec. 182



March 31, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at, Summary judgment granted, in part, summary judgment denied, in part by Christian Assembly Rios De Agua Viva v. City of Burbank, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 23640 (N.D. Ill., Feb. 21, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Michael Hyman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant church challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied its motion for a preliminary injunction seeking a declaration that it could operate a church on property on which it had a contract to purchase, notwithstanding appellee city's zoning ordinance that failed to allow such use.


OVERVIEW: The church sought an declaration that it could operate a church on certain property. The trial court denied the church's requested relief. The court affirmed on appeal. The church decided to assume the city's ordinance was invalid and proceeded at its own risk to enter into a contract and expend funds to purchase the property for use as church. The church could not reasonably rely on the illegality of the preamendment zoning ordinance when entering into the contract and expending money in an effort to buy the property. The trial court did not err in denying the church's preliminary injunction motion. Because churches, regardless of the makeup of their congregation, as well as all other nonrevenue-producing organizations, were prohibited in a certain commercial district, the amended ordinance did not show discrimination based on race, color or national origin under 740 ILCS 23/5 (2008).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Odom v. White


NO. 5-09-0631, NO. 5-10-0139


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


408 Ill. App. 3d 1113; 948 N.E.2d 1072; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 303; 350 Ill. Dec. 565



March 30, 2011, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. No. 09-MR-2. Honorable Joe Harrison, Judge, presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County. No. 09-MR-27. Honorable Terry H. Gamber, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, appellants, drivers, challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Jefferson County, Illinois, affirming the decisions of appellee Illinois Secretary of State, denying the drivers' petitions to rescind the suspensions of their driving privileges pursuant to 625 ILCS 5/6-206(a)(31) (2008).


OVERVIEW: The drivers were asked to and did submit to blood-alcohol tests. Both tests revealed an alcohol concentration of 0.08 or more. Driving privileges were suspended, and each driver contested the suspension. In each case the Secretary upheld the suspension. Both drivers sought administrative review in the circuit court, and in each case the circuit court affirmed the decision of the Secretary. The appellate court ruled that where the evidence was insufficient to establish that the drivers were involved in motor vehicle accidents which resulted in death or personal injuries within the meaning of the statute, they should not have been subjected to blood-alcohol tests and their driving privileges should not have been suspended. The Secretary expanded the implied-consent statute to include accidents which could be of a less serious nature, where the injuries were not so severe that they required that a person be carried from the scene by ambulance, but where a person was carried from the scene by ambulance regardless of the severity of the injuries. That expansion of the statute was contrary to the caselaw and contrary to the plain language of the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Lawlor v. N. Am. Corp.


No. 1-09-3603


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT


409 Ill. App. 3d 149; 949 N.E.2d 155; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 267; 350 Ill. Dec. 667



March 24, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 17, 2011.
Appeal granted by Lawlor v. N. Am. Corp., 955 N.E.2d 471, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1774, 353 Ill. Dec. 4 (Ill., 2011)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Lawlor v. N. Am. Corp., 2012 Ill. LEXIS 1505, 2012 IL 112530 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 CH 13876. The Honorable Carol Pearce McCarthy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment on a jury's verdict finding defendant former employer liable to plaintiff former employee for compensatory and punitive damages after she sued it for intrusion. On its breach of fiduciary duty counterclaim, the trial court awarded in a bench trial compensatory and punitive damages to it. The trial court also reduced her punitive damage award. She appealed and cross appealed. It appealed.


OVERVIEW: The former employee determined after she left her sales position with the former employer that it was investigating her. She ultimately learned that it was using nefarious means, known as "pretexting," to obtain her private phone records. While the investigation was conducted by the former employer's agents, the former employer used the information given to it. She sued it for intrusion upon seclusion. It counterclaimed for breach of fiduciary duty. A jury awarded her compensatory and punitive damages. The trial court in a bench trial awarded it compensatory and punitive damages despite no evidence showing that any customer left it to work with her at her new employer. Pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-1207 (2004), the trial court reduced the jury's punitive damage award to her. The appellate court found that the former employer was liable for the conduct of its agents, as it did not limit the investigation and used the information it was given. It also reinstated the full punitive damage award to her, especially given the large amount of attorney fees she incurred. Too, it found the damages awarded to the former employer were against the manifest weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment regarding the verdicts favoring the former employee and reinstated the jury's original punitive damage award. It also reversed the trial court's judgment against her on the former employer's breach of fiduciary duty counterclaim, and vacated the compensatory and punitive damages awarded to it on that claim. Too, it affirmed the trial court's directed verdict on her procuring cause claim.

Nelson v. Chi. Park Dist.


Nos. 1-09-0238, 1-10-0505


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


408 Ill. App. 3d 53; 945 N.E.2d 634; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 225; 348 Ill. Dec. 865



March 15, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 28, 2011.
Appeal denied by Nelson v. Chi. Park Dist., 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1420 (Ill., Sept. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 08 CH 35079. The Honorable Nancy J. Arnold, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed with prejudice plaintiff taxpayers' lawsuit against defendants, a public entity, a private school, and affiliates, alleging that a termination agreement executed between the public entity and private school over use of public property was void or voidable. It then imposed an Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 137 monetary sanction against the taxpayers' attorneys. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: A community organization and three individual city taxpayers sued the private school, the public entity, and affiliates over the public entity and private school's agreement granting the private school permission to build a soccer field on public property in return for priority use of it. After the public entity and private school executed a termination agreement, the trial court dismissed the case with prejudice. The taxpayers then sued the public entity, private school, and affiliates claiming the termination agreement was void or voidable. R. 137 sanctions against the taxpayers' attorneys for filing a frivolous lawsuit. The appellate court found that (1) res judicata barred the subsequent lawsuit since the taxpayers were in privity with the earlier lawsuit plaintiffs, there was an identity of the two actions, and the earlier lawsuit terminated on its merits; (2) the Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 137 sanctions awarded were proper; and (3) the Citizen Participation Act did not bar entry of the sanction award.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Ross


No. 1-09-1463


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


407 Ill. App. 3d 931; 947 N.E.2d 776; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 195; 349 Ill. Dec. 762



March 11, 2011, Decided 
March 11, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 20, 2011.
Appeal denied by People v. Ross, 949 N.E.2d 1102, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 989, 351 Ill. Dec. 7 (Ill., 2011)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Ross, 2014 IL App (1st) 120089, 2014 Ill. App. LEXIS 179 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 09 CR 3228. Honorable Vincent M. Gaughan, Judge Presiding.


DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, that convicted him of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon and of being an armed habitual criminal under 720 ILCS 5/24-1.7 (2008), arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support the latter conviction and that the armed criminal statute violated his constitutional right to bear arms.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court rejected defendant's contention that the State failed to prove him guilty of being an armed habitual criminal because the State failed to prove that he owned the vehicle in which the handgun was found or had knowledge of the gun's presence in his girlfriend's vehicle. Defendant's knowledge was presumed because defendant had control and possession of the vehicle, defendant abandoned the vehicle as police officers approached, and the gun was in plain view in the back seat. Knowledge could be established by evidence of defendant's conduct from which it could be inferred that he knew of the gun's presence. Further, the armed habitual criminal statute did not violate defendant's Second Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. II, right to bear arms. While the Second Amendment vested individuals with the right to bear arms to protect oneself in one's home, it did not give people the right to bear arms in public. The right to bear arms was subject to some restrictions, and the legislature was vested with the authority to disqualify certain classifications of people, such as convicted felons, from the exercise of Second Amendment rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Figiel v. Chi. Plan Comm'n


No. 1-09-2584


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, County Department, Chancery Division. No. 2008 CH 32919. The Honorable Sophia Hall, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court, County Department, Chancery Division (Illinois), entered a judgment that granted defendant amendment proponents' 735 ILCS 5/2-619 (2008) motion to dismiss plaintiff nearby private property owners' legal challenge to the city council's approval of an amendment to a city-planned development. The nearby private property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff nearby private property owners sued defendant amendment proponents to challenge the city council's decision to approve an amendment to one of the city's planned developments pursuant to the Chicago Zoning Ordinance, which allowed for the construction of a children's museum and a new park district field house facility in a city park. The trial court granted the amendment proponents' motion to dismiss pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-619 (2008) asserting that the relevant complaint was defective because the nearby property owners failed to comply with Illinois Municipal Code notice requirements set forth in 65 ILCS 5/11-13-8 (2008). The appellate court rejected the nearby private property owners' claim that compliance with 65 ILCS 5/11-13-8 (2008), which they conceded had not occurred, was not necessary since their amended complaint was not a declaratory judgment action but rather an independent action brought pursuant to 65 ILCS 5/11-13-25 (2008) of the Illinois Municipal Code. It found that recent authority had held that 65 ILCS 5/11-13-25 (2008) did not afford private property owners an independent cause of action to challenge any type of zoning ordinance amendments.

People v. Haywood


No. 2-09-1325


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


407 Ill. App. 3d 540; 944 N.E.2d 846; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 148; 348 Ill. Dec. 605



February 24, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by People v. Haywood, 949 N.E.2d 1101, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 992 (Ill., May 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Stephenson County. No. 08-CF-313. Honorable Michael P. Bald, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Stephenson County (Illinois) granting defendant's motion to quash the arrest and suppress evidence heroin seized following a traffic stop.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by granting defendant's motion to suppress because: (1) defendant's conduct of activating his right turn signal and driving past three opportunities to turn was not a traffic violation under 625 ILCS 5/11-804(d) and therefore the officer's stop of defendant's vehicle was not objectively justified by reasonable suspicion; and (2) the officer's mistaken belief that defendant's conduct amounted to a traffic violation did not justify the stop at its inception. The court rejected the State's contention that defendant's conduct violated 625 ILCS 5/12-208(b), 12-212 because those statutes governed a vehicle's equipment, not the driver's conduct. The State forfeited its claim that the officer had a reasonable articulable suspicion of a violation of 625 ILCS 5/12-101(a) because it raised it for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

People v. Aguilar


No. 1-09-0840


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


408 Ill. App. 3d 136; 944 N.E.2d 816; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 103; 348 Ill. Dec. 575



February 23, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 7, 2011.
Appeal granted by People v. Aguilar, 949 N.E.2d 1099, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 947, 351 Ill. Dec. 4 (Ill., 2011)
Motion granted by People v. Aguilar, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1151 (Ill., Sept. 22, 2011)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by People v. Aguilar, 2013 IL 112116, 2013 Ill. LEXIS 853 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Charles P. Burns, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (AUUW), under 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6(a)(1), (a)(3)(A) (2008), and unlawful possession of a firearm, under 720 ILCS 5/24-3.1(a)(1) (2008). He was sentenced to 24 months of probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the amended AUUW statute applied retroactively to the facts of his case because the amendment merely clarified the original intent of the statute under which he was convicted. The appellate court held that the amended AUUW statute did not apply because the incident involving defendant occurred more than a year before the effective date of the statutory amendments. Even if the statutory amendments applied, defendant's conviction would still stand because defendant did not have the requisite permission to possess the gun. The owner of the home and yard where defendant was arrested, denied that defendant had a gun. Defendant also denied having a gun. Thus, it could have been inferred that the owner did not give defendant the requisite "permission" to possess a gun on his land. Further, 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6 (2008) did not violate defendant's second amendment rights because it was substantially related to the important governmental objective of keeping police officers and the general public safe and the fit between the AUUW statute and the government objective was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

People v. Newton


No. 2-09-0449


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


407 Ill. App. 3d 517; 944 N.E.2d 471; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 147; 348 Ill. Dec. 518



February 23, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Newton, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 323 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Apr. 4, 2011)
Appeal denied by People v. Newton, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1499 (Ill., Sept. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County. No. 06-CF-458. Honorable Grant S. Wegner, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kendall County, Illinois, convicting him of one count of driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI) under 625 ILCS 5/11-501 (2006), a Class 1 felony, and sentencing him to 7 1/2 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: The offense was a Class 1 felony because defendant had four prior convictions of DUI. Defendant argued that his offense must be reduced from a Class 1 felony to a Class 4 felony, and the cause remanded for resentencing, because 2005 Ill. Laws 94-116 (eff. Jan. 1, 2006), which created 625 ILCS 5/11-501(c-1)(4) and made his offense a Class 1 felony, was unconstitutional. The appellate court ruled that defendant was properly convicted of Class 1 felony DUI. By passing 2005 Ill. Laws 94-116, the Illinois Legislature set up a coherent and consistent scheme under which any fifth DUI would be a Class 1 felony, while any fourth DUI would be, at most, a Class 2 felony. Under 5 ILCS 70/6 (2006), the conflict between 2005 Ill. Laws 94-609 (eff. Jan. 1, 2006) and 2005 Ill. Laws 94-116 was not irreconcilable and the Illinois Legislature had not intended that the latter repeal the former. 2005 Ill. Laws 94-609 made only a limited change to 625 ILCS 5/11-501, which had nothing to do with 2005 Ill. Laws 94-116.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

860 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Curtis


No. 2-09-0404


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


407 Ill. App. 3d 1042; 944 N.E.2d 806; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 142; 348 Ill. Dec. 565



February 23, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Curtis, 949 N.E.2d 1100, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1076 (Ill., May 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 08-CM-7016. Honorable Clarke C. Barnes, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) of one count of violating the duties of an animal owner pursuant to the Humane Care for Animals Act, 510 ILCS 70/3(d) (2008), by knowingly and unlawfully failing to provide humane care and treatment to her pet cat. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain her conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial evidence showed that 87 cats were removed from defendant's two-bedroom residence. Many of the cats had upper respiratory tract infections. Testimony at trial reflected that one cat was "severely infected" with an upper respiratory tract infection and had to be euthanized. A witness testified that no more than five cats should be kept in one residence to ensure a healthy environment for the animals. He testified that upper respiratory tract infections can continue circulating, being repeatedly passed from cat to cat, so that, in an overcrowded environment, none of the cats can ever recover. Defendant failed to protect her cat from a disease that would have been both preventable and treatable had she not allowed an excess of 80 stray cats into her residence. Furthermore, defendant's conduct of calling the animal control office and authorizing the animal control facility to remove and take custody of all 87 cats indicated that she was aware that she was unable to provide any of the cats with adequate humane care and treatment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Wilson v. Cook County


No. 1-08-1202


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


407 Ill. App. 3d 759; 943 N.E.2d 768; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 77; 348 Ill. Dec. 160



February 9, 2011, Decided 
February 9, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 14, 2011.
Review granted by Wilson v. Cook County, 949 N.E.2d 1104, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 984, 351 Ill. Dec. 9 (Ill., 2011)
Affirmed by, in part, Reversed by, in part Wilson v. County of Cook, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 337, 2012 IL 112026 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 07 CH 4848. Honorable Mary K. Rochford, Judge Presiding.
Wilson v. Cook County, 237 Ill. 2d 593, 935 N.E.2d 516, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1420, 343 Ill. Dec. 508 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action against defendants, a county, its commissioners, and its sheriff, plaintiff gun owners sought review of a dismissal pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-615 by the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, of their request for a declaration that Cook County, Ill., Ordinance No. 06-O-50 (2006) was unconstitutional. A prior affirmance was vacated, and the court reconsidered in light of McDonald v. City of Chicago.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance, which amended Cook County, Ill., Code of Ordinances § 54-211, banned certain assault weapons and assault ammunition. The owners claimed, inter alia, that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad and that it violated U.S. Const. amend. II. Upon reconsideration, the court affirmed. While the United States Supreme Court precedent of Heller had recognized that a prohibition on handgun possession in the home violated the Second Amendment, no such protection was afforded to those weapons not typically possessed by law-abiding citizens for lawful purposes. Using an intermediate scrutiny standard of review, the ordinance was found to be constitutional as it was sufficiently tailored in its restrictions to rapid-firing or high-capacity weapons. The ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague as it gave definitions and examples as objective criteria for its enforcement. The overbreadth doctrine did not apply as U.S. Const. amend. I rights were not implicated. An equal protection argument failed as assault weapons owners did not constitute a suspect classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

Innovative Modular Solutions v. Hazel Crest Sch. Dist. 152.5


Nos. 1-10-0212, 1-10-0554 & 1-10-0642 (Consolidated)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


407 Ill. App. 3d 143; 943 N.E.2d 283; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 76; 347 Ill. Dec. 993



February 9, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 14, 2011.
Appeal granted by Innovative Modular Solutions v. Hazel Crest Sch. Dist. 152.5, 949 N.E.2d 1098, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1016, 351 Ill. Dec. 3 (Ill., 2011)
Reversed by, Remanded by Innovative Modular Solutions v. Hazel Crest Sch. Dist. 152.5, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 307 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 06 CH 05767. Honorable Barbara A. McDonald, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 1-10-0212, Affirmed. No. 1-10-0554, Appeal dismissed. No. 1-10-0642, Judgment vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessor sued defendants, school district and finance authority. The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, granted summary judgment in favor of the district, and separately granted the claimant a judgment declaring that the authority lacked the power to cancel contracts except in accord with contract cancellation provisions. The authority and claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district leased portable classrooms from the lessor, and agreed to pay a cancellation fee if it cancelled the leases before the termination of the lease terms. The finance authority later cancelled the district's leases. The finance authority did not direct the district to pay the cancellation fees established in the leases, and the district did not pay the fees. The trial court found that the finance authority ordered the district not to pay the cancellation fees and that the order made performance by the district legally impossible. The trial court declared that the finance authority lacked the power to cancel contracts except in accord with contract cancellation provisions. The appellate court ruled that the trial court did not err when it found, due to a legal impossibility created when the State invoked the School Finance Law, 105 ILCS 5/1F-1 et seq. (2004), that the district lacked statutory authority to pay the lessor its cancellation fees. The State invoked the School Finance Law, which provided the finance authority exclusive control over the district's finances, the district was divested of control over its finances and had no statutory authority to pay its debts.


OUTCOME: The declaratory judgment in favor of the lessor was declared moot, and the summary judgment entered in favor of the district was affirmed.

People v. Lesure


No. 1-08-2333


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


408 Ill. App. 3d 12; 944 N.E.2d 780; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 75; 348 Ill. Dec. 539



February 8, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 7, 2011.
Rehearing denied by People v. Lesure, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 348 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Mar. 11, 2011)
Appeal denied by People v. Lesure, 949 N.E.2d 1101, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1063, 351 Ill. Dec. 6 (Ill., 2011)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by United States ex rel. LeSure v. Rednoir, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 108145 (N.D. Ill., Sept. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 CR 4529. Honorable Joseph M. Claps, Judge Presiding.
People v. Lesure, 311 Ill. App. 3d 1068, 766 N.E.2d 688, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 1721, 262 Ill. Dec. 768 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, which dismissed his post-conviction petition following a third-stage evidentiary hearing on the issue of his actual innocence.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was 15-years-old when he was involved in a shooting where one person was killed and another person was injured. He was convicted of first degree murder and attempted first degree murder. A petition for post-conviction relief was dismissed, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court held that a sentence that was void could have been attacked at any time. The appellate court rejected the inmate's assertion that the trial court was required to sentence him under the Illinois Juvenile Court Act, 705 ILCS 405/1-1 et seq (1996). Former 705 ILCS 405/5-4(6)(a) (1996) covered the five enumerated charges therein and all other charges arising out of the same incident. The inmate's conviction for attempted murder arose out of the same incident as his conviction for first degree murder. Pursuant to former 705 ILCS 405/5-4(6)(c)(i) (1996), the trial court properly sentenced the inmate under the Illinois Unified Code of Corrections, 730 ILCS 5/5-1-1 et seq (1996). Because the attempted murder charge was an offense covered by former 705 ILCS 405/5-4(6)(a) (1996), the State did not need to request a hearing to have the inmate sentenced in criminal court.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Byrd v. Hamer


No. 2-08-1011


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


408 Ill. App. 3d 467; 943 N.E.2d 115; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 59; 347 Ill. Dec. 825



January 28, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 18, 2011.
Appeal denied by Byrd v. Hamer, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 998 (Ill., May 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 07-MR-40. The Honorable Maureen P. McIntyre, Judge, Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Illinois Department of Revenue decided that appellant taxpayers' gambling winnings for 1999, 2000, 2001, and 2002 were taxable income and that their gambling losses for those years were not deductible. The Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) affirmed the Department's decision. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the Department did not clearly err by concluding that the taxpayers' gambling activity did not constitute a trade or business, and therefore the activity constituted causal gambling and the taxpayers were not entitled to a state tax deduction for their losses, because the evidence showed that the taxpayers did not devote themselves full time to gambling but rather that one taxpayer continued to work full time in the graphic arts industry where he drew a comfortable salary that supported their gambling. The court rejected the taxpayers' due process challenges to the Illinois Income Tax Act because the tax on gambling winnings did not constitute double taxation, as gambling winnings that represented the return of capital were not taxable under federal law, which Illinois followed, and thus were excluded from gross income before adjusted gross income was determined. In addition, gambling winnings had long been considered income under federal tax law and Illinois law acceded to that characterization by not permitting exclusion of gambling winnings from adjusted gross income as carried over from the federal return.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Newell v. Newell


No. 3-10-0003


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


406 Ill. App. 3d 1046; 942 N.E.2d 776; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 44; 347 Ill. Dec. 573


July 9, 2010, Assigned; August 31, 2010, Submitted 
January 27, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 7, 2011.

As Corrected February 10, 2011.
Appeal denied by Newell v. Newell, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 882 (Ill., May 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, will County, Illinois, No. 07-CH-1125. Honorable Michael J. Powers, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant son challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee bank in a breach of contract action.


OVERVIEW: The son received a settlement when he was a minor, and the proceeds were deposited in an account with instructions that they were not to be withdrawn without a court order. However, his mother removed funds from the account. The son later filed an action against his mother and the bank. Summary judgment was granted to the bank on the basis of a three-year limitations period, and this appeal followed. In reversing, the appellate court held that the three-year limitation period in 810 ILCS 5/4-111 (2006) applied in this case, despite the son's claim of a common law breach of contract. 810 ILCS 5/4-401(a) (2006) applied to situations where a withdrawal was alleged to be in breach of a signatory card and included instructions that formed the bank/customer agreement. However, the son's cause of action was not necessarily time barred. The discovery rule had been utilized by Illinois courts for Uniform Commercial Code and breach of contract cases, and fraudulent concealment by the mother could have tolled the statute of limitations as well. The trial court had to determine on remand when the son knew, or had reason to know, that a cause of action might have existed.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Empress Casino Joliet Corp. v. Giannoulias


No. 3-09-1056


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


406 Ill. App. 3d 1040; 942 N.E.2d 783; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 43; 347 Ill. Dec. 580


October 18, 2010, Assigned; January 19, 2011, Submitted 
January 27, 2011, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 7, 2011.
Appeal denied by Empress Casino Joliet Corp. v. Giannoulias, 949 N.E.2d 1097, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 943, 351 Ill. Dec. 2 (Ill., 2011)
Related proceeding at Arlington Park Racecourse LLC v. Ill. Racing Bd., 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 950, 2012 IL App (1st) 103743U (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. NO. 09-CH-112. Honorable Barbara Petrungaro, Judge, Presiding.
Empress Casino Joliet Corp. v. Giannoulias, 231 Ill. 2d 62, 896 N.E.2d 277, 2008 Ill. LEXIS 378, 324 Ill. Dec. 491 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, four riverboat casinos, appealed after the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois, granted motions to dismiss filed by defendants, the Illinois State Treasurer and the Illinois Racing Board, and intervenor defendant race tracks. The casinos had challenged the constitutionality of 2007 Ill. Laws 1008 (Act) (amending 230 ILCS 10/7 (2006))


OVERVIEW: The Act required the casinos to pay 3% of their adjusted gross receipts (AGR) into a fund to be distributed to the state's horse racing tracks. Casinos with 2004 AGR under $200 million were exempt from the tax. The casinos each had 2004 AGR in excess of $200 million. They challenged the Act based on the uniformity-clause, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2, arguing in part that the 2007 AGR should have been used. The tracks argued that the challenge was barred by collateral estoppel as the tax classification had been upheld in litigation regarding an almost identical 2006 statute. The appellate court did not address the collateral estoppel issue as it ruled that the tax classification was not unconstitutional. The four casinos were the highest grossing casinos in the state and had AGR over $200 million in both 2004 and 2007. No other casinos had that size AGR in those years. The four casinos were the only ones in the state that would be subject to the tax, regardless of which AGR year was used. The legislature's determination that the four casinos were in the best position to absorb the tax for three years following the enactment of the Act was not arbitrary or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

867 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Wirtz v. Quinn


Nos. 1-09-3163, 1-10-0344


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


407 Ill. App. 3d 776; 942 N.E.2d 765; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 33; 347 Ill. Dec. 562



January 26, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 9, 2011.
Reversed by Wirtz v. Quinn, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1107 (Ill., July 11, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Lawrence O'Gara, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, parties filing on behalf and for the benefit of taxpayers, challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, which denied them leave to file a complaint against defendant state officials under 735 ILCS 5/11-303 (2008) and denied a motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: It was alleged that 2009 Ill. Laws 34, 2009 Ill. Laws 35, 2009 Ill. Laws 37, and 2009 Ill. Laws 38 were unconstitutional. Plaintiffs were not able to file a complaint under 735 ILCS 5/11-303 (2008), and they sought review. In reversing, the appellate court determined that the single subject rule under Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) regulated the process by which legislation was enacted. It was designed to prevent the passage of legislation that, if standing alone, could not have mustered the necessary votes for enactment. The wide range of topics in 2009 Ill. Laws 34 could not have been considered to possess a natural and logical connection to the single subject of revenue to the state. 2009 Ill. Laws 34 did not involve the single subject of implementation of the state budget. When an act violated the single subject rule, it had to be struck in its entirety. Pursuant to their own terms, 2009 Ill. Laws 35, 2009 Ill. Laws 37, and 2009 Ill. Laws 38 were all contingent upon the enactment of 2009 Ill. Laws 34. Therefore, because 2009 Ill. Laws 34 was void, the remaining acts were not able to stand either.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed.

People v. Berardi


No. 3-10-0122


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


407 Ill. App. 3d 575; 948 N.E.2d 98; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 26; 350 Ill. Dec. 29

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the Ninth Judicial Circuit Fulton County, Illinois, No. 09-CM-227. The Honorable Edward R. Danner, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of the Ninth Judicial Circuit Fulton County, Illinois, convicting him of resisting a peace officer in violation of 720 ILCS 5/31-1 (2006).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was an alderman for the city. The city had published notice that the city's budget was available for viewing during normal business hours. Defendant was later informed by the budget director that he could not obtain a copy of the budget at that time. The same day defendant went to city hall, accompanied by his wife and friend. Defendant's wife prepared a video recording of the events that transpired when defendant went to city hall concerning the budget. The budget director informed defendant that the mayor had directed him not to distribute copies of the budget until the following Monday. Defendant was ultimately charged with refusing the police chief's request that defendant exit the city private offices. The appellate court ruled that defendant's acts did not constitute resistance under 720 ILCS 5/31-1. Defendant merely disputed the chief's authority to ask defendant to leave the private city office space based on defendant's reasonable belief that he had a right to be present. Defendant's act of verbally disputing the chief's authority for a brief time did not constitute resisting a peace officer.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed.

People v. White


No. 1-08-3090


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


407 Ill. App. 3d 224; 941 N.E.2d 1000; 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 3; 347 Ill. Dec. 131



January 7, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 22, 2011.
Rehearing denied by People v. White, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 157 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 8, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 07 CR 14329. Honorable Mary Margaret Brosnahan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erroneously admitted his two prior misdemeanor theft convictions. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant claimed his two convictions were of minimal probative value and were highly prejudicial. The court of appeals disagreed. The record clearly revealed that the trial court was aware of its discretion and exercised it stating that: "I understand the arguments of both of the parties and I think that there is always a careful balancing test to be performed when admitting proof of other crimes. In this case, the defendant is charged with burglary and the element is did he intend to commit a theft, so it is somewhat prejudicial that the defendant's five prior felony convictions are all thefts. On the other hand, that has to be balanced against the defendant's testimony and his credibility." Rather than "verbal homage" to the balancing test, the trial court's ruling demonstrated reasoned application. While defendant's convictions were not recent, it could not be said that the trial court applied the balancing test improperly. That others might have reached a different result did not render the trial court's decision erroneous.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Gillespie


Nos. 1-08-3016, 1-10-0702


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION

December 29, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 16, 2011.
Appeal denied by People v. Gillespie, 949 N.E.2d 661, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 579, 350 Ill. Dec. 869 (Ill., 2011)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorables Nicholas R. Ford, Stanley Sacks, Judges Presiding.
People v. Gillespie, 344 Ill. App. 3d 1212, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 7050 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of first degree murder. After several direct appeals and motions for postconviction relief, defendant appealed the trial court's order denying defendant leave to file his fourth postconviction petition and dismissing his petition under 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2008).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying postconviction relief because new evidence showed that four officers involved in defendant's interrogation were implicated in allegations of torture, coercion, and misconduct. The court of appeals disagreed. Only two examples cited by defendant to show a pattern and practice of abuse could have been known to the State at the time of defendant's trial. One was a 1991 incident involving a detective, in which he was reprimanded for failing to have a youth officer in the interrogation room, as required when questioning a juvenile suspect. Even if the State were aware of the reprimand, it was unclear why the State had a duty to disclose that information under Brady. Defendant did not allege that the detective was involved in defendant's interrogation and defendant's successive postconviction petitions did not name him in his allegations of police brutality. Further, the detective's reprimand did not involve similar methods of abuse as alleged by defendant. Therefore, that evidence could not be deemed material to defendant's allegations that police brutality compelled his confession.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Protein Partners, LLP v. Lincoln Provision, Inc.


No. 1-09-0823


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


407 Ill. App. 3d 709; 941 N.E.2d 308; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1382; 346 Ill. Dec. 750



December 21, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 15, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Protein Partners v. Lincoln Provision, Inc., 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1459 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 21, 2010)
Appeal denied by Protein Partners, LLP v. Lincoln Provision, Inc., 2011 Ill. LEXIS 648 (Ill., Mar. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 08 M1 602017. Honorable Patrick J. Sherlock, Judge Presiding.
Protein Partners, LLP v. Lincoln Provision, Inc., 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1105 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Oct. 19, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee food broker sued appellant corporation to recover commissions owed to the broker for services it rendered in Ohio. The corporation did not file an appearance, and a default judgment was entered against it in Ohio. The broker registered the Ohio judgment in the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. Thirty-seven days later, the corporation moved to quash the broker's registration of the Ohio judgment. The trial court denied the motion.


OVERVIEW: A motion to vacate a void judgment for lack of service that was filed more than 30 days after the judgment was entered was properly designated a 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2008) petition. An attack on a judgment on the basis of voidness may be construed as a 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2008) petition, and satisfaction of the time constraints or the requirement of a meritorious defense or due diligence was not necessary. Accordingly, the corporation's motion to quash registration of the Ohio judgment was in effect a petition under 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2008). The denial of the corporation's motion was therefore a final and appealable order under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 304(b)(3), vesting the court with jurisdiction. Review of a judgment on a 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2008) petition that was requesting relief based on the allegation that the judgment was void, shall be de novo. The technical defects in both the broker and the corporation's names during the course of the litigation were not fatal to the registration and entry of the Ohio judgment, nor could it be said that the real parties in interest were not at the table. The corporation's argument that the broker committed fraud therefore failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which recognized the Ohio judgment upon registration of that judgment in the trial court by the broker, was affirmed.
