People v. Hackett


No. 3-09-0396


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


406 Ill. App. 3d 209; 943 N.E.2d 13; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1388; 347 Ill. Dec. 723



December 21, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 26, 2011.
Appeal granted by People v. Hackett, 949 N.E.2d 661, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 626, 350 Ill. Dec. 869 (Ill., 2011)
Reversed by, Remanded by People v. Hackett, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 990, 2012 IL 111781 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the Twelfth Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois, No. 08-CF-2005. The Honorable Carla Alessio Policandriotes, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with aggravated driving under the influence and aggravated driving while license revoked. The Circuit Court of Will County, Illinois, granted defendant's motion to quash arrest and to suppress evidence on the grounds that the police lacked probable cause to stop defendant's vehicle. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The street was a four-lane roadway with two lanes of northbound traffic and two lanes of southbound traffic. While traveling in the left-hand northbound lane, the officer twice observed defendant's vehicle's cross the lane divider between the two northbound lanes of traffic. The officer testified that both times defendant's vehicle barely went over the lane divider and that both times, defendant's tires crossed the line for a matter of seconds. The appellate court ruled that the trial court properly granted defendant's motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence. The officer provided no testimony from which to find that all parts of defendant's vehicle were not at all times physically within a single lane of traffic. The officer provided no testimony from which to find that an officer in his position could reasonably believe that defendant was actually driving in two lanes and was therefore engaged in improper lane usage in violation of 625 ILCS 5/11-709(a) (2006). The facts and circumstances surrounding the traffic stop did not provide a reasonable, articulable suspicion to stop defendant based on the officer's stated reason of a violation of 625 ILCS 5/11-709(a).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Atherton


No. 2-08-1169


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


406 Ill. App. 3d 598; 940 N.E.2d 775; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1365; 346 Ill. Dec. 406



December 16, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 28, 2011
Ordered published by People v. Atherton, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1415 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Dec. 16, 2010)
Appeal denied by People v. Atherton, 239 Ill. 2d 558, 943 N.E.2d 1102, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 220, 348 Ill. Dec. 192 (2011)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Atherton, 2013 IL App (2d) 121017-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1564 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County. No. 05-CF-289. Honorable, J. Todd Kennedy, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Boone County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant of two counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child in violation of 720 ILCS 5/3-6(j) (2002) and 720 ILCS 5/12-14.1(a)(1) (2002). It then sentenced him to a total of 24 years in prison and ordered him to pay a Crime Stoppers fine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on two counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. On appeal, he claimed, inter alia, that: (1) he was not convicted beyond a reasonable doubt on one count; (2) the trial court failed to comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 431(b) regarding voir dire questioning; (3) 725 ILCS 5/115-10 (2002) was violated regarding admission of the statements of the alleged child sex abuse victim; (4) it erred in admitting child-sexual-abuse-accommodation syndrome evidence; and (5) a Crime Stoppers fine was impermissible. The appellate court found the victim's testimony that defendant's penis went inside her anus and, thus, supported the relevant conviction, the trial court complied with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 431(b), because the victim testified and was subject to cross-examination, none of the statements admitted pursuant to 725 ILCS 5/115-10 (2002) were improper under Crawford, based on prior judicial decisions, the trial court was not required to conduct a Frye hearing regarding the syndrome that a child welfare supervisor was sufficiently qualified to testify about generally, and the Crime Stoppers fine did not apply to defendants receiving a prison sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated defendant's Crime Stoppers fine. Otherwise, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Williams


No. 1-09-1667


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


405 Ill. App. 3d 958; 940 N.E.2d 95; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1284; 346 Ill. Dec. 95



December 2, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 21, 2011.
Vacated by People v. Williams, 953 N.E.2d 933, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1324, 352 Ill. Dec. 252 (Ill., 2011)
Adhered to, in part, Remanded by People v. Williams, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1264 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 08 CR 16364. Honorable Kenneth J. Wadas, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of two counts of unlawful use of a weapon by a felon under 720 ILCS 5/24-1.1(a) (2008) and six counts of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon (AUUW) under 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6 (2008), sentencing him to five years in prison, and assessing costs totaling $ 715.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court rejected defendant's contention that the recent cases of Heller and McDonald should be extended to invalidate 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6 (2008) and held that the statute did not violate the Second Amendment because there was a rational basis to the statute's ban on carrying and possessing loaded firearms outside of the home, namely the protection of police officers and the general public. Nor did Heller or McDonald render 720 ILCS 5/24-1.1(a) (2008) unconstitutional because defendant was found to be in possession of a handgun and ammunition while standing on a public street. However, the court held that the trial court erred by assessing defendant a $ 10 mental health fee, a $ 5 youth diversion fee, a $ 30 Children's Advocacy Center fee, and a $ 5 drug court fee because none of those fees were designed to reimburse the State for money it expended in prosecuting defendant, and therefore they were all fines for which presentence incarceration credit of $ 5 per day was authorized. The charges totaled $ 50 and defendant was entitled to that amount in credit from his presentence incarceration credit.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed. The costs were modified.

Gruwell v. Ill. Dep't of Fin. & Prof'l Regulation


NO. 4-09-0495


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


406 Ill. App. 3d 283; 943 N.E.2d 658; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1270; 348 Ill. Dec. 50



November 30, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Gruwell v. Ill. Dep't of Fin. & Prof'l Regulation, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 554 (Ill., Mar. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 05MR545. Honorable Leo J. Zappa, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant salesperson sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which upheld an administrative order imposing a civil fine upon her for engaging in the unlicensed practice of real estate.


OVERVIEW: The salesperson, acting as an independent contractor, sold advertisements on a Web site for homes that were for sale by owner. She was paid for each advertisement she sold. The company that owned the Web site entered into a consent order admitting that its activities amounted to unlicensed practice of real estate in violation of 225 ILCS 454/20-10 (2002) and agreeing to become a licensed corporate broker and to pay a fine. The court held that the salesperson engaged in licensed activities under 225 ILCS 454/1-10 (2002) because she used language resembling that of licensed brokers and actively referred clients to the Web site for advice on marketing and selling their homes. She acted for another, within the meaning of § 20-10, because she was not merely acting for herself. Although she did not receive commissions on the sale of homes, the payments she received were compensation under § 1-10. The court exercised its discretion under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 366(a)(5) to reduce the fine, noting that the company that owned the Web site had paid a significantly smaller fine. The court further held that a constitutional free speech argument was waived by failure to raise it sufficiently below.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision as modified to reflect a reduction in the fine.

Cutler v. Northwest Suburban Cmty. Hosp., Inc.


No. 2-09-1074


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


405 Ill. App. 3d 1052; 939 N.E.2d 1032; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1272; 345 Ill. Dec. 852



November 29, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 14, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Boone County. No. 05--L--13. Honorable John H. Young, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff brother appealed an order the Circuit Court of Boone County (Illinois) dismissing, under 735 ILCS 5/2-619 (2008), his medical malpractice action against defendants, two hospitals, several health services and treatment centers, and five doctors, which alleged that defendants were negligent in the postoperative care and treatment of the decedent, the brother's sister, and that their negligence caused her death.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the brother's action as a Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 219(c) sanction for failing to produce his expert for deposition and on the ground that the expert was not qualified to author the physican's report. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred by dismissing the brother's complaint because his expert was qualified to author the physician's report under 735 ILCS 5/2--622(a) (2004), as: (1) his report sufficiently set for the requisite § 2-622(a)(1) qualifications, including the fact that he was licensed to practice medicine in all its branches; (2) the expert had practiced within the last six years in the same area of health care law that was at issue, namely patients undergoing abdominal surgery and postoperative care; (3) the expert included detailed reasons for his determination that defendants' conduct fell below the standard of care; and (4) the expert's depositions showed that he had practiced in the last six years within the same area of health care at issue. The trial court also erred by dismissing the brother's complaint as a sanction for the failure to produce the expert for a deposition.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Ruisard v. Vill. of Glen Ellyn


No. 2-09-1083


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


406 Ill. App. 3d 644; 939 N.E.2d 1048; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1275; 345 Ill. Dec. 868; 51 Comm. Reg. (P & F) 1310



November 29, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 14, 2011.
Decision reached on appeal by Ruisard v. Village of Glen Ellyn, 2013 IL App (2d) 120480U, 2013 IL App (2d) 120480-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 189 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 08-CH-2550. Honorable Bonnie M. Wheaton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, Illinois, which granted a motion to dismiss filed by defendants, a village and a cell phone company, in an action opposing the addition of cell phone antennae to a water tower.


OVERVIEW: Glen Ellyn, Ill., Ordinance No. 3810 (1991) contained a condition that antennas on a water tower were to be kept to a minimum. Glen Ellyn, Ill., Ordinance 5606 (2007) allowed for the installation of a cellular antenna structure on the water tower. After the residents' first complaint was dismissed, they were granted leave to file a second amended complaint. A motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim was granted, and this appeal followed. In partially affirming, the appellate court held that the residents had standing challenge Glen Ellyn, Ill., Ordinance 3810 (1991) based on the language contained in 65 ILCS 5/11-13-15 (2008) and Glen Ellyn, Illinois, Zoning Code § 10-10-18(B). However, the residents failed to state a claim that the at a minimum requirement was violated. As to Glen Ellyn, Ill., Ordinance 5606 (2007), the village was properly named as a defendant since it was the owner of the property, and the residents had standing. A claim relating to radio frequency (RF) was preempted by the Telecommunications Act. However, the other allegations relating to Glen Ellyn, Ill., Ordinance 5606 (2007) should not have been dismissed for failure to state a claim.


OUTCOME: The portion of the decision that dismissed causes of action alleging a violation of Glen Ellyn, Ill., Ordinance 5606 not based upon RF emissions was reversed. The rest of the decision was affirmed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Johnson


No. 1-09-0879


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


408 Ill. App. 3d 157; 945 N.E.2d 610; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1256; 348 Ill. Dec. 841



November 24, 2010, Decided 
November 24, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 28, 2011.
Rehearing denied by People v. Johnson, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1466 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 23, 2010)
Appeal denied by People v. Johnson, 949 N.E.2d 662, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 757, 350 Ill. Dec. 870 (Ill., 2011)
Appeal denied by People v. Johnson, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1704 (Ill., Sept. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 04 CR 11607. The Honorable Kerry M. Kennedy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Cook County Circuit Court, Illinois, which convicted him of home invasion and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the trial court: (1) erred in rejecting his supplemental questions during voir dire regarding racial and ethnic bias; and (2) failed to comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 431(b). The appellate court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to ask the supplemental questions. Neither the State's theory of the prosecution nor the evidence demonstrated, in any fashion, that the crimes were motivated by race or ethnicity. Consequently, posing the proposed questions to the members of venire was irrelevant and would have tended to inject considerations of race into a case where the issue was absent. Although the trial court violated rule 431(b) by failing to ascertain whether the potential jurors understood and accepted each of the four Zehr principles, defendant forfeited the issue by failing to object at trial or in his posttrial motion. There was sufficient circumstantial evidence to link defendant to the crimes charged. While defendant claimed the evidence was closely balanced, he offered no challenge to its sufficiency. Because the evidence against defendant was not closely balanced, the appellate court honored the procedural default.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Crossroads Ford Truck Sales, Inc. v. Sterling Truck Corp.


NO. 4-10-0204


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


406 Ill. App. 3d 325; 943 N.E.2d 646; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1268; 348 Ill. Dec. 38



November 23, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Crossroads Ford Truck Sales, Inc. v. Sterling Truck Corp., 949 N.E.2d 657, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 683, 350 Ill. Dec. 865 (Ill., 2011)
Later proceeding at Crossroads Ford Truck Sales, Inc. v. Sterling Truck Corp., 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1134 (Ill., Sept. 21, 2011)
Affirmed by Crossroads Ford Truck Sales v. Sterling Truck Corp., 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1837 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 09L60. Honorable Patrick W. Kelley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motor vehicle dealer filed a second-amended complaint against appellees, corporation, its wholly owned subsidiary, and its president, for violations of the Motor Vehicle Franchise Act, 815 ILCS 710/1 et seq. (2008), fraud, and tortious interference with contract. The Circuit Court of Sangamon County, Illinois dismissed 12 of the 14 counts. The dealer filed a notice of interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that issues as to whether good cause existed to cancel or terminate a franchise or the refusal to extend the franchise were matters best left to the arbitrator or the Motor Vehicle Review Board under § 12(d) (815 ILCS 710/12(d) (2008)) of the Motor Vehicle Franchise Act and not the judiciary. As the circuit court did not have subject-matter jurisdiction over the 815 ILCS 710/4(d)(6) (2008) claims, the portions of the order dealing with those respective claims in the second-amended complaint were void and would not be addressed in the appeal. The allegations in two of the counts were nothing more than conclusions without specific facts in support. Thus, the dealer failed to state a cause of action under 815 ILCS 710/9(a) (2008). Although the dealer alleged the termination or nonrenewal of the franchise occurring after May 22, 2009, even with good cause, entitled the dealer to damages under 815 ILCS 710/9.5(a) (2009), the dealer failed to state a cause of action under 815 ILCS 710/9.5 because the sales and service agreement remained in effect and had not been terminated, and the subsidiary offered an extension of the agreement until December 31, 2012.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Davis


No. 1-08-2895


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


405 Ill. App. 3d 585; 940 N.E.2d 712; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1234; 346 Ill. Dec. 343



November 12, 2010, Decided 
November 12, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 6, 2011.
Rehearing denied by People v. Davis, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1431 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 17, 2010)
Appeal denied by People v. Davis, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 546 (Ill., Mar. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 07 CR 13118. Honorable James B. Linn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting him of violating the armed habitual criminal statute, 720 ILCS 5/24-1.7 (2006), and sentencing him to seven-and-a-half years in prison.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that even if the trial court failed to properly question prospective jurors as required by Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 431(b), which the court believed that it had, the error was not plain because defendant failed to identify any portion of the record affirmatively showing that the jury was not fair and impartial. The court rejected defendant's contention that 720 ILCS 5/24-1.7 was unconstitutional because defendant failed to show that making his prior convictions independent elements of the offense, rather than a sentencing enhancement, violated due process. Trial counsel was not ineffective for stipulating to defendant's prior convictions because doing so was inarguably less prejudicial than making the prior convictions an issue in the case. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to request a bifurcated trial because defendant failed to show that the trial court was authorized or compelled to order a bifurcated trial based on his prior convictions being elements of the offense. Counsel's opening statement did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

People v. Nesbitt


No. 2-09-0976


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


405 Ill. App. 3d 823; 938 N.E.2d 600; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1192; 345 Ill. Dec. 161



November 8, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 30, 2010


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Carroll County. No. 08-CF-49. Honorable Val Gunnarsson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Carroll County (Illinois) granting defendant's motion to suppress bank records belonging to her and her husband. Defendant had been charged with theft of property over $ 10,000 in violation of 720 ILCS 5/16-1(a)(2) (2008).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of obtaining by deception control over property in a bank in the amount of $ 40,200. On appeal, the court held that defendant did have a right to privacy in her bank records under Ill. Const. art. I, § 6. The court held that the intrusion was not reasonable under the Banking Act (Act), 205 ILCS 5/48.1 (2008) because: (1) there was no evidence supporting either that a police officer relied on the Act to make his or request of the bank or that the bank disclosed the records in reliance on the Act; and (2) the Act in no way provided an exception for state action. The intrusion was not reasonable in light of the parties' relationship, employee and employer, because the question was not whether the bank intruded into defendant's privacy but whether the State did. The court could not conclude that the State's request for documents, failure to obtain a subpoena or warrant, and intrusion on defendant's constitutional right to privacy in her bank records were reasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Lenczycki (In re Det. of Lenczycki)


No. 2-09-1052


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


405 Ill. App. 3d 1041; 938 N.E.2d 610; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1187; 345 Ill. Dec. 171



November 8, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 30, 2010


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 06--MR-486. Honorable Bonnie M. Wheaton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee priest was convicted of the aggravated criminal sexual abuse of three minors and served a term of incarceration for those convictions. Following a jury trial, the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) adjudicated him a sexually violent person under the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act (Act), 725 ILCS 207/1 et seq. (2006)), but permitted conditional release. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court erred by granting the priest conditional release. The appellate court held that the trial court's comment that one doctor's rescoring of the actuarial tests was "without foundation in the record" was supported by the doctor's testimony. The opinion was literally without foundation in the record and the trial court's characterization of it as such was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. Further, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by granting conditional release because two experts believed that the priest was unlikely to reoffend for a variety of reasons, and all of the actuarial tests administered by the various doctors reflected a low or, at most, moderate risk of rearrest for similar offenses. Additionally, the priest accepted responsibility for his actions, voluntarily admitted to previously unknown offenses, and was motivated and cooperative during his treatment in the secure detention facility. Moreover, the therapy he was receiving now would be more effective the restrictions and conditions imposed on the priest during his release were extensive.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Everhart


No. 1-08-3052


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


405 Ill. App. 3d 687; 939 N.E.2d 82; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1178; 345 Ill. Dec. 353



November 5, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 16, 2010.
Rehearing denied by Powell v. Everhart, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1354 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 9, 2010)
Appeal denied by People v. Everhart, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 541 (Ill., Mar. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 05 CR 21830. Honorable Michele M. Simmons, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of aggravated criminal sexual assault. It then sentenced him to natural life in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault after he attacked a woman, acted like he had a gun and would kill her if she did not submit, and sexually assaulted her. On appeal, he argued, inter alia, that he received ineffective assistance of counsel; that the trial court should not have admitted evidence he had previously committed that offense; that 725 ILCS 5/115-7.3 (2006) permitting admission of such evidence violated due process; and that the State failed to prove he violated the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute. The appellate court found that (1) he could not show he had been prejudiced when trial counsel stated defendant would testify and he did not do so; (2) the prior conviction evidence did not involve an offense too remote in time, but did involve a sufficiently similar offense for admissibility purposes; (3) the statute allowing admission of that evidence did not violate due process since the trial court under it could bar evidence that was too prejudicial; and (4) the State proved that he acted so as to threaten or endanger life and, thus, showed he violated the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute, 720 ILCS 5/12-14(a)(3) (2006).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and sentence.

Rajterowski v. City of Sycamore


No. 2-09-1136


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


405 Ill. App. 3d 1086; 940 N.E.2d 682; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1171; 346 Ill. Dec. 313



November 1, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 30, 2010.
Appeal denied by Rajterowski v. City of Sycamore, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 311 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of De Kalb County. No. 08-CH-271. Honorable Kurt P. Klein, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of De Kalb County (Illinois) dismissing their action against defendants, a city and a school district, alleging that the city's real estate transfer tax violated the federal and state constitutions and exceeded defendants' constitutional and statutory authority.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the taxpayers' complaint failed to sufficiently plead a violation of the privileges and immunities clause, U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2, cl. 1, because nowhere in the complaint did the taxpayers provide any factual allegations supporting their conclusion that residents of a foreign state who moved to the city and purchased real estate did not cause inadequate school funding. The taxpayers' complaint failed to state a claim that the ordinance was not rationally related to a legitimate government interest as required for a claim under the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment because the allegations showed that the ordinance made a reasonable distinction between those adding new burdens to the schools, who were subject to the transfer tax, and those who did not add to the underfunding, those were exempt from paying the tax. The taxpayers' claim that the tax violated the uniformity clause of Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 was also properly dismissed because it was reasonable to impose on new residents the one-time burden of contributing to the maintenance of a school district, as new residents generally will add to the school population and costs.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Jacobs


NO. 4-09-0878


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


405 Ill. App. 3d 210; 939 N.E.2d 64; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1168; 345 Ill. Dec. 335



November 1, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 07DT625. Honorable Charles McRae Leonhard, Judge Presiding.
People v. Jacobs, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 3337 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., Apr. 15, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment entered by the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted him of driving under the influence of alcohol and driving with an alcohol concentration of 0.08 or more under 625 ILCS 5/11-501(a) (2006).


OVERVIEW: A state trooper pulled defendant's vehicle over for having his high beams on within 500 feet of another vehicle. Defendant had a flushed face and red, glossy eyes and smelled of alcohol. Defendant performed the nine-step-walk-and-turn test correctly but failed the one-legged-stand test because he swayed slightly and raised his arms more than six inches past his side. The trooper arrested defendant; defendant agreed to take a Breathalyzer test, which registered a blood alcohol concentration (BAC) of 0.11. On appeal, the court affirmed. While defendant argued that the State failed for provide a proper foundation that the Breathalyzer was tested regularly for accuracy and was working properly, the foundation testimony did not violate the Confrontation Clause, U.S. Const. amend. VI, because the certification regarding the device's testing was not testimonial as the person performing the testing of the device's accuracy did so with no particular prosecutorial use in mind. The prosecutor did not violate a motion in limine regarding the horizontal gaze nystagmus (HGN) test because the trooper was not asked about the test but made a remark in passing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Schmidt


No. 3-08-1037


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


405 Ill. App. 3d 474; 938 N.E.2d 559; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1163; 345 Ill. Dec. 120



October 27, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 7, 2010.
Appeal denied by People v. Schmidt, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 342 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, Hancock County, Illinois. No. 08-CF-28. Honorable David F. Stoverink, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, Hancock County, Illinois found defendant guilty of unlawful use of property, 720 ILCS 646/35(a) (2008), unlawful possession of methamphetamine precursor, 720 ILCS 646/20(b)(1) (2008), unlawful possession of methamphetamine, 720 ILCS 646/60(a) (2008), obstructing justice, 720 ILCS 5/31-4(a) (2008), and aggravated fleeing, 625 ILCS 5/11-204.1(a)(1) (2008). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that his conviction for unlawful use of property cannot stand as § 35 of the Methamphetamine Control and Community Protection Act, 720 ILCS 646/35 (2008) was unconstitutional as it bore no reasonable relationship to a legitimate state interest. The appellate court found that 720 ILCS 646/35 satisfied the rational basis test because: (1) its language showed the legislature intended to safeguard the public welfare from the harm caused by manufacturing and distribution of methamphetamine; (2) prohibiting the use of a vehicle to bring about a violation of the Act was a reasonable method of accomplishing the Act's desired objective: that was, reducing or eliminating methamphetamine-related crimes in the state and the corresponding harm caused by those crimes; and (3) 720 ILCS 646/35's proscription against using vehicles to bring about a violation of the Act was reasonably designed to remedy the evils that the legislature has determined to be a threat to the public health, safety and general welfare of the state and was reasonably related to stopping the manufacturing and distribution of methamphetamine in the state.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed with the exception of defendant's conviction for possession of methamphetamine, which was vacated as a lesser-included offense of unlawful use of property. The case was remanded to the circuit court to modify its sentencing order consistent with the opinion.

Hytel Group, Inc. v. Butler


No. 2-09-1003


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


405 Ill. App. 3d 113; 938 N.E.2d 542; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1113; 345 Ill. Dec. 103; 31 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 859; 160 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P61,074



October 20, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 19, 2010.
Rehearing denied by Hytel Group, Inc. v. Butler, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1241 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Nov. 19, 2010)
Appeal dismissed by Hytel Group, Inc. v. Butler, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 514 (Ill., Mar. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 08-L-717. Honorable Robert B. Spence, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois), where plaintiff former employer sued defendant former employee claiming breach of fiduciary duties and fraudulent misrepresentations, and she moved to dismiss under 735 ILCS 5/2-615 (2008) and the Citizen Participation Act, 735 ILCS 110/1 et seq. (2008) (Act), granted the motion based on the Act. It then awarded to her some of the attorney fees requested. It appealed the dismissal; she cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The former employer hired the former employee as a comptroller. Even before she was hired, the former employer allegedly was in default on loan agreement obligations. Its lender was seeking appointment of a receiver. The former employer then fired her. She filed a wage claim with the state labor department seeking wages she was allegedly owed. The former employer soon sued her for breach of fiduciary duty and fraudulent misrepresentations allegedly connected to future employment she could expect with the lender once the loan dispute ended. She moved to dismiss under both 735 ILCS 5/2-615 (2008) and the Citizen Participation Act, 735 ILCS 110/1 et seq. (2008) (Act). The trial court dismissed based on the Act. It also awarded her attorney fees, although less than she requested. The appellate court found that the claims against her could be dismissed under the Act, as they "related to" her petitioning government regarding the wage claim, as required by 735 ILCS 110/15 (2008). It also found that the trial court should have included in her attorney fee award under 735 ILCS 110/25 (2008) the time spent preparing the petition for fees, which was recoverable under the Act.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment, although it modified that judgment to permit the former employee to recover attorney fees incurred in preparing and presenting a motion for fees pursuant to the Act.

Protein Partners, LLP v. Lincoln Provision, Inc.


No. 1-09-0823


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1105



October 19, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified December 21, 2010
Opinion withdrawn by Protein Partners, LLC v. Lincoln Provision, Inc., 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1352 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 16, 2010)
Modified and rehearing denied by Protein Partners, LLP v. Lincoln Provision, Inc., 941 N.E.2d 308, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1382, 346 Ill. Dec. 750 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 21, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 08 MI 602017. Honorable Patrick J. Sherlock, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant judgment debtor appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied its motion to quash plaintiff judgment creditor's registration of a foreign judgment under the Illinois Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act, 735 ILCS 5/12-650 et seq. (2008).


OVERVIEW: The creditor obtained a judgment against the debtor in Ohio. The debtor was served with the complaint according to the rules of Ohio civil procedure. It did not file an appearance, and a default judgment was entered against it in Ohio. The motion to quash was filed more than 30 days after the registration of the Ohio judgment in the circuit court. The court observed that the foreign judgment was subject under 735 ILCS 5/12-652(a) (2008) to the same procedures and defenses as any judgment entered in the circuit court, including the requirement of 735 ILCS 5/2-1203(a) (2008) that a posttrial motion be filed within 30 days. Because the motion to quash was untimely, the court construed it as a petition under 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2008) and found it appealable under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 304(b)(3). The court characterized the debtor's allegation that the creditor was not registered to do business in Ohio as intrinsic fraud in the procurement of the Ohio judgment; as such, it was a defense that the debtor could advance in an Ohio court. Technical defects in the parties' names during the course of the litigation were not fatal to the registration and did not amount to fraud.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Sandholm v. Kuecker


No. 2-09-1015


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


405 Ill. App. 3d 835; 942 N.E.2d 544; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1095; 347 Ill. Dec. 341; 38 Media L. Rep. 2377



October 18, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 3, 2010.
Appeal granted by Sandholm v. Kuecker, 239 Ill. 2d 589, 943 N.E.2d 1109, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 186, 348 Ill. Dec. 199 (2011)
Later proceeding at Sandholm v. Kuecker, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1133 (Ill., Sept. 21, 2011)
Reversed by, Remanded by Sandholm v. Kuecker, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 33 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lee County. No. 08-L-19. Honorable David L. Jeffrey, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lee County Circuit Court (Illinois) dismissed plaintiff high school basketball coach's lawsuit against defendant vocal opponents alleging defamation, false light, and tortious interference claims involving their attempts to have him removed from his position as coach and athletic director. It then limited their attorney fee award to the fees connected to the motion to dismiss. He appealed; they cross-appealed the fee ruling.


OVERVIEW: The vocal opponents started a campaign to have the coach removed as a high school's head basketball coach and athletic director due to their disagreement with his coaching style. When the school board did not remove him, they continued the campaign. Eventually, the school board removed him as a coach although he remained as an athletic director. The coach sued the vocal opponents alleging defamation, false light, and tortious interference claims. The trial court dismissed all claims against them upon finding that they had immunity under the Citizen Participation Act, 735 ILCS 110/1 et seq. (2008) (Act). It then limited their attorney fee award to the fees incurred in obtaining dismissal under the Act. The appellate court found that (1) the coach did not show that the Act was unconstitutional, as the legislature in enacting it properly balanced the right to petition the government for favorable action and a party's right to common law relief; (2) the Act applied to their attempts to get the school board to act favorably; and (3) the trial court, pursuant to the Act, properly limited the attorney fee award to the vocal opponents despite the case involved more than the Act.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment in its entirety.

People v. Thompson


No. 3-09-0019


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


404 Ill. App. 3d 265; 936 N.E.2d 195; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1060; 344 Ill. Dec. 53



October 5, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 20, 2010.
Rehearing denied by People v. Thompson, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1097 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., Oct. 20, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 07-CF-1521. Honorable Michael E. Brandt, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois, which convicted him of armed robbery and sentenced him to 26 years of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with four counts of armed robbery, and he entered a written waiver of a trial by jury. Later, he entered into a partially negotiated plea agreement where three of the counts were dismissed. The trial court announced that the parties had decided to proceed by way of a stipulated bench trial as to one count of robbery so that defense counsel could have later challenged the constitutionality of a 20-year sentencing enhancement under 720 ILCS 5/18-2(b) (2008). Defendant was sentenced to 26 years in prison, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court rejected the argument that the stipulated bench trial was tantamount to a guilty plea and that a remand was necessary for the trial court to comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 605(c) and Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d). Defense counsel did not stipulate that the facts presented by the State were sufficient for a finding of guilt. Moreover, it was clear that defense counsel was proceeding to a stipulated bench trial to preserve the constitutional issue. Defendant, with full knowledge and understanding of the proceedings, was allowed to preserve an issue for appeal and still receive the benefit of the plea proceeding.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Sherman v. Twp. High Sch. Dist. 214


No. 1-09-2746


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


404 Ill. App. 3d 1101; 937 N.E.2d 286; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1053; 344 Ill. Dec. 580



September 30, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 08, 2010.
Rehearing denied by Sherman v. Twp. High Sch. Dist. 214, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1227 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Oct. 27, 2010)
Review denied by Sherman v. Twp. High Sch. Dist. 214, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 276 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 09 CH 03690. Honorable Peter A. Flynn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a minor, through her father, filed a declaratory judgment action against appellees, school district and Illinois State Board of Education, and asserted that a $ 350 fee for a drivers' education course was unauthorized under Ill. Adm. Code tit. 23, § 252.30(a)(3), amended at 32 Ill. Reb. 10935 (2008), and Ill. Const. art. X, § 1. The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois dismissed the case with prejudice. The minor appealed.


OVERVIEW: Although the minor alleged that the district's request and renewal applications for waiver under 105 ILCS 5/2-3.25g(c) (2008) of the Illinois School Code, 105 ILCS 5/27-23 (2008), which sought to increase the driver's education fees in the district to include staffing costs, were unconstitutional under the free education clause, Ill. Const art. X, § 1, and were therefore invalid, 105 ILCS 5/27-23 (2008) provided that the school district may charge a reasonable fee, and the language of the statute must be given its plain and ordinary meaning, which illustrated that it was never intended to be free. Therefore, because driver's education was not covered by the free education clause, the $ 350 Drivers Education Course fee did not violate Ill. Const art. X, § 1, and the minor's complaint against the school district was properly dismissed with prejudice. The Illinois State Board of Education did not have the obligation to reject the district's waiver request for anything other than completeness, 105 ILCS 5/2-3.25g(d) (2008), and that completeness review did not warrant consideration of Ill. Admin. Code tit. 23, § 252.30(a)(3). Therefore, the Board was not a proper party defendant.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal was affirmed.

Knight v. Van Matre Rehab. Ctr., LLC


No. 2-09-1127


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


404 Ill. App. 3d 214; 936 N.E.2d 1152; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1044; 344 Ill. Dec. 395



September 29, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 12, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 09-L-229. Honorable J. Edward Prochaska, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of the dismissal entered by the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) of her medical malpractice complaint against defendants, a doctor and a rehabilitation center, on the basis that she failed to timely file a health care professional's report under 735 ILCS 5/2-622.


OVERVIEW: While the patient was a resident of the center, the doctor prescribed a medication for the patient that adversely affected her. When the patient had not filed her health care professional's report under 735 ILCS 5/2-622 within 90 days after filing her medical malpractice complaint, defendants made a motion to dismiss. The patient responded with a motion for additional time to file the report and filed the report, without leave of the trial court, within two weeks of the motion to dismiss. The trial court granted the motion to dismiss with prejudice on the basis that 735 ILCS 5/2-622 only allowed one 90-day extension for the filing of the report. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. Because 2005 Ill. Laws 677, which had added the provision regarding only one 90-day extension, had been declared unconstitutional after the action had been filed, 735 ILCS 5/2-622 reverted to its pre-2005 provisions, which did not include the limitation on extensions to file the report. The action was remanded for the trial court to determine whether the patient could establish good cause for not filing the report within 90 days.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal and remanded to the trial court for consideration of whether the patient should have extra time to filed the health care professional's report and whether striking the report that the patient filed previously was proper.

Macknin v. Macknin


No. 2-10-0221


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


404 Ill. App. 3d 520; 937 N.E.2d 270; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1041; 344 Ill. Dec. 564



September 23, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended September 28, 2010. Released for Publication October 22, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. Nos. 08-D-287, 09-OP-1220. Honorable George D. Strickland, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner natural mother sought a protection order against respondent/appellee ex-husband and alleged that he had sexually abused subpoena respondent/appellant minor daughter. After an emergency order of protection was entered, the ex-husband issued a deposition subpoena to the daughter. The Circuit Court of Lake County, Illinois granted the ex-husband's motion to disqualify the attorney hired to represent the daughter. The daughter appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ex-husband's motion to disqualify alleged a conflict of interest in the attorney representing the daughter and that, pursuant to the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, 750 ILCS 5/506 (2008) and article IX of the Supreme Court Rules, Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 900 et seq., the daughter could only be represented only by independent court-appointed counsel. The trial court did not make a finding of a conflict of interest but disqualified the attorney on the second ground alleged and appointed a county representative for the daughter. The court found that because the ex-husband did not have custody of the daughter and she was not involved in any custody or visitation matter, article IX was inapplicable to the daughter. Article IX was not a vehicle to appoint counsel. Rather, it represented a minimum standard or guideline when the trial court did appoint counsel for a minor who was involved in a custody dispute, so that the custody matter was expedited. Accordingly, the trial court abused its discretion by exceeding its authority and disqualifying the attorney pursuant to § 506 of the Dissolution of Marriage Act and article IX.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

Am. Bev. Ass'n v. City of Chicago


No. 1-09-1511


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


404 Ill. App. 3d 682; 937 N.E.2d 261; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1014; 344 Ill. Dec. 555



September 23, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 08, 2010.
Appeal denied by Am. Bev. Ass'n v. City of Chicago, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 171 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 08 CH 396. Honorable E. James Tolmaire III, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business associations sought review of a summary judgment entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) in favor of defendant city in plaintiffs' action challenging the constitutionality of Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 3-43-030 (2008) for imposing an unconstitutional occupation tax that violated Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e)(2), and violated the uniformity clause of Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance imposed a five cent per bottle tax on the sale of bottled water within the city; the tax had to be collected from the retail dealer by the wholesale dealer. On appeal, the court affirmed. The tax was not an unconstitutional occupation tax in violation of Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e)(2) because the tax was on tangible personal property and the ordinance expressly declared that the tax was to be paid by the purchaser. 65 ILCS 5/8-11-1(2002) did not apply because the bottled water tax was a sales tax rather than an occupation tax and was not measured by the gross receipts from sales but instead was a flat amount on each bottle sold. The uniformity clause in art. IX, § 2 was not violated because a real and substantial difference existed between the bottled water taxed and the beverages marketed for certain specific features, such as flavoring, that were not taxed and the classification bore a reasonable relationship to the object of the legislation to discourage the purchase of bottled water to, inter alia, conserve energy from nonrenewable sources because the bottles were made from nonrenewable petroleum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision.

People v. Adams


No. 1-08-0455


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION

People v. Adams, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1127 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Aug. 17, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of armed habitual criminal and sentenced to a term of 30 years' imprisonment. Defendant's motions for a new trial and to reconsider sentence were denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by excluding his proposed testimony of a private investigator regarding the transferability of gunshot residue and that defendant's hands could have acquired the gunshot residue from a contaminated environment rather than from handling the rifle. The court of appeals disagreed. The investigator utterly lacked the requisite education, experience or qualifications necessary to be offered as an expert. The investigator acknowledged that he was something of a hobbyist when it came to the analysis of gunshot residue beyond matters of basic collection of the evidence. Moreover, he did not exhibit any particular expertise in the area of transferability of gunshot residue over and above that offered by the State's expert who explained the dynamics of transference. The judge clearly understood the objective of the defense in offering the testimony and aptly perceived the shortcomings of the investigator's expertise as it related to that objective. It was clear the investigator lacked any education or training in the sciences nor did he have sufficient experience to support any such conclusions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Oakridge Dev. Co. v. Prop. Tax Appeal Bd.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for Review of the Order of the Illinois Property Tax Appeal Board. No. 06-01901.001-F-3.



DISPOSITION: Confirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, current and prior owners, appealed an order by respondent Illinois Property Tax Appeal Board that upheld respondent county board of review's rejection of their property tax appeal; the owners claimed that the Board erred in concluding that the subject property was not eligible for farmland classification under 35 ILCS 200/10-110 (2008) for property tax purposes.


OVERVIEW: For the eight years preceding 2006, the prior owners used the property for farming. In anticipation of a sale to the current owners, the prior owners declined to plant a crop in 2006. The court found, inter alia, in order to qualify for farmland valuation and assessment under 35 ILCS 200/10-110 (2008) the property had to be used as a farm for the two preceding years as well as the year under review. Because the property was not used as a farm during 2006, the owners were not entitled to valuation and assessment as farmland.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Du Page County Circuit Court (Illinois), after preliminary proceedings, entered a judgment that granted plaintiff city's motion for immediate vesting of title under the Eminent Domain Act, 735 ILCS 30/20-5-5 (2008), in a case where the city sought to condemn defendant cemetery owner's cemetery as the city sought to expand its airport. McKinley Found. at the Univ. of Ill. v. Ill. Dep't of Labor


NO. 4-09-0512


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


404 Ill. App. 3d 1115; 936 N.E.2d 708; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 955; 344 Ill. Dec. 179



September 10, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by McKinley Found. at the Univ. of Ill. v. Ill. Dep't of Labor, 239 Ill. 2d 555, 943 N.E.2d 1101, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 117, 348 Ill. Dec. 191 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2011)
Appeal denied by McKinley Found. at the Univ. of Ill. v. Ill. Dep't of Labor, 239 Ill. 2d 555, 943 N.E.2d 1101, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 54, 348 Ill. Dec. 191 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2011)
Appeal denied by McKinley Found. v. Ill. Dep't of Labor, 239 Ill. 2d 555, 943 N.E.2d 1101, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 29, 348 Ill. Dec. 191 (Ill., Jan. 26, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 08MR688. Honorable Michael Q. Jones, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Champaign County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted summary judgment to plaintiff foundation and defendants, a construction company and its subcontractors, after they claimed that the construction project all of them were involved in was not subject to the Prevailing Wage Act, 820 ILCS 130/1 et seq. (2008) (Act), because the foundation was not a "public body" under the Act. Defendant state labor department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The foundation, a not-for-profit corporation functioning as a Presbyterian ministry for college students, contracted with the construction company to build student housing and parking on its property. Financing, in part, stemmed from tax-free bonds issued through the Illinois Finance Authority. It sought summary judgment in a declaratory judgment case against the state labor department in which it claimed that the Prevailing Wage Act, 820 ILCS 130/1 et seq. (2008), was inapplicable because the foundation was not a "public body" under the Act. The trial court granted summary judgment to the foundation, contractor, and subcontractors. The appellate court found that the foundation was a "public body" under the Act since it financed its project with tax-exempt bonds issued under the Illinois Finance Authority Act, 20 ILCS 3501/801-1 et seq. (2008). It also rejected the foundation's claims that the Act violated equal protection, since the Act was rationally related to protecting workers, or the establishment clauses of the state and federal constitutions because the foundation's status as a private religious foundation was irrelevant to its identity under the establishment clauses.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

899 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gibson


No. 2-08-0738


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


403 Ill. App. 3d 942; 934 N.E.2d 611; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 880; 343 Ill. Dec. 287



August 19, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 1, 2010.
Appeal denied by People v. Gibson, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 695 (Ill., May 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 06-CF-1904. Honorable George J. Bakalis, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) of armed robbery, aggravated kidnapping, and unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon. The trial court sentenced defendant to concurrent prison terms of 12 years, 27 years, and 12 years, for each offense, respectively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that because his testimony that he participated in the crimes to avert harm to his family constituted, at the very least, "some evidence" to support his affirmative defense of necessity, the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on the defense. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant had other reasonable alternatives to acting as an accomplice to armed robbery and aggravated kidnapping. Defendant's own testimony revealed that when defendant knew what was happening and had opportunities to withdraw or ask for help, he chose to continue his association with the principals and aid and abet them in their criminal conduct. Defendant testified that, after he knew that he was contributing to numerous crimes, he was left sitting alone in the van. Yet, defendant did not attempt to flee or use his cell phone to call 911 or anyone else; instead, he smoked marijuana. Despite the fact that defendant had ample opportunity to use his cell phone to call 911 or his family, he never did. Further, when defendant was driving the van while the principals were in the truck with the victim, he could have driven away instead of following them.


OUTCOME: The unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon conviction under an accountability theory was reversed and the sentence was vacated. The case was remanded for resentencing on defendant's convictions of aggravated kidnapping. Defendant was given an additional day of jail credit.

People v. Snow


NO. 4-09-0924


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


403 Ill. App. 3d 734; 936 N.E.2d 662; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 913; 344 Ill. Dec. 133



August 18, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. No. 09DT33. Honorable Robert M. Travers, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol. He refused to submit to chemical testing and the State notified him his license would be suspended under 625 ILCS 5/11-501.1 (2008). Defendant's petition to rescind the summary suspension was denied. The Circuit Court of Livingston County (Illinois) ruled that the State was prohibited from presenting testimony from the suspension hearing in the criminal trial. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court erred by barring the use of defendant's testimony given at the rescission hearing as substantive evidence in the subsequent criminal proceeding. Defendant argued that he did not have a free choice whether to testify or remain silent at the rescission hearing, as the loss of his driving privileges was at stake. If he testified he risked being convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol. If he remained silent, he risked the suspension of his driving privilege. The appellate court agreed with the State, concluding that since defendant chose to testify instead of claiming the privilege against self-incrimination, his disclosures were not compelled incriminations. Therefore, defendant was foreclosed from invoking the privilege when such information was later introduced against him in the criminal prosecution. Defendant's rescission-hearing testimony was entirely voluntary and subsequently admissible in the criminal proceedings.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

People v. Dawson


No. 1-08-2106


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION

August 18, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 6, 2010.
Appeal denied by People v. Dawson, 238 Ill. 2d 659, 942 N.E.2d 457, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1790, 347 Ill. Dec. 254 (2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Dawson v. Illinois, 131 S. Ct. 2880, 179 L. Ed. 2d 1194, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 3381 (U.S., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. No. 07 CR 16141 (01). Honorable Joseph M. Claps, Judge Presiding.
People v. McCray, 395 Ill. App. 3d 1116, 986 N.E.2d 806, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 5550, 369 Ill. Dec. 493 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of three counts of aggravated discharge of a firearm and two counts of aggravated unlawful use of a weapon. Defendant was sentenced to eight years' imprisonment for the aggravated discharge of a firearm convictions and three years' imprisonment for the aggravated unlawful use of a weapon convictions. Defendant was assessed a $ 5 court system fee. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that 720 ILCS 5/24-1.6 was unconstitutional as violating U.S. Const. amend. II. The court of appeals disagreed. The holdings upon which defendant relied were limited to the question presented - the right to possess a commonly used firearm, a handgun, in the home for self-defense purposes. In the instant case, defendant was carrying the loaded firearm in his vehicle and shot at a person. Defendant also argued that the evidence was insufficient to sustain one conviction for aggravated discharge of a firearm. The court of appeals disagreed. The officer identified defendant as one of the shooters in the second shooting and corroborated much of the victim's disavowed testimony as to that event. Further, physical evidence linked both shootings to the handguns, shell casings and bullets that were found at the scene of the second shooting, in the car and in the victim's vehicle. Further, defendant was identified as one of the men holding a gun at the second shooting and discarding the guns through the window. That corroborating evidence provided support sufficient to support the victim's disavowed statement.


OUTCOME: The $ 5 court system fee and defendant's convictions under counts III and VII were vacated. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

People v. Raymond


No. 1-08-2891


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


404 Ill. App. 3d 1028; 938 N.E.2d 131; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 852; 344 Ill. Dec. 862



August 13, 2010, Decided 
August 13, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 13, 2010.
Rehearing denied by People v. Raymond, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1318 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Dec. 9, 2010)
Appeal denied by People v. Raymond, 949 N.E.2d 663, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 698, 350 Ill. Dec. 871 (Ill., 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Raymond, 2013 IL App (1st) 120087-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2449 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 06 CR 15120. Honorable Diane Cannon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. The trial court sentenced him to 20 years' imprisonment. Defendant's motion to reconsider the sentence was denied, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in admitting evidence concerning defendant's prior conviction for aggravated criminal sexual abuse under 725 ILCS 5/115-7.3. The court of appeals disagreed. There were general areas of similarity between the two crimes. The two victims were female and were in the same age range of 12 to 14 years old. Defendant was significantly older than each of the girls; he was almost 20 when he assaulted the prior complainant and 23 when he committed the charged offense against the victim. Both girls had problems with their home lives; the prior complainant described herself as a "runaway" and a "runner," while evidence indicated that the victim had not attended school on at least one occasion, prompting her mother to inform the police. Both began as consensual encounters, and both involved vaginal penetration. Defendant's closing argument reduced the prejudicial value of the evidence because defense counsel specifically asked the jury not to give the prior conviction any weight. Therefore, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence of defendant's prior conviction for aggravated criminal sexual abuse.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Owens v. Dep't of Human Rights


No. 1-09-0908


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


403 Ill. App. 3d 899; 936 N.E.2d 623; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 851; 344 Ill. Dec. 94



August 13, 2010, Decided 
August 13, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 16, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for review of An Order of the Chief Legal Counsel of the Illinois, Department of Human Rights. No. 2005 CA 2283.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Chief Legal Counsel for respondent Illinois Department of Human Rights entered a decision that found petitioner employee had failed to present substantial evidence in support of his charge that respondent employer was discriminating against him. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed an amended charge of discrimination against the employer alleging it issued two written reprimands against him despite him satisfactorily performing his duties as a warehouse worker fulfilling customer orders. He claimed that he received the reprimands due to his race, African-American, and his age, 55, in violation of the Illinois Human Rights Acts, 775 ILCS 5/2-102(A) (2004) (Act). The state human rights department investigated and found that he failed to present substantial evidence supporting his charge. Eventually, the chief legal counsel sustained the department's finding. The appellate court found that the employee did not present substantial evidence and, thus, did not show that the chief legal counsel's decision was an abuse of discretion. It determined that the employee did not show that either reprimand resulted in an adverse employment action against him or that similarly-situated workers not in the protected classes had been treated differently. It also held that he waived his claim that the 775 ILCS 5/7A-102(D)(2) (2004) substantial evidence standard was unconstitutionally vague because he did not show that it implicated First Amendment concerns.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the decision of the chief legal counsel of the state human rights department sustaining the department's decision to dismiss the employee's discrimination charge.

Snyder v. Heidelberger


No. 2-08-1061


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


403 Ill. App. 3d 974; 933 N.E.2d 1235; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 882; 342 Ill. Dec. 942



August 12, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 24, 2010.
Appeal granted by Snyder v. Heidelberger, 238 Ill. 2d 675, 942 N.E.2d 462, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1758, 347 Ill. Dec. 259 (2010)
Reversed by Snyder v. Heidelberger, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1097 (Ill., June 16, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 08-CH-802. Honorable Kenneth L. Popejoy, Judge, Presiding.
Snyder v. Heidelberger, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 964 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Oct. 6, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Du Page County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed plaintiff widow's claim against defendant attorney for alleged legal malpractice in the drafting of a deed to real property that her late husband allegedly intended to convey to her as his joint tenant. It did so after finding the claim to be barred by the statute of repose, 735 ILCS 5/13-214.3(c) (1994). The widow appealed.


OVERVIEW: The widow's late husband, shortly after they were married, retained the attorney to draft a deed to the premises where the widow and late husband lived to make him and the widow co-owners in joint tenancy with rights of survivorship. The attorney prepared a quitclaim deed that, by its terms, conveyed title to the premises from the late husband to the late husband and widow in joint tenancy. The next month, the attorney recorded the deed. More than 10 years after the deed was drafted and recorded, the late husband died. The widow then determined that the quitclaim deed conveyed nothing to her because the late husband did not hold title to the premises but merely held the beneficial interest in a land trust that did. She sued the attorney for legal malpractice about two months after the late husband died. The trial court found that the six-year statute of repose, 735 ILCS 5/13-214.3(c) (1994), applied and dismissed her claim. The appellate court disagreed and determined that she merely had to file within two years of the late husband's death pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/13-214.3 (1994) because the late husband could have corrected the problem at any time up to the time of his death.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Hill


No. 1-08-0116


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


402 Ill. App. 3d 903; 934 N.E.2d 43; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 773; 343 Ill. Dec. 43



August 4, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 11, 2010.
Appeal granted by People v. Hill, 238 Ill. 2d 663, 942 N.E.2d 458, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1685, 347 Ill. Dec. 255 (2010)
Appeal dismissed by People v. Hill, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1827 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Nicholas Ford, Judge Presiding.
People v. Hill, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 645 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 30, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for first degree murder and home invasion. Defendant was sentenced to 60 years in prison. A prior decision was modified upon rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that his sentence should be vacated because the State's notice of intent to seek the death penalty was not filed until 247 days after his arraignment, rather than 120 days, in violation of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 416(c). Defendant's motion to strike the notice had been denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. The issue was not moot because although a death sentence was not imposed, if the trial court had found defendant was not eligible for the death penalty, it might have sentenced defendant to less than 60 years in prison, and the instant court could remand for resentencing. Because Rule 416 contained no negative language prohibiting the State from pursuing the death penalty in the absence of a timely filed notice, the rule was directory as no specific consequence was triggered by the failure to comply. Reversal was not mandated because the rights intended to be protected were actually protected in defendant's case as he was provided with additional attorneys who specialized in death penalty cases and received additional peremptory challenges and permission to life qualify the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the matter with directions to vacate, with the State's agreement, the $ 5 court system fee, the $ 10 mental health court assessment, the $ 5 youth diversion/peer court assessment, the $ 5 drug court assessment, and the $ 25 court supervision assessment and to amend the fines and fees order to reflect a reduction in the total amount of $ 50.

Vill. of Woodridge v. Bd. of Educ. of Cmty. High Sch. Dist. 99


No. 2-08-0593


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


403 Ill. App. 3d 559; 933 N.E.2d 392; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 753; 342 Ill. Dec. 806



July 26, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 26, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 05--ED--64. Honorable John T. Elsner, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant district challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, Illinois, which denied a traverse and motion to dismiss in response to an eminent domain proceeding initiated by plaintiff village. The district also challenged the denial of a motion to reconsider.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that the taking would not have materially interfered with an existing use and was not detrimental to the public. The district then sought review. In affirming, the appellate court rejected the argument that the case was not justiciable because it required the resolution of two competing legislative determinations. There were clear criteria set forth for deciding the case under 65 ILCS 5/11-61-2 (2004), and there was no deference given to the legislative enactments of the units of local government. There was no abuse of discretion in denying the district's discovery requests because the material sought was not relevant. Next, the taking was authorized by 65 ILCS 5/11-61-2 (2004). The village was permitted to use the property to expand its facilities. Holding the property for a future use or for an investment did not constitute a "use already existing" within the meaning of 65 ILCS 5/11-61-2 (2004). There was no error in the trial court's finding that the taking was not detrimental to the public. The trial court did not err by excluding evidence of an offer, and the district did not suffer any meaningful prejudice from the exclusion of certain testimony.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of the first-degree murder of his eight-month-old son in violation of 720 ILCS 5/9-1(a)(2) (2004). It then imposed a mandatory term of life imprisonment. Defendant appealed the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's eight-month-old son was rushed to the hospital and placed on life support. He died soon thereafter. The State charged defendant with first degree murder and claimed that defendant shook the child to death. Defendant claimed that the death was due to brain damage from a seizure. It also found that the State proved under 720 ILCS 5/9-1(a)(2) (2004) that defendant knew his conduct in shaking the child created a strong probability of great bodily harm. Finally, it found that because the sentence of life imprisonment violated the Illinois Constitution's single-subject clause, defendant had to be resentenced.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction, vacated defendant's sentence of life imprisonment.

People v. Meyer


NO. 4-09-0153


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


402 Ill. App. 3d 1089; 931 N.E.2d 1274; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 713; 342 Ill. Dec. 91; 73 A.L.R.6th 699



July 8, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Meyer, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1481 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., Aug. 3, 2010)
Appeal denied by People v. Meyer, 238 Ill. 2d 666, 942 N.E.2d 459, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1690, 347 Ill. Dec. 256 (2010)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Meyer, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1031, 2012 IL App (4th) 100842U (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Adams County. No. 06CF743. Honorable Scott H. Walden, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions entered by the Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois) for two counts of unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, a Class 3 felony under 720 ILCS 5/24-1.1(a), (e) (2006).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed, inter alia, that trial counsel was ineffective and that the evidence was insufficient to sustain a conviction for possession of handgun ammunition. On appeal, the court affirmed. A video obtained by a confidential informant (CI) while he was present in defendant's trailer did not require a warrant under U.S. Const. amend. IV or Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 as defendant had no constitutionally protected privacy interest in any activity that the CI viewed while in his home. A search warrant application was not deficient because the CI's affidavit indicated that he had seen hydrocodone pills inside defendant's home within 72 hours of filing and had purchased prescription narcotic pills from defendant in the past. Defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to stipulate to defendant's prior conviction as the prior burglary conviction was over 30 years old at the time of trial and there was little danger that he was convicted based on an improper propensity inference. The statutory definition of firearm ammunition in 430 ILCS 65/1.1 (2006) did not require proof that the ammunition was live but only that it was designed to be used or adaptable to use in a firearm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of first degree murder and home invasion in the death of his former girlfriend. It then imposed a 60-year prison sentence upon defendant. Defendant appealed.

People v. Lara

As a result, he was charged with predatory criminal sexual assault in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-14.1(a)(1) (2006). Following a trial, a jury found him guilty.
