People v. Lamming


NO. 5-07-0471


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1058



June 17, 2010, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. Nos. 88-CF-337 & 88-CF-715. Honorable Charles V. Romani, Jr., Judge, presiding.
People v. Lamming, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1744 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., Feb. 25, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Motion granted; judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Madison County, Illinois, dismissing his petition for postjudgment relief. The State appellate defender filed a motion to withdraw as counsel, alleging that there was no merit to the appeal.


OVERVIEW: In 1988 the petitioner pled guilty to various offenses in two cases in exchange for the State's sentence recommendation. After admonishing the petitioner, the trial court accepted the petitioner's guilty plea and sentenced him in accordance with the plea agreement. The appellate court ruled that the petitioner's 735 ILCS 5/2-1401(f) (2006) petition did not set forth any allegation that the trial court lacked personal or subject matter jurisdiction. Although the entry of a judgment on multiple convictions in violation of the one-act/one-crime rule constituted error, it did not divest the trial court of jurisdiction, and the erroneous judgment was merely voidable, not void. The petition failed to set forth any cognizable claim that the petitioner's convictions and sentences were void. Also, the State fully performed its obligations under the plea agreement. The petitioner did not argue that the trial court's failure to admonish him regarding mandatory supervised release denied him due process or the benefit of his plea bargain. Caselaw did not suggest that the failure to admonish a defendant regarding mandatory supervised release deprived the trial court of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The motion to withdraw was granted, and the judgment was affirmed.

People v. 1998 Lexus GS 300


No. 1-09-0444


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


402 Ill. App. 3d 462; 930 N.E.2d 582; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 585; 341 Ill. Dec. 372



June 14, 2010, Decided 
June 14, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Publication allowed June 11, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 08 COFO 00312. Honorable Mark J. Ballard, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vehicle owner challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, which entered an order of forfeiture under 720 ILCS 5/36-1 (2002).


OVERVIEW: The owner was arrested for driving with a license that had been revoked because of a prior driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI) conviction. His vehicle was seized and subsequently forfeited. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court noted that the trial court considered mitigating factors and still concluded that a forfeiture was warranted. Moreover, there was nothing that required the trial court to consider mitigating evidence in determining the propriety of a vehicle forfeiture. The trial court's ruling was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. Next, the forfeiture of the vehicle did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The forfeiture of the vehicle in this case was not grossly disproportionate to the offense of driving on a revoked license. Driving with a revoked license that stemmed from a DUI conviction was one of the most serious driving offenses that could have been committed absent bodily injury. A forfeiture of personal property was less harsh than a forfeiture of real property, and a forfeiture of a vehicle worth more than the owner's had been previously upheld.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

People v. Holman


No. 2-08-0599


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


402 Ill. App. 3d 645; 937 N.E.2d 196; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 579; 344 Ill. Dec. 490



June 10, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: Released for Publication July 30, 2010.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Holman, 237 Ill. 2d 573, 938 N.E.2d 526, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1195, 345 Ill. Dec. 87 (2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Holman v. Dawson, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 41964 (N.D. Ill., Apr. 14, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 07-CF-3565. Honorable Christopher R. Stride, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Lake County, Illinois, defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, 720 ILCS 570/401(c)(2) (2006), a Class 1 felony. Defendant was sentenced under the habitual offender statute as a Class X offender, 730 ILCS 5/5-5-3(c)(8) (2006), and a fee for reimbursement of court-appointed counsel was imposed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another man were walking on a path when they were ordered to approach a squad car. The two men veered off the path into the bushes and then emerged and approached the officers. Cocaine was found in the bushes and on defendant's person. The court found that the amount of time that had passed and the proximity of defendant to the bushes rendered reasonable the inference that defendant possessed the cocaine. Defendant abandoned the drugs before he was seized. He was not seized until he returned to the path, approached the squad car, and submitted to the order. The allegedly unlawful seizure at the time of submission did not result in the recovery of any evidence. Thus, the arrest based on the drugs found during the perimeter search was proper, and the search incident to that arrest was valid. There was no error in preventing defense counsel from using a whiteboard as demonstrative evidence during cross-examination. Because defendant was sentenced as a Class X offender based on his criminal history, he was subject to a mandatory supervised release term of three years; his sentence of 14 years' imprisonment plus a three-year term of mandatory supervised release was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed except as to the reimbursement order, which it vacated and remanded for a hearing on defendant's ability to pay for the services of his court-appointed attorney.

Vill. of Ringwood v. Foster


No. 2-09-0473


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


405 Ill. App. 3d 61; 932 N.E.2d 461; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 592; 342 Ill. Dec. 334



June 9, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified July 13, 2010.

Released for Publication August 27, 2010.
Modified by, Rehearing denied by Vill. of Ringwood v. Foster, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 715 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., July 13, 2010)
Rehearing denied by Vill. of Ringwood v. Foster, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 900 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., July 13, 2010)
Appeal denied by Village of Ringwood v. Foster, 238 Ill. 2d 676, 942 N.E.2d 462, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1698, 347 Ill. Dec. 259 (2010)
Appeal after remand at Ringwood v. Foster, 2013 IL App (2d) 111221, 2013 Ill. App. LEXIS 61 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 07-MC-2. Honorable Michael J. Sullivan, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee village filed a complaint in the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), for authorization pursuant to § 11-31-1(a) of the Illinois Municipal Code, 65 ILCS 5/11-31-1(a) (2006), to demolish an apartment building that was owned by appellant property owner. The trial court issued an order authorizing the village to demolish the owner's building. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that the trial court erred in finding that the owner's building was dangerous and unsafe under the Illinois Municipal Code, because it erred in finding that the owner could not reasonably repair the building and because the village did not provide the notice which the Code required. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not err in concluding that the building was dangerous and unsafe under 65 ILCS 5/11-31-1(a). Further, the trial court did not err by consulting a village ordinance to set the Code's standard for determining whether repair to the building could not be reasonably accomplished. Furthermore, because the damage to the building exceeded the village ordinance's 50 percent standard, repairs were forbidden and thus not reasonable. However, the record did not reveal whether proper notice was given to any lienholders, as required by § 11-31-1(a), but the village did not dispute the owner's assertion that it was not. Therefore, vacation of the trial court's demolition order and remand for the trial court to make further determinations was necessary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated, and the matter was remanded for the trial court to determine whether there were any lienholders, and, if so, whether they were notified. If there was no deficiency in notification, the court could reenter its demolition order, but if there was inadequate notice to a lienholder, the court had to ensure proper notice and hear the lienholder's objections, if any, before entering (or declining to enter) a demolition order.

 

915 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Maxon v. Ottawa Publ. Co.


No. 3-08-0805


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


402 Ill. App. 3d 704; 929 N.E.2d 666; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 505; 341 Ill. Dec. 12; 38 Media L. Rep. 1953



June 1, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 8, 2010


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit La Salle County, Illinois. No. 08-MR-125. Honorable Eugene P. Daugherity Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a husband and his wife, appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of the 13th Judicial Circuit La Salle County, Illinois, which dismissed their amended petition for discovery pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 224 that sought disclosure from respondent publisher of identifying information concerning the persons responsible for certain comments posted on the publisher's web site, which petitioners alleged were defamatory.


OVERVIEW: Several online posts to an article on the publisher's web site stated that petitioners had bribed the town's planning commissioners. The trial court adopted a test known as the Dendrite-Cahill test, and found that petitioners had not satisfied the hypothetical summary judgment test because the literary and social context of the statements rendered them nonactionable opinions as a matter of law. The court disagreed and held that subjecting an Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 224 petition to the same level of scrutiny afforded the sufficiency of a complaint pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-615 would address any constitutional concerns arising from disclosing the identity of any potential defendant. Although certain types of anonymous speech were constitutionally protected, it was overly broad to assert that anonymous speech, in and of itself, warranted constitutional protection and anonymous Internet speakers did not enjoy a higher degree of protection from claims of defamation than the private individual who had a cause of action against him for defamation. Petitioners stated a cause of action for defamation sufficient to warrant the anonymous individuals to come forward and answer a complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for entry of an order granting the petition for disclosure pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 224.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), in proceedings under the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 ILCS 207/1 et seq. (2008), denied respondent detainee's request for discharge or immediate release from the care and custody of the state human services agency. The detainee appealed.

(2008) (Act), seeking to have him adjudicated a sexually violent person and committed to the care and custody of state human services agency. It also found that the disorder that the detainee had, "paraphilia NOS, nonconsent" met the requirements under the Act of being a valid disorder for which the detainee could be involuntarily committed, despite the fact that the disorder was not specifically named in a leading diagnostic manual, as the testimony of mental health expert witnesses identified is a valid disorder even if it was not named in that manual.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Forest Preserve Dist. of Du Page County v. First Nat'l Bank of Franklin Park


No. 2-08-0565


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


401 Ill. App. 3d 966; 930 N.E.2d 477; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 501; 341 Ill. Dec. 267



May 27, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 30, 2010
Rehearing denied by Forest Pres. Dist. v. First Nat'l Bank of Franklin Park, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 661 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., June 30, 2010)
Appeal granted by Forest Pres. Dist. v. First Nat'l Bank of Franklin Park, 238 Ill. 2d 650, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1605 (2010)
Appeal granted by Forest Pres. Dist. v. First Nat'l Bank of Franklin Park, 238 Ill. 2d 650, 942 N.E.2d 453, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1595, 347 Ill. Dec. 250 (2010)
Motion to strike denied by Forest Pres. Dist. v. First Nat'l Bank of Franklin Park, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1142 (Ill., Sept. 22, 2011)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Forest Preserve Dist. v. First Nat'l Bank (State ex rel. Madigan), 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1840 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 99-ED-54. Honorable Stephen J. Culliton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Du Page County Circuit Court (Illinois), in a condemnation case, granted summary judgment for plaintiff condemnor on whether the condemnor negotiated in good faith before suing and on a motion in limine to bar evidence. It then denied defendant condemnees' motion for a posttrial hearing to determine fair market value as of the time the jury set a "fair market value" figure, which was eight years after the action was filed. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: The condemnor decided to acquire some land that the condemnees had acquired years before. It notified the condemnees, offered to pay a certain sum, and gave the condemnees time to respond. The condemnees rejected the initial offer. The condemnor then filed a condemnation complaint. The trial court granted summary judgment to the condemnor on acting-in-good-faith and motion in limine issues. It declined the condemnees' request for a post-hearing valuation. After eight years passed from the filing of the case, the jury determined a "fair market value" figure, as of the date the condemnation case was filed. The appellate court found that (1) summary judgment was properly awarded to the condemnor on the good-faith and motion in limine issues, as the record showed it made an offer in-line with appraisal valuations and an annexation agreement would have barred further development of the land; and (2) a post-trial hearing should have been held on whether the substantial delay in rendering a verdict on the land's "fair market value" deprived the condemnees of Fifth Amendment just compensation, as use of a traditional "time-of-filing" valuation might be unconstitutional given the delay.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's granting of summary judgment in favor of the condemnor on the issue of whether it engaged in good-faith negotiations and the granting of its motion in limine. It vacated the jury's verdict setting forth the value of the property, which was subject to possible reinstatement by the trial court after a just compensation hearing. It also remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Harding


No. 1-07-2148


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


401 Ill. App. 3d 482; 929 N.E.2d 597; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 487; 340 Ill. Dec. 946



May 26, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 16, 2010.
Rehearing denied by People v. Harding, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 729 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 9, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 CR 14913. Honorable Kerry M. Kennedy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of three counts of child abduction and sentenced to six-year terms of imprisonment for each conviction, with two of the terms to be served consecutively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court improperly admitted evidence of his three convictions for attempted sexual assault because the evidence served only to demonstrate to the jury his propensity to commit crime. The court of appeals agreed. The prosecution's written motion for admission of defendant's prior crimes did not suggest similarities between those crimes and the alleged child abduction offense. Defendant's prior crimes involved attacks made by force upon adult women he followed from bars late at night. They offered no insight on his intentions in offering rides to elementary school girls from his car in broad daylight other than to show his propensity to commit sex crimes. Indeed, the prosecution's focus on defendant's propensity was demonstrated at trial by its reconsideration motion's invocation of his "sexually deviant background." Defendant's earlier crimes were not sufficiently similar to the child abduction charges to permit those crimes to establish his intent other than by demonstrating his propensity to commit sexual offenses. Therefore, the trial court committed reversible error in admitting the prior convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

People v. Sucic


No. 1-08-0371


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


401 Ill. App. 3d 492; 928 N.E.2d 1231; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 429; 340 Ill. Dec. 634



May 19, 2010, Decided 
May 19, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 29, 2010.
Rehearing denied by People v. Sucic, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 665 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 14, 2010)
Related proceeding at Zlatan v. Holder, 2010 U.S. App. LEXIS 15598 (7th Cir., July 28, 2010)
Appeal denied by People v. Sucic, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1269 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Garritt E. Howard, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after it found defendant guilty of cyberstalking, harassment through electronic communication, and stalking. It then sentences defendant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The alleged victim temporarily lived with defendant and also worked for him for a time. He became interested in marrying her, but she did not want to marry him. She quit working for him and found a new residence. He sent her multiple threatening e-mails, was seen loitering near her residence, and deflated her car's tires. He was then charged with stalking, cyberstalking, and harassment through electronic communication. After a bench trial, he was convicted of all three charges. The appellate court found that (1) the cyberstalking statute, 720 ILCS 5/12-7.5(a)(1) (2008), did not violate his First Amendment rights since it targeted knowing conduct occurring without lawful justification and, thus, was neither overbroad nor vague; (2) the cyberstalking and harassment through electronic communication convictions involved the same conduct, meaning they violated the one-act, one-crime rule and that the harassment conviction had to be vacated; (3) the State proved him guilty of cyberstalking and stalking beyond a reasonable doubt; and (4) the trial court made a proper inquiry into his pro se ineffective assistance of counsel claims before declining to appoint new counsel to pursue them.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction and sentences against defendant for cyberstalking and stalking. It also vacated defendant conviction and sentence for harassment through electronic communication.

A.B.A.T.E. of Ill., Inc. v. Giannoulias


NO. 4-09-0069


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


401 Ill. App. 3d 326; 929 N.E.2d 1188; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 498; 341 Ill. Dec. 109



May 3, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by A.B.A.T.E. of Ill., Inc. v. Giannoulias, 237 Ill. 2d 551, 938 N.E.2d 518, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1095, 345 Ill. Dec. 79 (2010)
Affirmed by A.B.A.T.E. of Ill. v. Quinn, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1825 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 06CH363. Honorable Leo J. Zappa, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Sangamon County, Illinois, granted the motion of defendants, state officials, for summary judgment and denied plaintiffs', non-profit corporation and member, motion to reconsider on their suit against the state officials barring the transfer of funds from a number of funds, including the Cycle Rider Safety Training Fund (CRST Fund), to the General Revenue Fund. The non-profit and member appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that because the monies in the CRST Fund were private, the legislature could not transfer the monies pursuant to the 2004 and 2005 budget implementations (BIMP) without violating the takings clauses of the Illinois and United States Constitutions. The appellate court noted that the collected and placed into the CRST Fund were fees charged by the State for the privilege of operating a motorcycle. They were not from the sale of a private corporation's assets with the proceeds being used, at the State's direction, to create a foundation or trust. Because there was no evidence that any private monies were transferred from the CRST Fund to the General Revenue Fund, plaintiffs could not show any private money was taken. The legislature had the authority to enact the 2004 and 2005 BIMPs that enabled the transfer of funds. The Illinois legislature, by enacting the 1992 amendments to the Cycle Rider Safety Training Act (Act), 625 ILCS 35/6 (1992), did not create an irrevocable trust and therefore had the authority to transfer funds. The legislative enactments showed that the legislature intended to authorize the transfer of CRST Fund monies into the General Revenue Fund.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Fitch v. McDermott, Will and Emery, LLP, 237 Ill. 2d 555, 938 N.E.2d 520, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1152, 345 Ill. Dec. 81 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 07-CH-108. Honorable Maureen P. McIntyre, Judge, Presiding.

The beneficiaries appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trust grantor hired the law firm to handle the trust grantor's estate plan. The law firm, with the accounting firm's help, prepared the trust grantor's trust and will. People v. Coleman


NO. 4-08-0682


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


399 Ill. App. 3d 1150; 927 N.E.2d 304; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 352; 339 Ill. Dec. 763



April 16, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Coleman, 2012 Ill. LEXIS 967 (Ill., May 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Vermilion County. No. 07CF249. Honorable Nancy S. Fahey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Sentence vacated; cause remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Vermilion County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of armed robbery with a firearm and armed violence. It then sentenced defendant to 15 years in prison on his conviction for armed violence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State charged defendant with, inter alia, armed robbery with a firearm and armed violence with a category I weapon predicated on the offense of robbery after he used a gun to rob a pizza delivery man. A jury found him guilty of armed robbery with a firearm and armed violence. The trial court sentenced him to 15 years in prison on his armed violence conviction. He alleged on appeal that (1) his trial counsel was ineffective for eliciting testimony from defendant about a prior juvenile conviction, and (2) the armed violence sentence violated the Illinois Constitution's proportionate penalties clause. The appellate court found that under 705 ILCS 405/5-150(1)(c) (2008), he could be impeached with a juvenile adjudication and, thus, his counsel prudently made the jury aware of it before the State did so. Next, it found his armed violence sentence, which had to be for at least 15 years due to 720 ILCS 5/18-2(b) (2006)'s mandatory enhancement for using a handgun, was harsher than the sentence for armed robbery with a firearm despite the offenses having identical elements. It thus concluded that the armed violence violated the proportionate penalties clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded his case to the trial court for resentencing.

Bartlow v. Shannon


NO. 5-10-0123


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


399 Ill. App. 3d 560; 927 N.E.2d 88; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 324; 339 Ill. Dec. 547



April 9, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion to publish granted, April 9, 2010.
Appeal denied by Bartlow v. Shannon, 237 Ill. 2d 552, 938 N.E.2d 518, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1362, 345 Ill. Dec. 79 (2010)
Appeal after remand at Bartlow v. Costigan, 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 695, 2012 IL App (5th) 110519 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Rule 23 order filed: March 24, 2010. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Franklin County. No. 10-CH-35. Honorable Robert W. Lewis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business owners filed an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendants, the director of the Department of Labor and the Illinois Attorney General. The Circuit Court of Franklin County (Illinois) denied plaintiffs' request for a temporary restraining order (TRO) preventing defendants from enforcing the Illinois Employee Classification Act, 820 ILCS 185/1 et seq., against them. Plaintiffs filed an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs claimed that the Act violated the Illinois Constitution and the United States Constitution and thus was unenforceable. The court first held that the issues plaintiffs raised were ripe for judicial decision under 735 ILCS 5/2-701(a) (2008). They were basically legal in nature, i.e., whether the Act was constitutionally valid, and a sufficient hardship existed to make judicial review appropriate. The court held that the trial court erred in denying the TRO request. Plaintiffs' procedural due process claim presented a fair question concerning plaintiffs' right to relief, since the Department's fact-finding investigations and enforcement sanctions under the Act appeared to fall outside the procedural protections normally afforded to persons subject to administrative investigations and administrative penalties. Plaintiffs alleged that immediate and irreparable harm to their business's relationships with its subcontractors would occur without a TRO, due to the threat of a $1.6 million penalty and the uncertainty of the pending investigations. Because of the potential harm to plaintiffs' businesses, they had an inadequate remedy at law. Thus, a TRO was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying plaintiffs' motion for a TRO. It remanded with directions for the trial court to enter a TRO enjoining the Department from enforcing the Act against the plaintiffs until the trial court could conduct a hearing on plaintiffs' motion for a preliminary injunction.

Vincent v. Alden-Park Strathmoor, Inc.


No. 2-09-0625


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


399 Ill. App. 3d 1102; 928 N.E.2d 115; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 306; 340 Ill. Dec. 396



April 7, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 28, 2010.
Appeal granted by Vincent v. Alden-Park Strathmoor, Inc., 237 Ill. 2d 592, 938 N.E.2d 531, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1396, 345 Ill. Dec. 92 (2010)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Vincent v. Alden-Park Strathmoor, Inc., 2011 Ill. LEXIS 451 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 07--L--448. Honorable J. Edward Prochaska, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal representative brought an action under the Survival Act, 755 ILCS 5/27-6 (2006), against defendant nursing home operator. The Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) granted defendant's motion to strike plaintiff's reservation of the right to request punitive damages on the basis that it did not survive the decedent's death. Plaintiff filed an interlocutory appeal, and the court was asked to answer a certified question.


OVERVIEW: The court, answering the certified question in the negative, held that common-law punitive damages were not available in a survival action brought under the Nursing Home Care Act ("Act"), 210 ILCS 45/1-101 et seq. (2006). There was no statutory basis for punitive damages. Case law reflected that the Act "authorized" punitive damages only in the sense that it did not preclude a plaintiff from pursuing other available causes of action in addition to those that were available under the Act. The legislative history of the repeal of the Act's treble damages provision clearly reflected that while the Act previously included an express provision for punitive damages, it no longer did. Furthermore, the Illinois Supreme Court had not created an equitable-considerations exception permitting recovery of punitive damages under the Survival Act. Even if such an exception existed, it did not apply here. The Act provided for a range of both civil and criminal penalties for violations thereof. Furthermore, it would be inappropriate for the court to conclude that equity required punitive damages availability in light of the legislature's repeal of the treble damages provision.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the negative. It remanded the cause for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.

Morawicz v. Hynes


No. 1-09-0316


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


401 Ill. App. 3d 142; 929 N.E.2d 544; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 309; 340 Ill. Dec. 893



April 7, 2010, Decided 
April 7, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 25, 2010. As Amended April 23, 2010.
Appeal denied by Morawicz v. Hynes, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1266 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. No. 07 L 6960. HONORABLE RONALD F. BARTKOWICZ, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an attorney and a party litigant, filed suit against defendants, the Illinois State Comptroller and Treasurer. Plaintiffs prevailed on their claim that funds were unlawfully transferred from the Lawyers Assistance Program (LAP) and the Mandatory Arbitration Fund (MAF) into the state's general revenue fund, but the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied a permanent injunction, interest, and attorney fees. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the Illinois Attorney General was not under a duty to withdraw as defendants' counsel. The Attorney General was deemed to have a conflict of interest only where she was interested as a private individual or was an actual party. Furthermore, plaintiffs had not shown that the Attorney General was under any legal obligation to provide or secure representation for any part of the judicial branch where, as here, no such entity was named as a party to the litigation. The trial court did not err in refusing to order that any interest accrued on the swept funds while in the general revenue fund be deposited with the LAP and MAF. Under 30 ILCS 105/4.1(a) (2006), interest on fees was to be deposited into the general revenue fund. Plaintiffs had not shown that the disposition of interest unduly infringed upon inherent judicial powers under Ill. Const. art. II, § 1 or unconstitutionally burdened access to the courts. Finally, expenses in civil litigation against the State was a subject matter in which the Court of Claims was given exclusive jurisdiction. Thus, the court lacked jurisdiction over plaintiffs' attorney fee claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

P&S Grain, LLC v. County of Williamson


NO. 5-09-0079


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


399 Ill. App. 3d 836; 926 N.E.2d 466; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 311; 339 Ill. Dec. 234



April 2, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by P&S Grain, LLC v. County of Williamson, 237 Ill. 2d 561, 938 N.E.2d 523, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1284, 345 Ill. Dec. 84 (2010)
Appeal after remand at P and S. Grain, LLC v. Williamson County, 2014 IL App (5th) 130507-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2110 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County. No. 08-CH-100. Honorable John Speroni, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Williamson County Circuit Court (Illinois) dismissed plaintiff companies' complaint seeking declaratory and injunctive relief, and a temporary restraining order, after they challenged a law allowing defendant county to impose a tax for school facility use, the validity of county ordinances imposing it that county, and the validity of defendant state agency's filing certificate regarding one ordinance. The companies appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Illinois legislature enacted the County School Facility Occupation Tax Law (School Facility Tax Law), 55 ILCS 5/5-1006.7 (Supp. 2007). The School Facility Tax Law allowed Illinois counties to impose a countywide retailers' occupation tax and a service occupation tax, the retail sales tax, at a rate of one percent, to be used exclusively for school facility purposes. Pursuant to the School Facility Tax Law, defendant Boards passed a similar resolution requesting that the county submit to the voters the question of imposing a one percent sales tax for school facility purposes. The county did so. The voters in an election voted for the county having the authority to impose the sales tax. The county passed ordinances that would allow for it to implement the tax. The companies claimed in an amended complaint that they were subject to the tax, which was unconstitutional as applied. The trial court granted a motion to dismiss the companies' amended complaint. The appellate court found that the companies had standing to challenge imposition of the tax, as they both alleged that they were retailers who were subject to the tax and, thus, that they were personally affected by it.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings.

S. Side Trust & Sav. Bank of Peoria v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus.


No. 1-09-0148


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


401 Ill. App. 3d 424; 927 N.E.2d 179; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 278; 339 Ill. Dec. 638



March 31, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 25, 2010.
Appeal denied by S. Side Trust & Sav. Bank of Peoria v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus., Ltd., 237 Ill. 2d 591, 938 N.E.2d 531, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1121, 345 Ill. Dec. 92 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2010)
Appeal denied by S. Side Trust & Sav. Bank of Peoria v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus., 237 Ill. 2d 591, 938 N.E.2d 531, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1278, 345 Ill. Dec. 92 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2010)
Appeal denied by S. Side Trust & Sav. Bank of Peoria v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus. Am., 237 Ill. 2d 591, 938 N.E.2d 531, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1291, 345 Ill. Dec. 92 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Dennis J. Burke, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and dismissed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), in plaintiff personal representative's action asserting strict product liability and negligence claims, regarding an airplane crash, against defendant manufacturers and sellers of a plane and its component parts, dismissed the product liability claims against the one seller. It then granted summary judgment to the manufacturers and sellers on all remaining claims. The personal representative appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two decedents were killed when a small plane owned and piloted by the one decedent crashed, allegedly because an inadequate fuel gauge led to propeller problems. It filed strict product liability and negligence claims against the manufacturer and seller of both the plane and its component parts. It also asserted breach of warranty claims against the one seller. The trial court dismissed the product liability claims against the one seller, and otherwise granted summary judgment to the manufacturers and sellers. The appellate court fond that it lacked jurisdiction to review the appeal of the personal representative about the ruling dismissing the product liability claims, as dismissal under 735 ILCS 5/2-621 (1994), the Illinois distributor statute, was not a final and appealable order given the possibility of further action in the trial court. It also held that genuine issues of material fact barred the summary judgment grant to the one seller on the negligence and breach of implied warranty claims. However, it found that the General Aviation Revitalization Act, with its 18-year statute of repose, protected the remaining manufacturers and sellers.


OUTCOME: The appellate court dismissed the personal representative's appeal from the trial court's judgment dismissing its strict liability counts against the one seller. Also, it reversed the trial court's summary judgment grant to the one seller on the personal representative's counts alleging negligence and breach of an implied warranty.

People v. 1998 Ford Explorer


Nos. 2-08-1024, 2-08-1025, 2-08-1027 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


399 Ill. App. 3d 99; 926 N.E.2d 999; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 264; 339 Ill. Dec. 524



March 31, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 14, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 08-MR-250. Honorable Michael J. Colwell, Judge, Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 08-MR-283. Honorable Michael J. Colwell, Judge, Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 08-MR-345. Honorable Michael J. Colwell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois), in three separate cases, rejected each appellant claimant's contentions that the property forfeiture provisions of the Criminal Code of 1961, 720 ILCS 5/36-1 et seq. (2008), were unconstitutional for not including a provision for a prompt "probable cause" hearing. It then ordered that the relevant vehicle in each case be forfeited. The claimants appealed and the appellate court consolidated the appeals.


OVERVIEW: In three separate cases, the county state's attorney filed a complaint for forfeiture and alleged that claimant's vehicle was subject to forfeiture. In each case, the claimant argued in the trial court that the property-forfeiture provisions of the Criminal Code of 1961, 720 ILCS 5/36-1 et seq. (2008), were unconstitutional because they did not include a provision for a prompt "probable cause" hearing. In each case, the trial court rejected the claimant's constitutional argument and ordered his vehicle forfeited. The appellate court first noted that the statute was presumed to be constitutional and the claimant in each case had the burden of overcoming that presumption. It then found that none of them was able to do so. It determined that the procedure accorded to the claimants in each case in the trial court comported with due process such that no additional procedures were required. The appellate court determined that the hearings complied with Barker for determining whether there was an undue delay and found that no such delay was shown. It then found that the law dictated that a forfeiture proceeding that met the Barker test satisfied due process.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Clark Invs., Inc. v. Airstream, Inc.


No. 3-09-0260


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


399 Ill. App. 3d 209; 926 N.E.2d 408; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 226; 339 Ill. Dec. 176


October 6, 2009, Assigned; November 17, 2009, Submitted 
March 23, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 30, 2010. Released for Publication May 12, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Iroquois County, Illinois. No. 06-L-17. Honorable Susan S. Tungate, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 21st Judicial Circuit Court, Iroquois County (Illinois), granted summary judgment to defendant recreational vehicle manufacturer after plaintiff recreational vehicle dealer filed suit against the manufacturer and alleged that the manufacturer violated the Illinois Motor Vehicle Franchise Act, 815 ILCS 710/1 et seq. (2008), in its business dealings with the dealer. The dealer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer and dealer entered into an agreement, the first contract, authorizing the dealer to sell one of the manufacturer's products. As the first contract was about to expire, the manufacturer sent the dealer a second contract. It did not define the dealer's sales territory, have an expiration date, or list sales goals. The dealer refused to sign it. The dealer entered into a new written contract, the third contract, with the manufacturer, which contained some similarities and some differences to the first contract. The manufacturer then located another dealer about 90 miles from the dealer's franchise location. The dealer claimed that the manufacturer's conduct violated the Illinois Motor Vehicle Franchise Act, 815 ILCS 710/1 et seq. (2008). The trial court, however, granted the manufacturer's summary judgment motion. The appellate court found that the manufacturer did not violate that statute because, (1) under 815 ILCS 710/4(e)(8) (2008), it did not have to give notice of the location of a new franchise because the new franchise was not within the relevant market area and (2) the manufacturer did not engage in any conduct prohibited by 815 ILCS 710/4(d)(6) (2008).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Jessica M. (In re Jessica M.)


No. 1-06-2007


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


399 Ill. App. 3d 730; 928 N.E.2d 511; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 217; 340 Ill. Dec. 512



March 19, 2010, Decided 
March 19, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 18, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Noreen M. Daly, Judge Presiding.
People v. Jessica M. (In re Jessica M.), 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 157 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Feb. 26, 2010)
People v. Jessica M. (In re Jessica M.), 385 Ill. App. 3d 894, 897 N.E.2d 810, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1009, 325 Ill. Dec. 271 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that adjudicated respondent juvenile delinquent on two counts of aggravated battery. The juvenile appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim and the juvenile scuffled. The juvenile then struck the victim such that the victim had to get stitches. The State charged the juvenile with two counts of aggravated battery, one count being based upon 720 ILCS 5/12-4(a) (2004), for causing great bodily harm, and the other count being based on 720 ILCS 5/12-4(b)(8) (2004), for causing harm to a victim on a public way. After a hearing, the trial court adjudicated her delinquent. It then sentenced her to five years of probation and ordered her to submit a DNA indexing sample. The appellate court found that (1) the State proved her delinquent beyond a reasonable doubt; (2) the juvenile did not lay a proper foundation for admission of testimony about the victim; (3) the one-act, one-crime rule applied to juvenile cases and, thus, she could only be found delinquent on one of the two aggravated battery charges, requiring a remand to determine which charge should be vacated; (4) her probation sentence could not extend beyond her 21st birthday; and (5) 730 ILCS 5/5-3-4 (2004), making it mandatory that she submit a DNA sample, was not facially unconstitutional under either the Fourth Amendment or Ill. Const. art. I, § 6.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment, but remanded the case to the trial court with directions to vacate one of the findings of delinquency, to correct the "Trial Order," and to modify the juvenile's probation to terminate on her 21st birthday, on a specified date.

Carpenter v. Exelon Enters. Co., LLC


No. 1-09-1222


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


399 Ill. App. 3d 330; 927 N.E.2d 768; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 212; 340 Ill. Dec. 29



March 18, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 18, 2010.
Appeal denied by Carpenter v. Exelon Enters. Co., LLC, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1231 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 08 L 006480. Honorable Brigid Mary McGrath, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) denied defendant majority shareholder's motion to dismiss plaintiff minority shareholders' amended complaint alleging in regard to a merger and sale transaction that the majority shareholders mistreated them and forced them to accept an inadequate payment for their shares. It then certified a question about whether the three-year limitations period of 815 ILCS 5/13(D) (2008) applied to the action.


OVERVIEW: The minority shareholders filed an amended complaint against the majority shareholder, and asserted breach of fiduciary duty and related claims against the majority shareholder stemming from the majority shareholder's alleged conduct during a merger and sale transaction. The minority shareholders claimed that they were mistreated and forced to sell their shares for inadequate value. Since the minority shareholders filed suit four years after the alleged misconduct, the majority shareholders claimed that their action was barred under the Illinois Securities Law's three-year limitations period set forth in 815 ILCS 5/13(D) (2008). The trial court disagreed and found that the lawsuit was governed by the residual five-year limitations period of 735 ILCS 5/13-205 (2008). The appellate court, on the trial court's certified question, found that 815 ILCS 5/13(D) (2008) did not apply to bar the minority shareholders' lawsuit against the majority shareholders. It so concluded because it found that 815 ILCS 5/13 (2008) did not concern retroactive common law damages claims for breach of fiduciary duty brought by sellers of securities in general, or minority shareholders in particular.


OUTCOME: The appellate court answered the trial court's certified question in the negative and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

March 5, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 9, 2010.
Appeal denied by Condo. Ass'n of Commonwealth Plaza v. City of Chi., 236 Ill. 2d 552, 932 N.E.2d 1029, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 945, 342 Ill. Dec. 568 (2010)

Plaintiff nearby property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: In one case, the hospitals applied with the city to request that the city council change the zoning classification of certain land around their campus to allow for implementation of an Institutional Planned Development. It then found that under Landmarks, that was not a valid reason for invalidating a home rule unit's ordinance.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

Fosler v. Midwest Care Ctr. II, Inc.


No. 2-08-1005


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


398 Ill. App. 3d 563; 928 N.E.2d 1; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 170; 340 Ill. Dec. 282



March 1, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 16, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 08-L-148. Honorable Ronald L. Pirrello, Judge, Presiding.
Fosler v. Midwest Care Ctr. II, Inc., 391 Ill. App. 3d 397, 911 N.E.2d 1003, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 269, 331 Ill. Dec. 773 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Winnebago County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that denied defendant nursing home operators' motion to enforce an arbitration provision after plaintiff nursing home resident sued them for relief under the Nursing Home Care Act, 210 ILCS 45/1-101 et seq. (2006), and for negligence for care she received during her stay at their long-term care facility. The operators appealed.


OVERVIEW: The resident sued the operators for relief under the Nursing Home Care Act, 210 ILCS 45/1-101 et seq. (2006) (Care Act), and for negligence for wrongful injuries she said she suffered while she was cared for at their long-term care facility. The operators answered her complaint and moved for enforcement of an arbitration provision contained in the written agreement that was signed so that she could become a resident at the facility. The trial court denied the motion to enforce. The appellate court found that the policy favoring arbitration set forth in the Federal Arbitration Act, 9 U.S.C.S. § 2 (FAA), was in direct conflict with provisions of the Care Act, namely, 210 ILCS 45/3-606 (2006) and 210 ILCS 45/3-607 (2006), that purported to nullify the arbitration provision in the nursing home admission agreement. It then found that pursuant to the supremacy clause contained in the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. art. VI, cl. 2, the FAA preempted the Care Act regarding the enforceability of the arbitration provision.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Hossfeld v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections


No. 1-09-3598


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


398 Ill. App. 3d 737; 924 N.E.2d 88; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 143; 338 Ill. Dec. 228



February 24, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 9, 2010.
Appeal granted by Hossfeld v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections, 236 Ill. 2d 504, 930 N.E.2d 408, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 398, 341 Ill. Dec. 198 (2010)
Affirmed by Hossfeld v. Ill. State Bd. of Elections, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1533 (Ill., Oct. 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 09 COEL 060. The Honorable Edward O'Brien, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner objected to the Republican candidacy of respondent candidate, who was running for state senator, on the ground that he had voted a Democratic ballot in a consolidated primary election. A tie vote of respondent Illinois Board of Elections resulted in the candidate's name remaining on the ballot. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied a petition for administrative review. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The candidate voted a Democratic ballot in a consolidated primary election and later voted in a general township election in April 2009. In October 2009, he filed his nomination papers as a Republican party candidate in the 2010 Republican primary. The court stated that restrictions on candidates' party-switching had not been held unconstitutional. 10 ILCS 5/8-8 (2006), however, no longer provided express time limitations on party-switching for candidates; the only remaining restriction was that the candidate had to be a qualified primary voter. Apart from the basic age and residency requirements contained therein, 10 ILCS 5/7-43 (2006) had very limited requirements for primary voting, including declaring party affiliation and refraining from participating in the opposing party's activities within 45 days of the primary. If § 7-43 was accorded with the other relevant restrictions on primary voting found in § 8-8, that a "qualified primary elector" of a party could not sign petitions or be a candidate of more than one party, then the candidate had declared affiliation and was a qualified primary voter of the Republican Party. Thus, his statement of candidacy was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the petition and confirmed the Board's decision that the candidate could remain on the primary ballot.

 

936 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Glorioso


No. 2-08-0271


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


398 Ill. App. 3d 975; 924 N.E.2d 1153; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 107; 338 Ill. Dec. 627



February 16, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 2, 2010.
Appeal denied by People v. Glorioso, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 821 (Ill., May 26, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 07-CF-888. Honorable Fred L. Foreman, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of a substance containing cocaine. The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) had denied his motion to suppress evidence seized during a search of his home on the ground that under the United States Supreme Court's decision in Hudson, the exclusionary rule did not apply. Defendant appealed. He argued that the evidence should be excluded under Ill. Const. art. I, § 6.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the search violated the knock-and-announce rule of U.S. Const. amend. IV. In Hudson, the United States Supreme Court had held that the federal exclusionary rule did not apply to violations of the knock-and-announce rule. Because the Illinois Supreme Court had with limited exceptions construed § 6 in "lockstep" with the United States Supreme Court's construction of the Fourth Amendment, the trial court declined to find that § 6 required suppression. The court stated that it would not expand the state exclusionary remedy beyond the federal one unless (1) the framers of the 1970 constitution intended the expansion; or (2) denying the expansion would be antithetical to state tradition and values as reflected by long-standing case precedent. Here, because the state exclusionary rule was a judicially created remedy, the language of § 6 did not show anything, and the framers had not discussed the exclusionary rule. Moreover, the narrow exception that the Illinois Supreme Court had carved to the lockstep doctrine involved legislation authorizing unconstitutional searches and did not support carving out another exception under the very different circumstances here.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Jablonski v. Ford Motor Co.


NO. 5-05-0723


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


398 Ill. App. 3d 222; 923 N.E.2d 347; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 65; 337 Ill. Dec. 788; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P18,370



February 1, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Jablonski v. Ford Motor Co., 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 1487 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., Feb. 25, 2010)
Appeal withdrawn by Jablonski v. Ford Motor Co., 236 Ill. 2d 555, 932 N.E.2d 1030, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 980, 342 Ill. Dec. 569 (2010)
Appeal granted by Jablonski v. Ford Motor Co., 236 Ill. 2d 555, 932 N.E.2d 1030, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 835, 342 Ill. Dec. 569 (2010)
Reversed by Jablonski v. Ford Motor Co., 955 N.E.2d 1138, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1136, 353 Ill. Dec. 327, 2011 IL 110096 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 03-L-2027. Honorable A. A. Matoesian, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Madison County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment awarding damages on a jury's verdict for plaintiffs, a wife and an estate representative, against defendant automobile manufacturer. Their case had been submitted to the jury alleging negligent-design and willful-and-wanton-conduct claims stemming from a car collision involving a vehicle designed and built by the automobile manufacturer. The automobile manufacturer appealed.


OVERVIEW: Another vehicle struck the rear-end of husband and wife's vehicle, causing their fuel tank to rupture and explode, and injuring the wife while fatally injuring the husband. At the subsequent trial, claims of negligent design and willful-and-wanton conduct against the automobile manufacturer were submitted to the jury. The jury returned a general verdict for them, and awarded both compensatory and punitive damages. The appellate court found that (1) the jury properly considered the negligent design claims, as evidence was admitted that aft-of-the-axle fuel tanks such as was on their vehicle were defective because they tended to rupture in rear-end collisions, causing postcollision fires, that the automobile manufacturer was long aware of that hazard, and that it was negligent in continuing to so design vehicles without at least guarding against the hazard or warning vehicle owners about it; (2) the jury was properly instructed; (3) not submitting the automobile manufacturer's special interrogatories to the jury was not error, as answers to them might still allow for the return of a general verdict; and (4) the evidence supported giving a jury instruction on punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

938 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Bhagwan Dass Jain v. Johnson


No. 2-09-0080


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


398 Ill. App. 3d 135; 922 N.E.2d 1188; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 45; 337 Ill. Dec. 611



January 20, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 5, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 08-AR-1012. Honorable John T. Elsner, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Du Page County Circuit Court (Illinois) dismissed plaintiff former client's legal malpractice case filed against defendant former lawyers. The case, dismissed for want of prosecution, was refiled under the Illinois saving statute, 735 ILCS 5/13-217 (2008), before the trial court agreed with the former lawyers that it should be dismissed as barred by the legal malpractice claims statute of repose, 735 ILCS 5/13-214.3(c) (2008). He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The former client filed a legal malpractice action against the former lawyers for legal malpractice for allegedly failed to file a lawsuit on the former client's behalf before the statute of limitations expired. The malpractice action itself was filed within the applicable statutes of limitations and repose in 735 ILCS 5/13-214.3 (2008). During the pendency of the case, however, both the statute of limitations and the statute of repose expired. Eventually, the malpractice case itself was dismissed for want of prosecution. Two months later, the former client refiled the case under the Illinois saving statute, 735 ILCS 5/13-217 (2008). The trial court, however, found that the refiled suit was barred by the six-year statute of repose for claims of legal malpractice, 735 ILCS 5/13-214.3(c) (2008). The appellate court found that the Illinois saving statute permitting the refiling of certain dismissed actions, such as those for want of prosecution, within one year of the dismissal created an exception to the statute of repose for legal malpractice actions, 735 ILCS 5/13-214.3 (2008) and, thus, the former client should have been allowed to maintain his refiled action.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Leavell v. Dep't of Natural Res.


CONSOLIDATED NO. 5-08-0298


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


397 Ill. App. 3d 937; 923 N.E.2d 829; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 43; 337 Ill. Dec. 978; 178 Oil & Gas Rep. 445



January 19, 2010, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion to publish granted, January 19, 2010.
Related proceeding at Leavell v. Ill. Dep't of Natural Res., 600 F.3d 798, 2010 U.S. App. LEXIS 7120 (7th Cir. Ill., 2010)
Appeal denied by Leavell v. Dep't of Natural Res., 2010 Ill. LEXIS 830 (Ill., May 26, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Rule 23 Order Filed: December 4, 2009. Appeal from the Circuit Court of White County. Nos. 01-MR-4, 02-MR-8, 04-MR-4, 04-MR-5, & 04-L-2. Honorable David K. Frankland, Judge, presiding.
Leavell v. Dep't of Natural Res. (In re Leavell), 343 Ill. App. 3d 303, 796 N.E.2d 623, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1074, 277 Ill. Dec. 537 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The White County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered judgments for defendant state natural resources agency in five separate cases filed in the trial court involving oil wells that had been operated by plaintiff oil well operator that were found to be abandoned in various administrative hearings. The operator in each case had challenged the sufficiency of the notice given regarding the abandoned wells. The operator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state natural resources agency filed five separate cases in the trial court involving oil wells operated by the operator. The trial court in each case agreed with administrative proceedings that found the wells had been abandoned. In each case, the operator then raised issues concerning the alleged lack of notice given to the operator regarding the hearings. The trial court eventually dismissed the operator's claims. The appellate court found that (1) the state natural resources agency's settlement offer in two cases was too indefinite to be enforced under contract law; (2) the trial court lost jurisdiction over one of the cases after entering a final judgment dismissing it with prejudice, which became an adjudication on the merits under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 273, and res judicata barred the operator from relitigating an alleged lack of notice involving a second well; (3) a finding that the operator received sufficient notice of the proceedings concerning two wells was not against the manifest weight of the evidence; and (4) a separate lawsuit was not sufficiently related to the current case such that the trial court was required to recuse itself under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 63(C).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

940 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kane


No. 3-08-1008


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


397 Ill. App. 3d 851; 924 N.E.2d 1120; 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 8; 338 Ill. Dec. 594


July 15, 2009, Assigned; September 3, 2009, Submitted 
January 11, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 26, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 08-CM-991. Honorable James E. Egan, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Kane, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1197 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., Dec. 7, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 12th Judicial Circuit Court, Will County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant had violated the Smoke Free Illinois Act, 410 ILCS 82/15 (2008). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police officers from the forum county's health department observed defendant smoking in a forum county tavern. Defendant was then issued a ticket that charged her with violating 410 ILCS 82/15 (2008), known as the Smoke Free Act, which banned smoking in specified places. Following a jury trial, she was found guilty of violating that law, and was ordered to pay a fine and submit to court supervision. Defendant claimed on appeal that the State could not prosecute alleged violations of the law through criminal proceedings in the trial court. The State claimed that the law did not contain ant language that specifically deprived the trial court of jurisdiction. The appellate court found that the legislature could divest trial courts of original jurisdiction by enacting a comprehensive statutory scheme if it explicitly did so in that scheme. It then found that due to the legislature's mention of the Department of Public Health and enforcing agencies in that law, the legislature had clearly signaled an intent that violations of the law were not to be handled through criminal proceedings in the trial courts, which meant defendant's conviction had to be reversed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Our Savior Evangelical Lutheran Church v. Saville


No. 2-08-0105


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


397 Ill. App. 3d 1003; 922 N.E.2d 1143; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1336; 337 Ill. Dec. 566



December 31, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 11, 2010.
Appeal denied by Our Savior Evangelical Lutheran Church v. Saville, 236 Ill. 2d 508, 930 N.E.2d 410, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 499, 341 Ill. Dec. 200 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 06-MR-99. Honorable Michael J. Colwell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Kane County Circuit (Illinois) entered a judgment for defendant city after plaintiff church filed a lawsuit to challenge the city's denial of the church's applications for a site plan review of its proposed new building addition, parking lot, and driveway or, in the alternative, a special use permit for the same improvements to the church's property. The church appealed.


OVERVIEW: The church applied for a site plan review of its proposed new building addition, parking lot, and driveway, or, alternatively, a special use permit for the same improvements. The city denied the applications. The church claimed that the denials were improper. The trial court ruled for the city. The appellate court found that the determination that noncomplying churches could not use the site plan review process, Aurora, Ill., Zoning Ordinance § 5.14, but should submit their application to the special use permit process was not irrational and did not discriminate based on religion. For that reason, the appellate court also concluded that not allowing the church to use the site review plan process did not impose a "substantial burden" on churches or their members in violation of the Illinois Religious Freedom Restoration Act, 775 ILCS 35/1 et seq. (2006). However, it also found that the law regarding special permit applications was amended while the case was pending on appeal and, thus, a remand was necessary under the amended law, 65 ILCS 5/11-13-25, to determine whether the city's denial of the special permit application violated the church's substantive due process rights.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision that the church could not use the site plan review process and that not allowing such use did not violate the Illinois Religious Freedom Restoration Act. It reversed the trial court's judgment affirming the city's denial of the special use permit and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Southside Trust & Sav. Bank of Peoria v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus.


No. 1-09-0148


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1324; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P18,352

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Dennis J. Burke, Judge Presiding.
Commerce Trust Co. v. Air 1st Aviation Cos., 366 Ill. App. 3d 135, 851 N.E.2d 131, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 383, 303 Ill. Dec. 233 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), in plaintiff personal representative's action against defendant manufacturers and sellers of a plane, and its component parts, asserting strict product liability and negligence claims regarding an airplane crash, dismissed the product liability claims against the one seller. It then granted summary judgment to the manufacturers and sellers on all remaining claims. The personal representative appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two decedents were killed when the small plane owned and piloted by one decedent crashed. The personal representative believed that the crash was caused by an inadequate fuel gauge leading to propeller problems. It asserted strict product liability and negligence claims against the manufacturers and sellers of both the plane and its component parts. It also asserted breach of warranty claims against one seller. The trial court dismissed the product liability claims against the one seller, and granted summary judgment to the defendants on the remaining claims. The appellate court found that it lacked jurisdiction to review the appeal of the personal representative about the ruling dismissing the product liability claims, as the dismissal pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-621 (2006) was not a final and appealable order since further action in the trial court under that statute was possible. It also found that genuine issues of material fact precluded a summary judgment grant to the one seller as to the negligence and breach of implied warranty claims. However, it found that the General Aviation Revitalization Act, with its 18-year statute of repose, protected the remaining defendants.


OUTCOME: The appellate court dismissed the personal representative's appeal from the trial court's order dismissing its strict liability counts against the one seller. It also reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the one seller on the personal representative's negligence and breach of implied warranty counts. Otherwise, it affirmed the rulings granting summary judgment.

Devon Bank v. Miller (In re County Collector)


No. 1-08-1737


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


397 Ill. App. 3d 535; 921 N.E.2d 462; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1321; 336 Ill. Dec. 848



December 29, 2009, Decided 
December 29, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 18, 2010.
Rehearing denied by In re Application, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 123 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Jan. 27, 2010)
Appeal denied by Devon Bank v. Miller (In re County Collector), 236 Ill. 2d 554, 932 N.E.2d 1030, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 788, 342 Ill. Dec. 569 (2010)
Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by County Treasurer & Ex-Officio County Collector v. Checkmate Acquisitions, Inc., 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 3073 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 02 CD 2234. Honorable Susan Fox-Gillis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner bank filed a petition under 735 ILCS 5/2-1401(f) (2006) against respondent purchaser to set aside a tax deed issued to respondent successful bidder. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied the bank's motion for summary judgment and granted the purchaser's cross-motion for summary judgment. The bank appealed. It argued that it never received notice of the sale under the Property Tax Code, 35 ILCS 200/1-1 et seq. (2006).


OVERVIEW: The court stated that the bidder had not made a diligent effort to ascertain the identity of the record owner of the lot. It had never consulted the actual public records to determine the name and address of the party entitled to notice; it had relied upon a tract index; and it did not use a correct legal description of the property. When numerous errors in the process of determining the identity of the record owner of the property resulted in a total lack of notice to the record owner, the record owner was entitled to relief from a tax deed under 35 ILCS 200/22-45(4) (2006). Moreover, this lack of notice was a violation of the bank's right to due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Further, this total lack of notice meant that the circuit court never acquired personal jurisdiction over the bank and that the tax deed was void. The purchaser was not a bona fide purchaser for value under § 2-1401(e). At the time he contracted to buy the property, the sellers did not have a legally recorded ownership interest, and a chain of title inquiry would have placed him on inquiry notice to investigate the tax deed proceeding, which would have disclosed numerous deficiencies.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment. It remanded the cause with directions for the trial court to set aside the tax deed.

People v. Stanley


1-08-1017


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


397 Ill. App. 3d 598; 921 N.E.2d 445; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1304; 336 Ill. Dec. 831



December 24, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 18, 2010.
Rehearing denied by People v. Stanley, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 124 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Jan. 20, 2010)
Appeal denied by People v. Stanley, 236 Ill. 2d 571, 932 N.E.2d 1036, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 763, 342 Ill. Dec. 575 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 07 CR 14926. The Honorable Victoria A. Stewart, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County, defendant was convicted of unlawful use of a weapon, defacing identification marks on a firearm, and aggravated unlawful use of a firearm. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State conceded that the evidence was insufficient to prove that the shotgun was modified. The court stated that the mens rea applicable to 720 ILCS 5/24-5(b) (2006) was knowledge. The knowledge required applied only to the possessory component of the offense. The State did not have to prove knowledge of the character of the firearm. Though the defacement bore upon the commission of the offense, it was not an element of the offense. Here, an officer's testimony that he saw defendant carrying the defaced shotgun and placing it inside the door of his home was sufficient to demonstrate his knowing possession of the firearm as well as its unlawful nature. Next, the State's identification testimony was sufficient to prove that defendant was the possessor of the firearm. The officer had a significant opportunity to view defendant and never lost sight of him. There was no lapse between the offense and the identification. Finally, even if defense counsel was ineffective for failing to lay the proper foundation for the admission of a clothing receipt from a jail, defendant had not shown prejudice. The contents of the receipt would have been cumulative of the testimony already offered.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction for possession of a modified shotgun. It affirmed the rest of the judgment.

People v. Hammond


NOS. 4-08-0651, 4-08-0652, 4-09-0214 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1310



December 21, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified by People v. Hammond, 397 Ill. App. 3d 342, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1388 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., Dec. 21, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. No. 06CF50. No. 05CF289. No. 07CF134. Honorable Jennifer H. Bauknecht, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 4-08-0651, Affirmed. No. 4-08-0652, Affirmed. No. 4-09-0214, Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Livingston County Circuit Court (Illinois) in three separate cases granted the motions to dismiss filed by the first defendant, second defendant, and third defendant and dismissed the State's respective petitions for revocation of probation. It did so based on defendants in each case having accepted and completed 730 ILCS 5/5-6-4(i) (2008) intermediate sanctions proposed by their probation officers. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: In three separate cases, the State petitioned for the revocation of probation. The first defendant, second defendant, and third defendant moved for dismissal of the respective revocation petitions based on 730 ILCS 5/5-6-4(i) (2008), which established the alternative of intermediate sanctions as a way of avoiding a potential revocation of probation. The trial court granted the respective dismissal motions because the first defendant, second defendant, and third defendant had accepted and completed the sanctions their probation officers had proposed. The State appealed in all three cases, which presented the same question: whether that statute violated the doctrine of separation of powers, Ill. Const. art. II, § 1, by unduly infringing on the executive branch or, more specifically, the State's Attorneys in their function of prosecuting probation violations. The appellate court found that the State had not rebutted the presumption that the statute was constitutional. It so held upon finding that granting or denying probation revocation in Illinois had long been a judicial function and the probation officer proposing the intermediate sanctions was a judicial officer.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment in each of the three cases at issue.
