People v. Wishard


NO. 4-08-0712


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


396 Ill. App. 3d 283; 919 N.E.2d 1118; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1264; 336 Ill. Dec. 193



December 15, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Wishard, 236 Ill. 2d 544, 930 N.E.2d 415, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 575, 341 Ill. Dec. 205 (2010)
Subsequent appeal at People v. Wishard, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1014, 2012 IL App (4th) 100950U (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 08CF359. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Champaign County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after defendant pleaded guilty to attempted residential burglary in violation of 720 ILCS 5/8-4(a), 19-3(a) (2006), aggravated battery in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-4(b)(18) (2006), and disarming a peace officer in violation of 720 ILCS 5/31-1a (2006). It then sentenced him. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with multiple offenses due to his attempt to break into a woman's residence and his unsuccessful attempt to take a police officer's weapon. He pled guilty to the offenses, including the offense of 720 ILCS 5/31-1a (2006), disarming a peace officer. On appeal, he argued that 720 ILCS 5/31-1a (2006) impermissibly included conduct constituting both the inchoate and completed offense. The appellate court first found that defendant normally would have been considered to forfeit the issue, Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d), for not raising it earlier. However, it also concluded that he could alternatively relief under the plain error doctrine since the general attempt statute, 720 ILCS 5/8-4(a) (2006), could not apply in place of 720 ILCS 5/31-1a (2006). It so determined because it found that 720 ILCS 5/31-1a (2006) contained a manifest legislative intent to exclude application of the general attempt statute through language of "takes or attempts to take." Accordingly, it also held that he could not show his counsel provided ineffective assistance for not raising the issue of whether the disarming statute could apply instead of the general attempt statute.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Kelly


No. 1-08-1728


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


397 Ill. App. 3d 232; 921 N.E.2d 333; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1245; 336 Ill. Dec. 719



December 11, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 29, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 02 CR 14952. Honorable Vincent Gaughan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), in a criminal case, sealed certain pretrial proceedings and records, and also issued a "Decorum Order" which restrained the speech of attorneys and witnesses. It then denied appellant media intervenors' emergency motion to obtain access to certain closed pretrial proceedings and records and to vacate the Decorum Order. The media intervenors appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a high-profile entertainer, was charged with having sex with a minor. Before jury selection, the trial court sealed certain pretrial proceedings and records, and, separately, issued a "Decorum Order," which restrained the speech of attorneys and witnesses. The sealed proceedings concerned mainly two topics: proposed questions for potential jurors, and a motion by the State requesting the trial court for permission to introduce evidence of defendant's other criminal acts. The media intervenors were allowed to intervene, but their motions for access to the closed proceedings and documents, and to vacate the "Decorum Order" were denied. Defendant was then acquitted. The media intervenors claimed violation of their First Amendment right to freedom of speech. The appellate court disagreed and found, inter alia, that (1) a petition to intervene was the proper way to seek relief; (2) appellate court jurisdiction under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 307 was proper to review the denial; (3) the public interest exception to the mootness doctrine applied; (4) the presumption of access did not apply to the pretrial proceedings and documents involved; and (5) the Decorum Order was proper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Gorga


No. 1-08-1470


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION

December 8, 2009, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A man waiting for a bus was pushed against a viaduct wall by the defendant and co-defendant, who then took money from the man's wallet and fled. A witness saw the robbery and alerted police, who arrested the defendant and co-defendant nearby. Following a bench trial, defendant was found guilty of robbery. The defendant claimed on appeal that the trial court should not have refused his request to represent himself and allowed an ineffective interpreter to participate. The appellate disagreed. It found that even assuming he made a knowing and intelligent self-representation request, his right to represent himself pursuant to the Sixth Amendment and Ill. Const. art. I, § 8 was not timely made because defendant's appointed counsel at the time of the request already had a long involvement with the case and defendant had already been found guilty. It also found that he forfeited the interpreter issue by not timely objecting. Although he requested Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(a) plain-error review, the appellate court determined such review would not be proper since the evidence was not closely balanced and any alleged errors by the interpreter did not affect the fairness of his trial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

950 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kane


No. 3-08-1008


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1197


July 15, 2009, Assigned; September 3, 2009, Submitted 
December 7, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at People v. Kane, 924 N.E.2d 1120, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 8 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., Jan. 11, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Illinois, defendant was convicted of violating § 15 of the Smoke Free Illinois Act (Act), 410 ILCS 82/15 (2008). Following the denial of her post trial motions, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, among other things, that the Act was not enforceable through criminal proceedings. The court agreed that the Act was not enforceable through criminal proceedings. Pursuant to the Act, 410 ILCS 82/40(c) (2008), defendant should have been given the opportunity to pay the fine without objection or to contest the citation in accordance with the Illinois Administrative Procedure Act, 5 ILCS 100/1-1 (2008). The citation and complaint given to defendant noted, "court appearance required" in the circuit court of Will County and contained no option to summarily pay the fine or contest the citation in accordance with the Administrative Procedure Act. These facts alone mandated reversal of defendant's conviction. In addition, the language of the Act made clear that the legislature intended that violations of the Act were enforced administratively. Therefore, the State could not enforce violations of the Act through criminal proceedings in the circuit courts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated defendant's conviction.

County of Kankakee v. Ill. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 3-04-0271 (Consolidated with Nos. 3-04-0285 and 3-04-0289)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


396 Ill. App. 3d 1000; 955 N.E.2d 1; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1185; 352 Ill. Dec. 825



December 4, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 26, 2010. Released for Publication January 28, 2010.
Released for Publication January 28, 2010.
Appeal denied by County of Kankakee v. Ill. Pollution Control Bd., 236 Ill. 2d 502, 930 N.E.2d 407, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 557, 341 Ill. Dec. 197 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Illinois Pollution Control Board. Docket Nos. PCB 04-33, PCB 04-34, PCB 04-35.
County of Kankakee v. Ill. Pollution Control Bd., 231 Ill. 2d 659, 902 N.E.2d 1077, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 640, 327 Ill. Dec. 691 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois Pollution Control Board confirmed the decision of city council of respondent city that granted respondent applicants' second request seeking local siting approval for a proposed landfill within the city. Petitioner objectors appealed, the matter was decided, and the state supreme court vacated the judgment in favor of the appellate court deciding the case based on factors as directed.


OVERVIEW: Following an unsuccessful request, the applicants filed a second request seeking local siting approval for a proposed landfill within the city. The city council eventually approved it. The objectors petitioned for review before the Board, which upheld the city council's decision. The objectors then appealed approval of the applicants' second request. The appellate court found that (1) applicants' first request during the prior year was disapproved for purposes of 415 ILCS 5/39.2(m) (2004) of the Illinois Environmental Protection Act (Act) when the Board reversed the city's council's decision on that earlier application on the grounds that the city council erred in finding the proposed landfill met the criterion in 415 ILCS 5/39.2(a)(ii) (2004) of the Act; (2) remand was not necessary to determine whether the subsequent request was substantially similar to their request from a year earlier because their later request failed to satisfy all of the criteria in 415 ILCS 5/39.2(a) (2004); and (3) the finding that the later application failed to satisfy all of the statutory criteria was dispositive because all of the statutory criteria had to be met for local siting approval.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the Board's judgment.

 

952 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Learn


No. 2-04-1169


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


396 Ill. App. 3d 891; 919 N.E.2d 1042; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1234; 336 Ill. Dec. 117



December 4, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 15, 2010.
Appeal denied by People v. Learn, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 518 (Ill., Mar. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. December 11, 2009. No. 04-CF-275. Honorable John T. Phillips, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Learn, 371 Ill. App. 3d 701, 863 N.E.2d 1173, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 221, 309 Ill. Dec. 276 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual abuse in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-16(c)(1)(i) (2002). The present court reversed the conviction and remanded the cause for a new trial. The Supreme Court of Illinois ordered the present court to reconsider the case.


OVERVIEW: The charges involved defendant's four-year-old niece. The court first held that the trial court erred in ruling that the niece was available and that she testified for purposes of 725 ILCS 5/115-10 (2002). She neither made accusations nor gave relevant and material testimony. The niece's inability to answer the single question about alleged abuse--to accuse defendant--led only to the State's ability to bring in other witnesses to testify about what the victim said to them at some other time. If a child did not testify at trial, § 115-10(b)(2)(B) still allowed the introduction of the child's nontestimonial out -of-court statement if there was corroborative evidence of the act which was the subject of the statement. Here, however, there was no corroborative evidence of any act alleged in the niece's statements. The only evidence was the various recitations of the niece's out-of-court statements. Next, one witness had not testified as to what the niece had said but as to what an officer serving as a translator told her the niece had said. In such a case, § 115-10(a)(2) required the State to present the testimony of the person who actually heard the niece's remarks--the translator.


OUTCOME: On reconsideration, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court. It remanded the case for a new trial.

 

953 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dabbs


No. 3-08-0709


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


396 Ill. App. 3d 622; 919 N.E.2d 501; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1236; 335 Ill. Dec. 782



December 2, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 7, 2010.
Appeal granted by People v. Dabbs, 236 Ill. 2d 516, 930 N.E.2d 411, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 315, 341 Ill. Dec. 201 (2010)
Affirmed by People v. Dabbs, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1555 (Ill., Nov. 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the Tenth Judicial Circuit Tazewell County, Illinois. No. 08-CF-244. Honorable Stephen Kouri, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Dabbs, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 997 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., Oct. 15, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 10th Judicial Circuit Court, Tazewell County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of domestic battery in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-3.2(a)(1) (2006) stemming from an altercation with his girlfriend. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with domestic battery in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-3.2(a)(1) (2006) regarding alleged violence against his girlfriend. At trial, his ex-wife was permitted to testify pursuant to 725 ILCS 5/115-7.4 (Supp. 2007), concerning the admission of evidence of prior acts of domestic abuse, that defendant had physically abused her prior to their marriage. The jury found him guilty. On appeal, he contended that 725 ILCS 5/115-7.4 (Supp. 2007) violated both his constitutional equal protection and due process rights. The appellate court disagreed. It determined that alleged domestic abusers did not constitute a suspect class and, thus, the statute to pass muster under an equal protection clause analysis only had to be rationally based. It found that the statute qualified because domestic abuse crimes often went unreported and such a statute helped to promote the prosecution of such crimes. It also found that the statute did not violate his due process rights because a trial court had to weigh the probative value of the prior acts evidence against its prejudicial effect as a means of excluding such evidence that was unfairly prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

954 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Robin C. (In re Robin C.)


No. 3-08-0690


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


395 Ill. App. 3d 958; 918 N.E.2d 1284; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1136; 335 Ill. Dec. 471


August 24, 2009, Assigned; October 14, 2009, Submitted 
November 20, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 08-MH-106. Honorable Katherine Gorman, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 10th Judicial Circuit Court, Peoria County (Illinois), entered judgments that committed respondent mental health patient to a mental health facility and authorized the facility's staff to administer psychotropic medication to the patient against her will. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: After police officers delivered the patient to a hospital following an incident where she became disruptive and physically abusive, a social worker completed a petition for involuntary admission. A doctor and a psychiatrist completed certificates stating that the patient was a mentally-ill person who presented a danger to herself or others. The psychiatrist also filed a petition for authority to administer involuntary medication. The trial court held commitment and medication hearings. After hearing from the psychiatrist, the trial court ordered the patient to be involuntarily committed to a mental health facility and medicated against her will. The appellate court found that the matter was moot because the involuntary admission was only for a limited time period which had passed. However, it found that the public interest and capable-of-repetition-yet-evading review exceptions to the mootness doctrine applied. It then found that the State conceded that it provided neither social investigation nor possible alternative placement reports required by 405 ILCS 5/3-810 (2006) to the trial court, and that such an error could not be considered harmless or forfeited.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgments.

 

955 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


First Am. Bank Corp. v. Henry (In re County Collector of Du Page Judgment for Taxes for the Year 1999)


No. 2-08-0927


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


397 Ill. App. 3d 301; 922 N.E.2d 372; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1111; 337 Ill. Dec. 249



November 17, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 3, 2009. Released for Publication December 17, 2009.
Rehearing denied by First Am. Bank Corp. v. Henry, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1376 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Dec. 17, 2009)
Appeal granted by First Am. Bank Corp. v. Gwen Herny (In re County Collector for Judgment for Taxes), 236 Ill. 2d 505, 930 N.E.2d 409, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 587, 341 Ill. Dec. 199 (2010)
Affirmed by First Am. Bank Corp. v. Henry, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 7 (Ill., Jan. 21, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 00-T-1. Honorable Thomas C. Dudgeon, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Du Page County Circuit Court (Illinois) granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, a county tax collector and county forest preserve district, after appellant taxpayers filed objections to certain taxes collected by the collector on behalf of the district. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed objections regarding certain annual taxes collected by the collector on behalf of the district, which was specifically for the district's levy for its annual contribution to the Illinois Municipal Retirement Fund. The taxpayers argued that the district had no authority to levy taxes in one fiscal year to pay for the district's fiscal year contribution during the next year to the Fund, because the district had not first passed any appropriation for that contribution. The trial court granted summary judgment to the collector and district. The appellate court found that the Illinois Pension Code, 40 ILCS 5/7-171(b)(1) (1998), authorized the assessment of such taxes to allow the district to make its contribution to the Illinois Municipal Retirement Fund, and nowhere in that statute was there a requirement that the district had to first pass an appropriation for the contribution before the assessment could be levied. It added that it did not have the power to read into that statute a requirement that did not exist.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

956 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Vernon


No. 2-07-1134


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


396 Ill. App. 3d 145; 919 N.E.2d 966; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1114; 336 Ill. Dec. 41



November 17, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 31, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 05-CV-1395. Honorable Charles D. Johnson and Victoria L. Martin, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of the misdemeanor offense of unlawful display of martial arts devices on Department of Natural Resources land. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant received a citation for the misdemeanor offense of unlawful display of martial arts devices on Department of Natural Resources land after a conservation police officer investigated a complaint at a park that defendant had several martial arts devices on park land. Defendant requested a jury trial. However, he was informed that he would be granted a bench trial. He represented himself and the trial court entered a judgment placing him on supervision. He appealed and was granted a new trial. He then filed a pro se motion to dismiss, which the trial court denied after a hearing. The trial court granted defendant a public defender and defendant signed a voluntary jury waiver. After the trial, the trial court found defendant guilty. The trial court then denied his motion for a new trial. Defendant appealed. The appellate court agreed with defendant's contention that the trial court violated Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 401(a) by failing to admonish defendant of his right to counsel before he represented himself on his motion to dismiss, and, thus, that he was deprived of his right to counsel at a critical stage of the proceedings. It therefore found him entitled to a new trial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated defendant's conviction and remand the case to the trial court to conduct a new trial, which would include giving defendant proper admonitions if necessary.

 

957 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Torski C. (In re Torski C.)


NO. 4-08-0952


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


395 Ill. App. 3d 1010; 918 N.E.2d 1218; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1116; 335 Ill. Dec. 405



November 17, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Torski C (In re Torski C.), 236 Ill. 2d 506, 930 N.E.2d 409, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 322, 341 Ill. Dec. 199 (2010)
Appeal dismissed by, As moot, Motion denied by People v. Torski C. (In re Torski C.), 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1904 (Ill., Sept. 15, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 08MH865. Honorable Esteban F. Sanchez, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sangamon County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment following a hearing that granted a petition for the emergency involuntary admission of respondent alleged mentally ill person and directed that he be hospitalized for no more than 90 days. The alleged mentally ill person appealed.


OVERVIEW: The alleged mentally ill person's mother petitioned for his emergency involuntary admission. The petition asserted that he was mentally ill, unable to understand his need for treatment, and reasonably expected to engage in 405 ILCS 5/1-119(3) (2008) "dangerous conduct." The trial court conducted a hearing, granted the petition, and ordered a limited hospitalization. The appellate court, after finding the case moot because the hospitalization had ended but reviewable under the public interest exception to mootness, held that the definition of "dangerous conduct" in 405 ILCS 5/1-104.5 (2008) was void for vagueness, as it did not provide a sufficient standard to justify the involuntary hospitalization of a mentally ill individual, particularly in the alleged mentally ill person's case where his conduct and beliefs might seem annoying, but where he reasonably appeared to present little threat of engaging in dangerous conduct. It also found that "dangerous conduct" as referenced in 405 ILCS 5/1-119(3) (2008), which presented the same vagueness problem, violated substantive due process guarantees since it could apply to harm that nevertheless did not justify an involuntary commitment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated as void the trial court's judgment temporarily committing the alleged mentally ill person to a mental-health institution.

Heupel v. Jenkins


No. 1-07-1338


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


395 Ill. App. 3d 689; 919 N.E.2d 378; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1080; 335 Ill. Dec. 659



November 10, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 23, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Heupel v. Jenkins, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 54 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Jan. 28, 2010)
Appeal denied by Heupel v. Jenkins, 236 Ill. 2d 553, 932 N.E.2d 1029, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 745, 342 Ill. Dec. 568 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 05 L 928. The Honorable Richard J. Elrod, Judge Presiding.
Heupel v. Jenkins, 379 Ill. App. 3d 893, 884 N.E.2d 1263, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 175, 319 Ill. Dec. 18 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2008)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment on a jury's verdict in a personal injury case that found defendant alleged tortfeasor not liable to plaintiff pedestrian after the alleged tortfeasor's vehicle collided with another person's vehicle in an intersection, spun out of control, and struck the pedestrian on a nearby sidewalk. The pedestrian appealed.


OVERVIEW: The pedestrian was walking on a sidewalk. Two cars, one driven by the alleged tortfeasor and one driven by another person collided in a nearby intersection. The alleged tortfeasor's vehicle then spun into the sidewalk, struck the pedestrian, and pinned her against a building, which resulted in her suffering extensive injuries. Prior to filing a lawsuit, the pedestrian reached a settlement agreement with the other person for the limit of that other person's insurance policy. The trial court then denied the alleged tortfeasors' motion to file a third party action against the other person. Following a trial, a jury returned a verdict in favor of the alleged tortfeasor. The appellate court found that the trial court should not have included the other person, a settling tortfeasor, on the verdict form because that person under 735 ILCS 5/2-1117 (2004) was not a defendant "sued by the plaintiff pursuant to the state supreme court's recent interpretation of that statute in Ready, and because the appellate court could not state for certain that the jury did not consider the other person's role in the accident in reaching its verdict, it found a new trial was warranted.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for it to conduct a new trial.

People v. Robert F. (In re Robert F.)


NO. 4-08-0810


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


396 Ill. App. 3d 304; 917 N.E.2d 1201; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1102; 335 Ill. Dec. 137



November 9, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 08MH765. Honorable Esteban F. Sanchez, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sangamon County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that found respondent mental illness patient that he was a person subject to involuntary admission and ordering him to be treated for his mental illness for a period not to exceed 90 days at a specified facility pursuant to an agreement for alternative treatment. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient had a long history of mental illness. Petitioner State filed a petition for involuntary admission, at a specific facility, pursuant to the Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Code, 405 ILCS 5/3-813 (2008). The same day that petition was filed, the State petitioned for alternative treatment, alleging that the patient's condition had recently improved; also provided was an agreement for alternative treatment, which the patient decided not to sign. The trial court then held a hearing on the involuntary admission petition. It found that the State had proved its position by clear and convincing evidence. It then noted that it was allowing the alternative treatment requested in the agreement. The appellate court found that although the case was technically moot since the 90-day involuntary admission period had passed, it involved a matter of public interest and should be reviewed. It also found that the involuntary admission judgment, pursuant to 405 ILCS 5/2-107.1 (2008), and the alternative treatment judgment, under 405 ILCS 5/3-801.5 (2008), could not stand because those proceedings were mutually exclusive and provided for different remedies.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the trial court's judgment as void for want of statutory authority.

 

960 of 2788 DOCUMENTS



Dubey v. Public Storage, Inc.


No. 1-09-0094


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


395 Ill. App. 3d 342; 918 N.E.2d 265; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1049; 335 Ill. Dec. 181



October 23, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 7, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Dubey v. Public Storage, Inc., 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1361 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Nov. 24, 2009)
Appeal denied by Dubey v. Public Storage, Inc., 2010 Ill. LEXIS 574 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 L 14696. The Honorable Allen S. Goldberg, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed as modified; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments awarding damages after defendant storage facility owners were found liable to plaintiff renter on claims for breach of contract, conversion, and a violation of the Illinois Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act, 815 ILCS 505/10a (2002), due to loss of her personal property from a storage unit. The owners appealed; she cross appealed for a compensatory damage increase.


OVERVIEW: The renter obtained a storage unit from the owners in return for her credit card being automatically billed. However, she was not told that her items were put in a rental unit already rented to another person. The owners sold the personal items stored in her unit when the person to whom the unit was rented fell behind in paying rent, and did not notify the renter, who had always timely paid rent. She sued the owners for breach of contract, conversion, and a violation of the Illinois Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act, 815 ILCS 505/10a (2002) (Act). A jury awarded her identical compensatory damages on the breach of contract and conversion claims. The trial court awarded her damages on claims under the Act. She was also awarded punitive damages on the conversion and Act claims, and attorney fees under the Act. The appellate court found that she could not receive compensatory damages for both breach of contract and conversion, since the claims were based on the same act. It also found the punitive damage award for conversion to be excessive and determined that the compensatory damage award for conversion had to be reexamined, but held the awards made under the Act.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment, but ordered that the jury's compensatory damage award be reduced, and directed that the case be remanded to the trial court for a new trial be held on both compensatory and punitive damages regarding the conversion claim.


 

961 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dabbs


No. 3-08-0709


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 997



October 15, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at People v. Dabbs, 919 N.E.2d 501, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1236, 335 Ill. Dec. 782 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., Dec. 2, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of the Tenth Judicial Circuit Tazewell County, Illinois. No. 08-CF-244. Honorable Stephen Kouri, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Tenth Judicial Circuit Court, Tazewell County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of domestic battery in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-3.2(a)(1) (2006) against his girlfriend. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with domestic battery in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-3.2(a)(1) (2006) against his girlfriend. At trial, his ex-wife testified that defendant had physically abused her prior to their marriage. The jury found defendant guilty. Defendant argued on appeal that 725 ILCS 5/115-7.4 (Supp. 2007), which allowed evidence of prior acts of domestic battery to be admissible in a domestic battery trial, was unconstitutional. The appellate court rejected his claim and affirmed upon finding that statutes were presumed to be constitutional and defendant did not meet his burden of showing that 725 ILCS 5/115-7.4 (Supp. 2007) was unconstitutional. It determined that as an alleged domestic abuser, defendant was not a member of a suspect class for equal protection purposes and, thus, the legislation allowing admission of prior bad acts only had to have a rational basis, which it did. It then found that for due process purposes, the statute contained sufficient procedural safeguards because the evidence could not be admitted unless it was both relevant and not unfairly prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

962 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Lamar Whiteco Outdoor Corp. v. City of W. Chicago


No. 2-08-0020


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


395 Ill. App. 3d 501; 916 N.E.2d 886; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 991; 334 Ill. Dec. 246



October 8, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 20, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 01-MR-907. Honorable Kenneth L. Popejoy, Judge, Presiding.
Lamar Whiteco Outdoor Corp. v. City of W. Chicago, 355 Ill. App. 3d 352, 823 N.E.2d 610, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 94, 291 Ill. Dec. 318 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee outdoor advertiser sued appellant city in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief regarding the enforcement of an advertising ordinance against the advertiser. The court barred the city from enforcing the ordinance against the advertiser and ruled that the advertiser was eligible for attorney fees and costs as a prevailing party under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city argued that the award of fees and costs was to be reversed because (1) the advertiser was not a prevailing party under the Civil Rights Act of 1991; (2) even if the advertiser was a prevailing party, any victory was de minimis; and (3) section 9-102 of the Illinois Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, 745 ILCS 10/9-102 (2006), did not prescribe attorney fees. On appeal, the court dismissed the appeal for lack of jurisdiction under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 301 and 303, on the ground that the order finding the advertiser eligible for fees was not appealable because it did not specify the amount of the award. The order denying the motion to reconsider would have been a final order only if the court had set an amount of the award rather than staying the ultimate determination until after the appeal. In addition, the trial court's finding that the order was final and appealable was insufficient to confer appellate jurisdiction under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 304(a). The inclusion of a Rule 304(a) finding in the order did not transform the nonfinal order into a final and appealable order.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.

 

963 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Snyder v. Heidelberger


No. 2-08-1061


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 964



October 6, 2009, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, Petition denied by, Opinion withdrawn by Snyder v. Heidelberger, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 821 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Aug. 12, 2010)
Substituted opinion at Snyder v. Heidelberger, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 882 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Aug. 12, 2010)
Rehearing denied by, Petition denied by, Substituted opinion at, Opinion withdrawn by Snyder v. Heidelberger, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 819 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Aug. 13, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 08-CH-802. Honorable Kenneth L. Popejoy, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff client's wife filed a legal malpractice action against defendant attorney, alleging that the attorney breached his duty of care to the wife, a third-party beneficiary of the professional relationship between the attorney and her husband, the client, and seeking imposition of a constructive trust. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) granted the attorney's motion to dismiss the duty of care claim. The wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The client hired the attorney to either change legal title to, or the beneficial interest in, the property on which the client and the wife lived. The attorney prepared a quitclaim deed that convey title from the client to the client and the wife in joint tenancy and recorded the deed. After the client died, the wife discovered that the property was held in trust and thus, the quitclaim deed conveyed nothing to the wife. On appeal, the wife contended that the dismissal was improper because 735 ILCS 5/13-214.3(d) (1994) excluded the case from the six-year statute of repose. The appellate court agreed. Because the wife did not suffer her injury until after the client died, § 13-214.3(b) of the statute of repose allowed her to file her action against the attorney within two years after the client's death. The appellate court found that the wife did so. Therefore, the trial court erred in holding that the statute of repose barred the duty of care claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

964 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


County of Du Page v. Lake St. Spa, Inc.


Nos. 2-08-1078, 2-08-1079, 2-08-1080 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


395 Ill. App. 3d 110; 916 N.E.2d 1240; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 965; 334 Ill. Dec. 352



October 2, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 20, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 03-CH-724. Honorable Kenneth L. Popejoy, Judge, Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 03-CH-1334. Honorable Kenneth L. Popejoy, Judge, Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. Nos. 99-CH-749, 99-OV-3111, 99-OV-3361. Honorable Bonnie M. Wheaton, Judge, Presiding.
Wright v. County of Du Page, 316 Ill. App. 3d 28, 736 N.E.2d 650, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 746, 249 Ill. Dec. 456 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The DuPage County Circuit Court (Illinois), where appellant adult businesses challenged appellee county's zoning codes regulating adult expression, granted the county's summary judgment motions alleging that whether a zoning ordinance left reasonable avenues for continued permitted expression should be determined from the ordinance's effective date rather than when a lawsuit challenging the ordinance was filed. The adult businesses appealed.


OVERVIEW: The adult businesses filed a challenge pursuant to the First Amendment against the county's zoning ordinances on the ground that the ordinances were impermissibly regulating adult expression. Whether a zoning ordinance left reasonable avenues for continued permitted expression by the businesses affected caused a subissue: whether the determination of whether sufficient sites for such expression remained had to be made at the time an ordinance was enacted or whether it should be made at the time such businesses filed a lawsuit to challenge an ordinance. The trial court granted the county's summary judgment motion alleging that the applicable time was at enactment. The appellate court found that whether sufficient sites existed had to be made at the time such a business filed a lawsuit attacking the validity of the ordinance, as the relevant consideration was the current effect of the ordinance on the business seeking to present such expression and not the situation occurring at the time that the local government enacted the ordinance to address the problem in the first place, which was more concerned with whether the ordinance addressed a substantial government interest.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial courts' judgments and remanded the cases to the trial courts for further proceedings.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois) denying his amended petition pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 (2006). The inmate had been convicted of murder and armed robbery, and sentenced to natural life imprisonment for murder and a concurrent 30 years for robbery. The inmate's motion to vacate a void sentencing order, recharacterized as a postconviction petition, was dismissed, an order reversed on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate contended that his petition stated a valid claim that his natural life sentence violated Apprendi. The appellate court found no error. The appellate court disagreed with defendant's claim that the prospective application of Apprendi, in and of itself, violated due process and equal protection.


OUTCOME: The order denying the inmate's petition was affirmed.

People v. Garmon


No. 1-07-2892


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. 06 CR 8853. The Honorable Marjorie Laws, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of theft. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with theft in violation of 720 ILCS 5/16-1(a)(5) (2006) for obtaining or exerting control over property in the custody of any law enforcement agency after defendant purchased several cell phones from undercover police. Defendant bought the phones over several months for sums far less than their indicated retail price. Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted. On appeal, he asserted that the evidence was insufficient to establish he had the crime's requisite knowledge and that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel. The appellate court found that even though testimony did not show that the term "stolen" was ever used during the transactions, the statute's requirement that an "explicit representation" be made that the property was stolen because unambiguous veiled references to stealing, such as police telling defendant that they nearly got caught taking the phones from a store, were made. It also found that defendant did not show he received ineffective assistance of counsel since most of what defendant objected to was defense counsel's choice of trial tactics, and defendant did not show that he had been prejudiced by counsel's conduct.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Commonwealth Edison Co. v. Ill. Commerce Comm'n

398 Ill. App. 3d 510; 924 N.E.2d 1065; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 913; 338 Ill. Dec. 539



September 17, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 6, 2010.
Appeal denied by Commonwealth Edison Co. v. Ill. Commerce Comm'n (Chicago Transit Auth.), 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1312 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2010)
Appeal denied by Commonwealth Edison Co. v. Ill. Commerce Comm'n, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1471 (Ill., Sept. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
On Petition for Administrative Review from the Illinois Commerce Commission. ICC Case No. 05-0597. On Petition for Administrative Review from the Illinois Commerce Commission. ICC Case No. 05-0597. On Petition for Administrative Review from the Illinois Commerce Commission. Case No. 05-0597. On Petition for Administrative Review from the Illinois Commerce Commission. Case No. 05-0597.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: These consolidated appeals arose out of a filing by a utility company of an action with the Illinois Commerce Commission in which the company sought to restructure and alter the rates it charged certain customers, including a building manager association and two railroads.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the benefits of the incentive plan to ratepayers in the sense that attracting good employees raised the level of service customers would receive was too remote to be included in the rate base under 220 ILCS 5/16-108(c). The company did not show a sufficient nexus between the earnings-per-share portion of the incentive compensation plan and a benefit to ratepayers. Discontinuance of the members of the association's rider that gave them a preferential rate for electricity used for space-heating purposes was not a termination of service under 220 ILCS 5/16-103(a), and was within the Commission's authority. The allowance for the recovery of the company's construction costs for new supply facilities and of the charges for reserving capacity within its distribution system did not violate the Contract Clauses, U.S. Const., art. I, § 10 and Ill. Const. art. I, § 16. A rider that allowed the company to recover costs associated with reserving capacity for the railroads' automatic load transfer systems did not violate the Illinois Public Utilities Act, 220 ILCS 5/1-101 et seq. (2004). 220 ILCS 5/16-129 did not limit the Commission's authority over utility rates.


OUTCOME: The order of the Commission was affirmed.

People v. Williams


No. 1-08-0487


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


394 Ill. App. 3d 286; 915 N.E.2d 815; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1086; 333 Ill. Dec. 744



September 15, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Williams, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1665 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Oct. 16, 2009)
Appeal denied by People v. Williams, 235 Ill. 2d 603, 924 N.E.2d 460, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 212, 338 Ill. Dec. 254 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 07 CR 17234. Honorable Victoria Stewart, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after it found defendant guilty of unlawful use of a weapon for possession of a sawed-off shotgun in violation of 720 ILCS 5/24-1(a)(7)(ii) (2006). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Following a bench trial, defendant was convicted of unlawful use of a weapon for possession of a sawed-off shotgun in violation of 720 ILCS 5/24-1(a)(7)(ii) (2006)). He then received a probationary sentence. He claimed on appeal that: (1) the State failed to prove him guilty of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt because the weapon recovered was in such disrepair that it was not a deadly weapon; and (2) the statute was unconstitutional as applied to him because it punished his innocent conduct. The appellate court found that unlike some other statutes regarding weapons, 720 ILCS 5/24-1(a)(7)(ii) (2006) did not contain an exception for broken down weapons in a non-functioning state, and, thus, it was within the trial court's province to determine whether the weapon was a deadly weapon under the statute. It also found that the statute was designed to protect the public from the inherent dangers of sawed-off shot guns and imposing a culpable mental state would defeat that purpose. As a result, it found that the statute, as applied to defendant, did not violate his due process rights because it was reasonably related to the goal of public safety and did not sweep too broadly.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Irwin Indus. Tool Co. v. Dep't of Revenue


Nos. 1-07-3331 & 08-0750


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


394 Ill. App. 3d 1002; 915 N.E.2d 789; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 893; 333 Ill. Dec. 718



September 11, 2009, Decided 
September 11, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Irwin Indus. Tool Co. v. Dep't of Revenue, 235 Ill. 2d 588, 924 N.E.2d 455, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 230, 338 Ill. Dec. 249 (2010)
Affirmed by Irwin Indus. Tool Co. v. Ill. Dep't of Revenue, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1065 (Ill., Sept. 23, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, County Department, Law Division. No. 04 L 50666. Honorable Alexander P. White, Judge Presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court, County Department Law Division (Illinois), where defendant state revenue department sought to tax plaintiff corporation's airplane based on its purchase price, granted summary judgment for the Department regarding the validity of the tax. However, it granted summary judgment to the corporation upon finding that only a limited "actual use" tax could be imposed. Both the Department and the corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the corporation purchased the aircraft partially for use in Illinois, the Department audited the purchase and determined that a use tax pursuant to the Use Tax Act, 35 ILCS 105/1 et seq. (Act), was due. As a result, it issued a notice of tax liability to the corporation that assessed use tax, penalties, and accrued interest. The corporation paid the amount allegedly owed and sued the Department. One of the corporation's claims was that the use tax was not validly imposed because the use did not have a "substantial nexus" with Illinois. It also asserted that even if the use tax was valid, the tax should not be on the airplane's purchase price, but according to the more limited "actual use" of the airplane in Illinois. The trial court granted summary judgment for the Department on the validity question, but granted summary judgment to the corporation on the claim for a limited tax. The appellate court found that the evidence showed that the use of the airplane had a "substantial nexus" with Illinois. However, it also found that an "actual use" limitation was not required because the Act allowed for apportionment via a credit provision in case a use tax was imposed elsewhere.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment to the extent that the trial court found that the use tax was validly imposed. It reversed the trial court's judgment to the extent that the trial court found that the use tax had to be limited to the actual usage of the airplane because a use tax did not have to be apportioned so long as a credit provision was in place.

Curtis v. Lofy


NO. 4-08-0750


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


394 Ill. App. 3d 170; 914 N.E.2d 248; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 872; 333 Ill. Dec. 41



September 2, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Curtis v. Philip G, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1682 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2009)
Appeal denied by Curtis v. Lofy, 235 Ill. 2d 586, 924 N.E.2d 454, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 266, 338 Ill. Dec. 248 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 06L140. Honorable Leslie J. Graves, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sangamon County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment in a case where plaintiff injured party sued defendants, a vehicle driver and a vehicle owner, after the injured party was struck by a vehicle operated by the vehicle driver, that denied the injured party's motion for substitution of a judge and that sanction her attorney. It also granted summary judgment to the vehicle driver. The injured party appealed those rulings.


OVERVIEW: The injured party sued a vehicle driver and his mother, the vehicle owner, for injuries she sustained when she was struck by a vehicle being operated by the vehicle driver. The trial court granted the vehicle owner's motion for summary judgment. Thereafter, the injured party voluntarily dismissed the suit. She then refiled her action. The trial court granted summary judgment to the vehicle owner and vehicle driver on res judicata grounds. It also sanctioned the injured party's counsel for not appearing at the hearing regarding the vehicle driver's motion. Furthermore, it denied the injured party's 735 ILCS 5/2-1001(a)(2) (2006) motion for substitution of judge. The appellate court found that denial of the motion for substitution was proper since there had already been a ruling on a substantial issue and that the injured party did not support her argument with citation to relevant authority about her counsel being sanctioned. However, it found that the 735 ILCS 5/2-1009(a) (2004) voluntary dismissal as to the vehicle owner was not a final and appealable ruling as to the vehicle driver, which meant he should not have been granted summary judgment on res judicata grounds.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the motion for substitution of judge and sanctioning the injured party's attorney. It reversed the trial court's judgment that granted summary judgment in favor of the vehicle driver. Too, it remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Mund v. Brown


NO. 5-08-0178


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


393 Ill. App. 3d 994; 913 N.E.2d 1225; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 795; 332 Ill. Dec. 935



August 21, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Mund v. Brown, 234 Ill. 2d 525, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 2180 (Ill., Nov. 25, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 05-L-83. Honorable Lloyd A. Cueto, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the order of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, Illinois, denying their motion to dismiss the present lawsuit with plaintiff pursuant to 735 ILCS 110/15 (Supp. 2007) of the Citizen Participation Act.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed a 23-count second amended complaint alleging, inter alia, abuse of process, malicious prosecution, and intentional infliction of emotional distress, arising from a lawsuit defendants previously filed against plaintiff in federal court. The instant appeal was from an order denying two motions to dismiss. The appellate court ruled that it did not have jurisdiction over the appeal. The denial of a motion to dismiss, of itself, was not a final and appealable order within the purview of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 307, as it was a mere interlocutory order, which did not give the appellate court jurisdiction on appeal. Also, 735 ILCS 110/20 (a) (Supp. 2007) would not confer jurisdiction on the appellate court in the absence of a final judgment, and to the extent the Citizen Participation Act attempted to provide for appeals from less than final judgments, it would be unconstitutional. Ill. Const. art. VI, § 6, granted the right to appeal from a final judgment only. A statute that claimed to give a right to an interlocutory appeal not covered by supreme court rules or to give the appellate court jurisdiction over that appeal would violate Ill. Const. art. VI, § 6.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

People v. Harris

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION

August 20, 2009, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 04 CR 30101. Hon. Joseph M. Claps, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, convicting him of false personation of an attorney under 720 ILCS 5/32-5 (2002) for rendering a trademark opinion while he knowingly lacked the authority to practice law, and sentencing him to one year of probation and 100 hours of community service.


OVERVIEW: In 2003, the client retained defendant's services as a patent attorney to provide a legal opinion on a trademark matter. Defendant, a law school graduate since 1974, replied to the letter with a three-page legal opinion on the trademark issue, listing himself in the opinion's letterhead as an attorney at law and patent attorney. Defendant collected $ 11,005.70 for this work. Defendant had been admitted to the patent bar until 1990, when his name was removed from the roster of registered patent attorneys and patent agents. The appellate court ruled that the State provided sufficient evidence to convict defendant of false personation of an attorney. A mere assertion by defendant that he was admitted to the bar in Texas or anywhere else was insufficient to require the State to prove he was not admitted in that jurisdiction. The State presented sufficient evidence to prove that defendant knowingly practiced law without authorization from the Michigan bar. Also, the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant knowingly practiced law without authority from the United States Patent and Trademark Office.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed plaintiff county residents' amended complaint seeking declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against defendants, a county and county representatives, to the effect of determining that a county ordinance banning assault weapons ban was unconstitutional. The county residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county residents sought relief claiming that county legislation known as the Blair Holt Assault Weapons Ban, Cook County, Ill., Ordinance No. 06-O-50 (2006) was unconstitutional. OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 12th Judicial Circuit Court, Will County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after defendant pled guilty to a misdemeanor charge of prostitution in violation of 720 ILCS 5/11-14(a) (2002). It then denied her motion to withdraw her plea and sentenced her to court supervision. Defendant appealed.

Too, it found that her equal protection rights were not violated since she was not similarly situated to clients under the statute and that she did not show she had an adequate ground for withdrawing her guilty plea.

Hubble v. Bi-State Dev. Agency


NO. 5-07-0661


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


393 Ill. App. 3d 1016; 915 N.E.2d 64; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 761; 333 Ill. Dec. 543



August 6, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hubble v. Bi-State Dev. Agency, 393 Ill. App. 3d 1016, 915 N.E.2d 64, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1663, 333 Ill. Dec. 543 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by Hubble v. Bi-State Dev. Agency of the Illinois-Missouri Metro. Dist., 238 Ill. 2d 262, 938 N.E.2d 483, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1066, 345 Ill. Dec. 44 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 07-L-118. Honorable Lloyd A. Cueto, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court (CC) of St. Clair County (Illinois) denied a motion by defendant interstate compact entity to dismiss a complaint filed against it by plaintiff driver, arising from a vehicle collision with a public bus. The CC certified a question regarding whether, inter alia, the entity was a "local public entity" as defined by the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, 745 ILCS 10/8-101 et seq. (2006).


OVERVIEW: The entity was responsible for operating mass transportation on both sides of the Mississippi River. The driver's vehicle was hit by a bus, and he filed suit, alleging that the bus driver's negligence caused the collision, and that the entity was vicariously liable. The entity sought dismissal based on 735 ILCS 5/2-619(5) (2006), and the CC denied it. It certified a question as to whether the agency was a local public entity under 745 ILCS 10/1-206 (2006), such that it was subject to the one-year statute of limitations of 745 ILCS 10/8-101(a) (2006). The court reviewed the nature of interstate compact entities, noting that authority for such an entity had to come from both states and be approved by Congress. It concluded that the legislature did not intend to include the entity within the Act's definition of a "local public entity." Accordingly, the one-year limitations period under § 8-101(a) did not apply to the driver's claim. The court noted that while it could not overrule the precedential decision of Grady, 151 Ill. App. 3d 749, it declined to follow it. The Transportation Cooperation Act, 5 ILCS 225/2 (2006), did not support inclusion of the entity within the definition.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the negative.

People v. Cotton


No. 1-06-3354


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


393 Ill. App. 3d 237; 913 N.E.2d 578; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 690; 332 Ill. Dec. 646



July 20, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 8, 2009.
Rehearing denied by People v. Cotton, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1674 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)
Appeal denied by People v. Cotton, 235 Ill. 2d 593, 924 N.E.2d 457, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 81, 338 Ill. Dec. 251 (2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Cotton v. Illinois, 131 S. Ct. 103, 178 L. Ed. 2d 64, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 6298 (U.S., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 03 CR 3262. Honorable Diane Gordon Cannon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for murder, attempted murder, and aggravated discharge of a firearm by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) as well as his sentences of 60 years for murder and 10 years for aggravated discharge of a firearm. He argued, inter alia, that a codefendant's testimony pursuant to a plea agreement denied him due process, and that the jury was improperly instructed on felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of shooting at a van full of people and killing one of them. The appellate court noted that codefendant, who was the driver of the vehicle defendant was riding in when he shot at the van, was offered the benefits of a plea agreement in exchange for his "truthful" testimony, not in exchange for his "consistent" testimony." In addition, codefendant was required to plead guilty to conspiracy and swear to the facts contained in the plea agreement. Thus, the admission of codefendant's testimony pursuant to a plea agreement did not deny defendant due process. There was no evidence that defendant fired at the van to kill the victim. Rather, he simply opened fire on the van and, as a result, the victim was shot. Defendant's felonious conduct had a purpose other than the killing of the victim. Thus, the trial court did not err in instructing the jury on felony murder. While defendant was deprived of his constitutional right to be present when the trial judge responded to the jury's note in his absence, he failed to establish that he was prejudiced by the error. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing the sentences.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The trial court was directed to correct the mittimus to reflect 1,397 days sentencing credit.

In re Marriage of O'Brien


No. 2-07-0264


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


393 Ill. App. 3d 364; 912 N.E.2d 729; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 654; 332 Ill. Dec. 242



July 14, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 21, 2009.
Rehearing denied by In re O'Brien, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 874 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Aug. 21, 2009)
Affirmed by In re Marriage of O'Brien, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 1110 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 03-D-2323. Honorable Joseph R. Waldeck and Christopher S. Starck, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois), in a divorce case, heard and denied petitioner former husband's motion for a substitution of judge. A different judge, the subject of the substitution motion, heard evidence about the parties' financial circumstances, and ordered him, inter alia, to make specified maintenance payments. He appealed the denial of the motion for a substitution of judge and maintenance rulings.


OVERVIEW: The former husband and former wife married and had two children. He was charged with domestic battery. The trial judge ruled that evidence she presented should be admitted. A different judge heard the case. He was found not guilty. When he sought a divorce, the case was assigned to the judge. Neither party objected. He later moved for substitution of a judge pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/2-1001(a)(3) (2004) and alleged that the judge had presided over the domestic battery case, that the judge knew her because she worked at the health club where he was a member, and that they had greeted each other during a few chance encounters. A different judge heard and denied the motion. The judge then awarded maintenance, and, in doing so, took into account that the former wife was the primary caretaker for the children, which allowed the former husband to earn a substantial salary. The judge also directed the former wife to obtain employment commensurate with her training and education. The appellate court found that the former husband did not establish that the judge was actually prejudiced against him and the award of maintenance was not an abuse of discretion given the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

979 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Michael H. (In re Michael H.)


NO. 5-07-0557


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


392 Ill. App. 3d 965; 912 N.E.2d 703; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 617; 332 Ill. Dec. 216



July 7, 2009, Decided 
July 7, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Michael H. (In re Michael H.), 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1687 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., July 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Randolph County. No. 07-MH-232. Honorable Richard A. Brown, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied; judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, a mentally impaired man, appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Randolph County (Illinois), which found him subject to involuntary admission, pursuant to the Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Code, 405 ILCS 5/1-100 et seq. (2006). Petitioner filed a petition for involuntary admission, alleging that respondent continued to be a person subject to involuntary admission pursuant, 405 ILCS 5/3-813(b) (2006).


OVERVIEW: Respondent had been residing at a mental health center after he was acquitted from attempting to escape from a group home. Petitioner asserted that respondent was a danger to himself and others and was unable to provide for his basic physical needs or protect himself from harm without help. Petitioner alleged that respondent was aggressive and often refused medication. Respondent had a long history of mental illness and he was placed in the custody of the State as an infant due to inadequate parental supervision. Of significance in the case was that respondent waived his right to a hearing on the petition to find him subject to involuntary admission. The court found error, concluding that the trial court's inquiry into respondent's capacity to make the waiver was woefully inadequate. The court further held that respondent, nor any other person subject to possible involuntary commitment, may not effectively waive the entire hearing on a petition for involuntary admission.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court finding respondent subject to involuntary admission.

 

980 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


No. 1-05-0810


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


393 Ill. App. 3d 77; 910 N.E.2d 1272; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 593; 331 Ill. Dec. 516



June 30, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 10, 2009.
Appeal granted by People v. Williams, 234 Ill. 2d 549, 920 N.E.2d 1080, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 2147, 336 Ill. Dec. 490 (2009)
Affirmed by People v. Williams, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1556 (Ill., Nov. 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 CR 26083. Honorable Daniel P. Darcy, Judge Presiding.
People v. Williams, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1135 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Nov. 19, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and codefendants were charged with violating the criminal drug conspiracy statute, 720 ILCS 570/405.1 (1998). Defendant was also charged with official misconduct, 720 ILCS 5/33-3(b) (1998). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted defendant a directed verdict on the criminal drug conspiracy count, but found defendant guilty of official misconduct and sentenced defendant to probation and community service. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State of Illinois accused defendant, a police department dispatcher, of notifying a codefendant about police activity near the codefendant's residence to facilitate illegal drug-dealing by the codefendant. Defendant contended that, assuming she disseminated confidential information, the State failed to prove that her acts violated a law as required by the official misconduct statute. The State maintained that it proved defendant guilty of official misconduct because she violated the rules and regulations of the police department by disseminating confidential information to the codefendant. On appeal, the court found that defendant was a public employee because (1) she was authorized to perform official functions (dispatched information for the police department); and (2) she was paid by a municipality of the State under 720 ILCS 5/2-17 (1998). However, the official misconduct statute required the State to prove that defendant violated a law. Instead, the State presented evidence that defendant violated the police department's rules and regulations, which were not laws. Therefore, defendant did not violate the official misconduct statute because defendant did not violate a law.


OUTCOME: The conviction for official misconduct was reversed, and a judgment of acquittal was entered.

 

981 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stroud


No. 1-05-0683


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


392 Ill. App. 3d 776; 911 N.E.2d 1152; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 594; 331 Ill. Dec. 922



June 30, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 10, 2009.
Appeal denied by People v. Stroud, 233 Ill. 2d 592, 919 N.E.2d 363, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1367, 335 Ill. Dec. 644 (Ill., Sept. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 CR 26083. Honorable Daniel P. Darcy, Judge Presiding.
People v. Stroud, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1134 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Nov. 19, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of criminal drug conspiracy under 720 ILCS 570/405.1 (2004) and delivery of more than 100 but less than 400 grams of cocaine, possession of more than 900 grams of cocaine with intent to deliver, and possession of 1 to 15 grams of cocaine with intent to deliver under 720 ILCS 570/401(a)(2)(D) (2004). The court sentenced defendant to terms of imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested following an undercover investigation into a suspected drug ring. Throughout the trial, the State of Illinois played tape-recorded conversations between an undercover police investigator and a drug dealer as well as surveillance videotapes of their interactions. The State also played tape-recorded conversations that were intercepted pursuant to electronic surveillance orders. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in issuing wiretap orders under 725 ILCS 5/108B-4(a)(3)(viii) (1998), or extensions of the wiretaps, because the affidavits appended in support of the application sufficiently demonstrated that other normal investigative procedures had been tried and had failed, appeared to be unlikely to succeed if tried, or were too dangerous to employ. Furthermore, the evidence was sufficient to support the criminal drug conspiracy conviction. Moreover, the stop and search of a vehicle without a warrant was not unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 6. However, defendant could not have been convicted of both criminal drug conspiracy and intent to deliver cocaine under 720 ILCS 5/8-5 (1998).


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence for criminal drug conspiracy were vacated, but the remaining convictions and sentences for possession with intent to deliver were affirmed. The clerk was directed to correct the mittimus.
