People v. Sharp


NO. 4-02-0913


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


391 Ill. App. 3d 947; 909 N.E.2d 971; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 545; 330 Ill. Dec. 949



June 26, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Sharp, 233 Ill. 2d 591, 919 N.E.2d 362, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1342, 335 Ill. Dec. 643 (Ill., Sept. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of DeWitt County. No. 02CF8. Honorable Stephen H. Peters, Judge Presiding.
People v. Sharp, 355 Ill. App. 3d 786, 825 N.E.2d 706, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 218, 292 Ill. Dec. 118 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child, pursuant to 720 ILCS 5/12-14.1(a)(1) (Supp. 2001). The Circuit Court of DeWitt County (Illinois) sentenced him to 20 years in prison. The appellate court affirmed. Defendant filed for leave to appeal. The Supreme Court of Illinois denied the petition but entered a supervisory order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that because 725 ILCS 5/115-10(b) (2002) created a hearsay exception that was not firmly rooted in the common law, the Confrontation Clause of the Sixth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VI, required that the victim's statements to her mother and a child advocacy worker possess particularized guarantees of trustworthiness. The appellate court concluded that the Confrontation Clause was not an issue under the circumstances of the instant action, because the victim "appeared" for cross-examination and answered defense counsel's questions. Defendant also argued that the admission of the subject statements was error because the statements were unreliable. While defendant forfeited the issue, the appellate court nonetheless rejected it on the merits, concluding that the victim's delay in reporting the incident did not render the statements inadmissible and the statements did not seemed coached. Finally, defendant argued that he was denied a fair trial based in improper comments made by the prosecutor. Even if the comments were improper, the error did not result in substantial prejudice to defendant, as the jury was instructed that closing arguments were not evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated its previous opinion and then affirmed defendant's conviction again.

 

983 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Willner


NO. 4-07-0926


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


392 Ill. App. 3d 121; 924 N.E.2d 1029; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 554; 338 Ill. Dec. 503



June 26, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Willner, 233 Ill. 2d 597, 919 N.E.2d 364, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1338, 335 Ill. Dec. 645 (Ill., Sept. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Adams County. No. 07CM319. Honorable Thomas J. Ortbal, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Adams County (Illinois), which convicted her of unlawful possession of pseudoephedrine in violation of § 20(b) of Methamphetamine Precursor Control Act, 720 ILCS 648/20(b) (2006). She argued that § 20(b) violated the due-process guarantee of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 because it was overbroad and criminalized the innocent act of purchasing products containing methamphetamine precursors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant knowingly purchased products containing more than 7,500 milligrams of pseudoephedrine within a 30-day period in violation of the Act. The appellate court held that the restrictions in § 20(b) represented a valid exercise of police power and did not violate the due-process clause of the Illinois Constitution. Section 20(b) bore a reasonable relationship to the State's interest in stopping the manufacture and distribution of methamphetamine. The legislature found that ephedrine or pseudoephedrine was the "essential ingredient," 720 ILCS 648/5 (2006), in methamphetamine. It could reasonably have determined that a link existed between individuals making repeated purchases of small quantities of products containing methamphetamine precursors over short periods of time and the manufacture and distribution of methamphetamine. Section 20(b) provided a reasonable means of limiting the amount of methamphetamine precursor available for diversion to the manufacture of methamphetamine. That diversion affected the public welfare. As a result, the legislature had the ability to use its police power to place limits on the purchase of products containing methamphetamine precursors.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

984 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kitch


NO. 4-05-0982


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


392 Ill. App. 3d 108; 915 N.E.2d 29; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 558; 333 Ill. Dec. 508



June 25, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 18, 2009.
Appeal granted by People v. Kitch, 233 Ill. 2d 581, 919 N.E.2d 360, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1381, 335 Ill. Dec. 641 (2009)
Affirmed by People v. Kitch, 2011 Ill. LEXIS 11 (Ill., Jan. 21, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Schuyler County. No. 05CF5. Honorable Alesia A. McMillen, Judge Presiding.
People v. Kitch, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 1353 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., Apr. 7, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of predatory sexual assault of a child and aggravated sexual abuse and was sentenced to nine consecutive life terms of imprisonment for the predatory sexual assault and a concurrent 14-year term for aggravated sexual abuse. The convictions were affirmed, and the life sentences were made concurrent. Defendant's petition for leave to appeal with the Illinois Supreme Court was denied.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court was directed to reconsider its decision in light of In re Rolandis G. The appellate court held that 725 ILCS 5/115-10 (2004) was not facially unconstitutional as a violation of the Confrontation Clause, U.S. Const., amend. VI and Ill. Const. art. I, § 8. The admission of an 11-year-old victim's hearsay statements under § 115-10 did not violate the Confrontation Clause. The victim testified consistently with her hearsay statements that defendant forced his penis into her mouth, between her legs, and into her vagina. On cross-examination, the victim answered all of the questions put to her by defense counsel. The victim appeared for cross-examination under Crawford and the Confrontation Clause. As the victim was present for cross-examination and answered defense counsel's questions, the Confrontation Clause did not constrain the use of the victim's prior statements. Life terms could not be served consecutively. Defendant forfeited his appeal as to the use of the age of the victim as an aggravating factor for aggravated criminal sexual abuse. Rolandis G. did not warrant a different result as it did not address when a declarant appeared for cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's earlier decision was vacated. After reconsideration, the conviction was affirmed as modified, and the case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to amend its sentencing order to reflect concurrent natural-life sentences for defendant's nine predatory sexual assault convictions. The State was granted its statutory assessment of $ 50 against defendant as costs of the appeal.

People v. Ligon


No. 1-07-1991


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


392 Ill. App. 3d 988; 910 N.E.2d 1252; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 531; 331 Ill. Dec. 496



June 24, 2009, Decided 
June 24, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 10, 2009.
Appeal granted by People v. Ligon, 233 Ill. 2d 582, 919 N.E.2d 360, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1394, 335 Ill. Dec. 641 (2009)
Affirmed by People v. Ligon, 239 Ill. 2d 94, 940 N.E.2d 1067, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1560, 346 Ill. Dec. 463 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable James M. Obbish, Judge Presiding.
People v. Ligon, 365 Ill. App. 3d 109, 847 N.E.2d 763, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 245, 301 Ill. Dec. 753 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, appellant inmate was found guilty of aggravated vehicular hijacking and sentenced to natural life in prison as an habitual offender. On direct appeal, the inmate's conviction and sentence were affirmed, but the appellate court declined to rule on his ineffectiveness of counsel claims. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) summarily dismissed the inmate's pro se postconviction petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On direct appeal, the inmate raised two claim of ineffective assistance by trial counsel, which the court found would be more appropriately decided in a postconviction proceeding. The inmate failed to raise those issues in his postconviction petition. On appeal, the inmate contended that the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the constitution required that he have legal counsel appointed to assist him in preparing his postconviction petition. The appellate court concluded that the inmate waived his ineffective assistance claims and that it did not have the authority to excuse that waiver. The appellate court further concluded that the inmate did not have a constitutional right to the assistance of counsel in preparing his postconviction petition. The appellate court disagreed with the inmate's claim that the appellate court effectively created a discretionary review process, requiring him to make a preliminary showing of merit before he could secure his first direct review of the ineffective assistance claims when it declined to consider them on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the inmate's petition for postconviction relief was affirmed.

Bernstein v. Dep't of Human Servs.


No. 1-07-3005


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


392 Ill. App. 3d 875; 910 N.E.2d 733; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 441; 331 Ill. Dec. 324



June 19, 2009, Decided 
June 19, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 27, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. County Department, Chancery Division. No. 06 CH 23280. Honorable Kathleen M. Pantle, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant legal guardian, on behalf of her son, filed suit against appellees, the Illinois Department of Human Services and a group home operator, in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for breach of contract, declaratory judgment, and injunctive relief. The court granted the Department's and the group home operator's motion to dismiss. The legal guardian appealed.


OVERVIEW: The legal guardian averred that her autistic and mentally retarded adult son lived in a group home, and, because of his disabilities, he engaged in self-injurious behavior. She further alleged that the one therapy that was successfully utilized to control this behavior was contingent electronic shock (CES). She therefore sought to require the group home operator to use CES therapy to treat her son. On appeal, the court found that (1) § 2-110 of the Illinois Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Code, 405 ILCS 5/2-110 (2006), was unconstitutional as it violated the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV; (2) § 15f of the Illinois Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities Administrative Act, 20 ILCS 1705/15f (2006), forbid electric shock treatment of mentally disabled individuals who suffered from behavioral challenges; (3) no substantive due process right under U.S. Const. amend. XIV or 405 ILCS 5/2-102(a) (2006) to adequate and humane care and services in the least restrictive environment was violated; (4) a settlement agreement did not require the continued use of CES; and (5) the separation of powers doctrine was not violated by the enactment of 20 ILCS 1705/15f.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court dismissing the complaint was affirmed.

People v. Bryant


NO. 4-05-1071


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


391 Ill. App. 3d 1072; 909 N.E.2d 391; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 543; 330 Ill. Dec. 678



June 17, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 1, 2009.
Appeal denied by People v. Bryant, 233 Ill. 2d 569, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1842 (Ill., Sept. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Coles County. No. 05CF141. Honorable Gary W. Jacobs, Judge Presiding.
People v. Bryant, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 1429 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., May 31, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of two counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child and sentenced him to consecutive nine-year prison terms on each count. On direct appeal, defendant's convictions were affirmed. The Supreme Court of Illinois denied defendant's petition for leave to appeal but also entered a nonprecedential supervisory order and remanded the case.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court first found that defendant forfeited his objection to the admission of the victim's testimony via closed-circuit television on the ground that the requirements of 725 ILCS 5/106B-5(a)(2) (2004) were not met, by failing to object on that ground. The appellate court also rejected defendant's challenge to the admission of the victims' statements under 725 ILCS 5/115-10 (2004), finding the statute constitutional and the Confrontation Clause not an issue. Among other things, the appellate court found that the victim "appeared" for cross-examination, in that she was present for cross-examination and answered defense counsel's questions. While the trial court erred in failing to give the jury an instruction regarding the statements admitted under § 115-10 with all of the other instructions, reversal was not required as the jury was provided such an instruction after the testimony of each of the three witnesses who testified about the victim's statements. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the decision in In re Rolandis G. did not warrant a different result, as that decision did not address the issue of whether the declarant "appeared" for cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated its earlier decision and then again affirmed defendant's convictions.

People v. Coleman


NO. 4-07-0921


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


391 Ill. App. 3d 963; 909 N.E.2d 952; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 552; 330 Ill. Dec. 930



June 17, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Coleman, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1693 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., July 16, 2009)
Appeal denied by People v. Coleman, 234 Ill. 2d 530, 920 N.E.2d 1075, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1995, 336 Ill. Dec. 485 (2009)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Seventeen Thousand Five Hundred Thirty-Two Dollars ($17,532) in United States Currency v. Coleman, 2011 IL App (4th) 100894-U, 2011 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 2070 (2011)
Post-conviction relief granted at, Remanded by People v. Coleman, 2012 IL App (4th) 110463, 981 N.E.2d 1178, 2012 Ill. App. LEXIS 1043, 367 Ill. Dec. 450 (2012)
Post-conviction relief granted at, Remanded by People v. Coleman, 2015 IL App (4th) 131045, 2015 Ill. App. LEXIS 8 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 06CF448. Honorable Katherine M. McCarthy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part as modified and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Macon County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver it, unlawful delivery of a controlled substance, and criminal drug conspiracy. The trial court then imposed sentence, with particular credits, and certain fines. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant brought cocaine to a female acquaintance's residence. The same day, police raided it. The acquaintance testified about his role in supplying cocaine to a second dealer. A jury found defendant guilty of, inter alia, unlawful delivery of a controlled substance in violation of 720 ILCS 570/401(a)(2)(D) (2006). Defendant was sentenced and fined. The appellate court found that (1) defendant stipulated to an adequate chain of custody of the cocaine; (2) his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel regarding the stipulation was better suited to postconviction proceedings; (3) any waiver of defendant's presence while notes from the deliberating jury were discussed was harmless; (4) he could not be convicted of an inchoate offense, conspiracy, and the principal offense, unlawful delivery, but only of unlawful delivery; (5) he could not be found guilty of a greater offense, unlawful delivery, and a lesser offense, unlawful possession with intent to deliver, but only of unlawful delivery; and (6) he could be fined under separate statutes, one mandatory and one discretionary, but was entitled to a presentence credit and a credit on a mandatory drug treatment assessment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the convictions and sentences for unlawful possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver and criminal drug conspiracy. It modified the judgment of conviction to allow eight additional presentence credit days and a $ 40 drug-treatment assessment credit. It also remanded the case to the trial court to amend the sentencing order as directed and otherwise affirmed the judgment of conviction.

 

989 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Winningham


NO. 4-08-0572


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


391 Ill. App. 3d 476; 909 N.E.2d 363; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 364; 330 Ill. Dec. 650



June 5, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 07CF1061. Honorable Robert J. Eggers, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated driving under the influence of alcohol (aggravated DUI) under 625 ILCS 5/11-501(d)(1)(F) (2006). Following a sentencing hearing, the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to three years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the statutory sentencing provision requiring a trial court to find "extraordinary circumstances" existed before it could impose a sentence of probation was unconstitutionally vague on its face and because it was subject to arbitrary and discriminatory application. The appellate court disagreed, concluding that the uncertainty of when probation could be imposed did not render the statute unconstitutionally vague on its face. The fact that the legislature did not specifically delineate the exact circumstances that constitute an "extraordinary circumstance," but rather left such a determination to a trial court's sound discretion, did not render 625 ILCS 5/11-501(d)(2) (2006) of the Illinois Vehicle Code unconstitutionally vague. Defendant also argued that even assuming the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, the trial court nonetheless abused its discretion by failing to find extraordinary circumstances existed. Essentially, defendant argued that because he did not receive probation, the sentence imposed by the trial court was excessive. The appellate court disagreed, finding no abuse of discretion and that the sentence imposed was entirely reasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The State was awarded a $ 50 statutory assessment against defendant as costs of the appeal.

State Bldg. Venture v. O'Donnell


No. 1-08-2714


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


391 Ill. App. 3d 554; 909 N.E.2d 894; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 290; 330 Ill. Dec. 872



May 26, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 23, 2009. Released for Publication July 7, 2009.
Appeal granted by State Bldg. Venture v. O'Donnell, 234 Ill. 2d 552, 920 N.E.2d 1081, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 2087, 336 Ill. Dec. 491 (2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by State Bldg. Venture v. O'Donnell, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1554 (Ill., Nov. 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 07 CH 21547. Honorable Mary Anne Mason, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Acting Director of the Illinois Department of Central Management Services appealed an order entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied its motion to dismiss plaintiff tenant's declaratory judgment count seeking an interpretation of 20 ILCS 405/405-315(a) (2006), and granting the tenant's motion for judgment on the pleadings.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the prayer for relief did not transform the claim from a statutory interpretation claim into a contract dispute. The tenant's claim was a claim for prospective relief and was not barred by sovereign immunity. Because the interpretation of the statute was never litigated in a prior case, it was not barred by collateral estoppel. There was an actual controversy between the parties. A ruling as to the interpretation of the statute would resolve any uncertainty regarding the duration of the tenant's leasehold, the future marketability of the leasehold, and any mortgage financing issues. The tenant's complaint sought a declaration of the parties' rights pursuant to the enabling statute, which was a law, not a recommendation. The claim was ripe. Finally, the trial court properly interpreted the statute. The Director could exercise her discretion to enter into the lease only at its inception, not at every renewal period.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Leonard


No. 3-07-0780


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


391 Ill. App. 3d 926; 911 N.E.2d 403; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 520; 331 Ill. Dec. 582



May 26, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 27, 2009.
Appeal denied by People v. Leonard, 233 Ill. 2d 582, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1678 (Ill., Sept. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 14th Judicial Circuit, Rock Island County, Illinois. No. 06-CF-313. Honorable Walter D. Braud, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for the 14th Judicial Circuit, Rock Island County (Illinois), which convicted him of the offenses of habitual armed criminal and unlawful possession of a weapon by a felon, in violation of 720 ILCS 5/24-1.7(a) and 24-1.1(a) (2006), following a jury trial. Defendant was sentenced to concurrent terms of imprisonment of 30 years and 10 years, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from the police obtaining a search warrant following a statement from a jail informant that defendant had an illegal firearm hidden under a couch at a certain residence, which was discovered. On appeal, defendant asserted that his conviction for the offense of armed habitual criminal was violative of the prohibition against ex post facto laws. The court disagreed and held that the armed habitual criminal statute was not violative of the constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto laws as the statute did not punish defendant for the offenses he committed before the statute creating the offense was enacted. Rather, defendant was convicted for the separate offense of possessing a firearm after having been convicted of three of the statute's enumerated offenses. Thus, his prior convictions were only an element of the offense and he was not punished for acts that occurred prior to the statute's effective date but for the new act of possessing a firearm. The court found no abuse of the trial court's discretion in allowing the State to declare the jail informant a hostile witness since he could not remember his prior statement and was uncooperative.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Cowart


No. 1-07-0053


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1724



May 13, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 94 CR 29080, 94 CR 25257, 94 CR 25258, 94 CR 25259, 94 CR 25260, 94 CR 25261, 94 CR 28843, 94 CR 28844. Honorable Lon William Shultz Judge Presiding.
People v. Cowart, 389 Ill. App. 3d 1046, 907 N.E.2d 1, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 47, 329 Ill. Dec. 682 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded; sentences modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, dismissing his petition under the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 ILCS 5/122-1 (2004).


OVERVIEW: The circuit court erred by dismissing appellant's petition under the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 ILCS 5/122-1, because four of his sentences for home invasion exceeded the statutory maximum and were void. Appellant also asserted a claim of constitutional deprivation based on a double jeopardy violation caused by a second home invasion conviction for a single break-in. Appellant did not forfeit his claim regarding the violation of the one-act one-crime principle by failing to raise it in a direct appeal. The summary remand for noncompliance with the attorney certification requirement of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d) had the same effect as the filing of no appeal at all. Accordingly, the petition was neither frivolous nor patently without merit.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of appellant's post-conviction petition was reversed, and the case was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings. The appellate court reduced four of appellant's sentences to the statutorily authorized maximum for his offenses.

Fosler v. Midwest Care Ctr. II, Inc.


No. 2-08-1005


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


391 Ill. App. 3d 397; 911 N.E.2d 1003; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 269; 331 Ill. Dec. 773



May 8, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 19, 2009.
Petition dismissed by, Dismissed without prejudice by Fosler v. Midwest Care Ctr. II, Inc., 233 Ill. 2d 555, 919 N.E.2d 352, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1681, 335 Ill. Dec. 633 (2009)
Rehearing denied by Fosler v. Midwest Care Ctr. II, Inc., 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 158 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Mar. 1, 2010)
Modified and rehearing denied by, Supplemented by Fosler v. Midwest Care Ctr. II, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 170 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Mar. 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 08-L-148. Honorable Ronald L. Pirrello, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee former patient sued appellants, a nursing home and others, alleging violations of the Nursing Home Care Act (210 ILCS 45/1-101 et seq. (2006)) and for negligence. Appellants challenged a ruling by the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) that denied their motion to enforce an arbitration clause that required that disputes be resolved through arbitration, as governed by the Federal Arbitration Act (FAA) (9 U.S.C.S. § 1 et seq.).


OVERVIEW: The parties agreed that § 2 of the FAA and 210 ILCS 45/3-606 and 3-607 of the Nursing Home Care Act were unambiguous and that, absent preemption, the Nursing Home Care Act governed the admission agreement and the resident's stay at the home. The court followed the holding in Perry and rejected Carter, finding that there were only two limitations on the enforceability of arbitration provisions governed by the FAA: (1) they had to be part of a written maritime contract or (2) a contract evidencing a transaction involving commerce, and such clauses were revocable on grounds as existed at law or in equity for the revocation of any contract. There was nothing in the FAA to indicate that the broad principle of enforceability of arbitration clauses was subject to any additional limitations under state law; 710 ILCS 5/2(a) (2002) favored arbitration as a means of resolving disputes. The court found that the resident forfeited the issue of whether the nursing home admission agreement was a contract evidencing a transaction involving commerce and held that the judicial forum provisions of §§ 3-606 and 3-607 were not grounds as existed at law or in equity for the revocation of any contract.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying appellants' motion to dismiss and remanded the case for proceedings consistent with this opinion.

Turnipseed v. Brown


No. 1-08-2571


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


391 Ill. App. 3d 88; 908 N.E.2d 546; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 257; 330 Ill. Dec. 358



May 4, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 22, 2009.
Appeal denied by Turnipseed v. Brown, 233 Ill. 2d 601, 919 N.E.2d 366, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1623, 335 Ill. Dec. 647 (2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Turnipseed v. Brown, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 3380 (U.S., Apr. 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 04 CH 17172. Honorable Kathleen M. Pantle, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that granted the motion of plaintiff bail bond interest claimants for class certification and denied the motion to dismiss filed by defendants, a circuit clerk and a county, after the claimants sought payment of interest on returned bail bond funds. The appellate court granted the petition for leave to appeal the circuit clerk and county filed regarding the grant of class certification.


OVERVIEW: The claimants sought to recover the interest that accrued on money that they deposited with circuit clerk, in connection with bail bonds that they executed. In addition to suing the circuit clerk, they also sued the county. The trial court granted the claimants' motion for class certification and denied the circuit clerk and county's motion to dismiss asserting that the claimants had not stated a cause of action. The appellate court granted the circuit clerk and county's petition for leave to appeal the grant of class certification. The appellate court then found that the claimants could not meet the threshold requirement of showing that they stated a cause of action, making moot a ruling on whether class certification was properly granted. The appellate court found that the statute regarding the return of bail bond funds, 725 ILCS 5/110-7(f) (2006), did not say anything about paying interest. Too, though the claimants asserted that the statute was facially unconstitutional for taking property without just compensation, no taking occurred because the amounts at issued were paid to secure the release of a person and, thus, no automatic right to return of the funds existed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgments granting class certification, and denying the motion to dismiss filed by the circuit clerk and county.

People v. Borello


NO. 4-08-0504


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


389 Ill. App. 3d 985; 906 N.E.2d 1250; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 248; 329 Ill. Dec. 639



April 28, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Borello, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1496 (Ill., Sept. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 96CF427. Honorable Scott Drazewski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Scott County Circuit Court (Illinois) entered a judgment that dismissed defendant's pro se postconviction petition filed more than 10 years after he accepted a fully-negotiated guilty plea to four counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child in violation of 720 ILCS 5/12-14.1(a)(1) (1996) and after he had not filed a direct appeal of his convictions or resulting sentence. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered into a fully negotiated plea of guilty to four counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. He agreed to consecutive sentences of six years in prison on each charge, the sum total of which had to be served at 85 percent pursuant to a truth-in-sentencing law. He also received a sentence credit. He did not file a direct appeal. More than 11 years after he was sentenced, he filed a 735 ILCS 5/122-1 et seq. (2006) pro se postconviction relief petition. The trial court determined that the petition was not timely filed and that he had received the benefit of his plea. The appellate court found that the trial court erred in finding the petition to be untimely filed because the State had not raised that issue. However, it also found that he was not entitled to shorten his sentence by the mandatory supervised release (MSR) time that attached to it, but about which he had not been informed. The appellate court found that a reduction of his sentence due to the fact that the truth-in-sentencing law had been found unconstitutional meant that his ultimate sentence, even with the MSR, was considerably less than amount of time he agreed to under the plea bargain.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

996 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mott


NO. 4-07-0756


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


389 Ill. App. 3d 539; 906 N.E.2d 159; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 224; 329 Ill. Dec. 314



April 20, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Circuit Court of Clark County. No. 06CF105. Honorable Tracy W. Resch, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with unlawful possession of a controlled substance. The Circuit Court of Clark County (Illinois) granted defendant's motion to suppress, finding that a deputy did not have a reasonable suspicion to stop defendant's car to investigate a material obstruction of the driver's view out of her front windshield in violation of § 12-503(c) (625 ILCS 5/12-503(c) (2004)) of the Illinois Vehicle Code.


OVERVIEW: The State appealed. The appellate court held that the air freshener was significantly smaller than the deputy estimated on the witness stand. The air freshener was less than three inches wide at its widest point and only three inches tall. The deputy only articulated facts showing defendant had an air freshener suspended from her rearview mirror. The deputy's decision to pull defendant over was based upon a mistake of law. Defendant made a prima facie showing the search was unlawful, and the burden shifted to the State. Given the lack of specificity in the deputy's response and his overestimation of the air freshener's size, the trial court did not improperly find the deputy's testimony lacked credibility. Although made in good faith, the stop was pretextual for Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV purposes. The deputy never testified how he believed the air freshener might have materially obstructed defendant's view. Size alone did not determine whether an object materially obstructed the driver's view. The appellate court recommended that the Illinois legislature consider whether the approach used to regulate obstruction of drivers' views.


OUTCOME: The ruling on the motion to suppress was affirmed.

Raintree Homes, Inc. v. Vill. of Long Grove


No. 2-06-1105


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


389 Ill. App. 3d 836; 906 N.E.2d 751; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 221; 329 Ill. Dec. 553



April 15, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 19, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Raintree Homes, Inc. v. Vill. of Long Grove, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 933 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., May 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 98-MR-148. Honorable Margaret J. Mullen, Judge, Presiding.
Raintree Homes, Inc. v. Vill. of Long Grove, 209 Ill. 2d 248, 807 N.E.2d 439, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 362, 282 Ill. Dec. 815 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) in favor of plaintiff developer in the developer's declaratory judgment action wherein a village ordinance requiring the payment of impact fees as a condition of obtaining building permits was found unenforceable. The developer cross-appealed the trial court's denial of its motion for prejudgment interest.


OVERVIEW: As part of its judgment, the builder obtained a refund of the impact fees it paid to the village for 19 homes in built there between 1993 and 1997, namely an award of $ 114,700. The trial court found that the village exceeded its authority in enacting the ordinances imposing the impact fees and, therefore, determined that the ordinances were unenforceable. The court agreed, finding that as to the school impact fees charged, the trial court properly found that those fees were void under the Illinois Municipal Code, 65 ILCS 5/11-12-5(1)(b) (2000), which prohibited a cash donation for general operations, as opposed to school grounds, as the fees directed to be forwarded to a school's general operation fund. As to the open space impact fees, the court held that the trial court properly found that the fees were solely revenue oriented and that there was no evidence that the village ordinances considered anything individual to the developer's activity. As to the developer's cross-appeal, the court found that the village's actions were not fraudulent, therefore, there was no entitlement to collecting prejudgment interest against it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Stoffel


NO. 5-07-0314


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


389 Ill. App. 3d 238; 907 N.E.2d 79; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 217; 329 Ill. Dec. 760



April 14, 2009, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by People v. Stoffel, 233 Ill. 2d 592, 919 N.E.2d 363, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1843, 335 Ill. Dec. 644 (2009)
affirmed on other grounds by, Modified by, Remanded by People v. Stoffel, 2010 Ill. LEXIS 1896 (Ill., Dec. 23, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Fayette County. No. 04-CF-18. Honorable Michael D. McHaney, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court of Fayette County (Illinois) that dismissed his 735 ILCS 5/2-1401 petition for relief from judgment; defendant claimed that the trial court erred in failing to recharacterize his petition as a pleading filed under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 ILCS 5/122-1 et seq. (2006).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's appellate counsel, on three separate occasions, informed the court that defendant's petition was a postconviction petition, and each time the State failed to object to the characterization. In addition, defense counsel specifically asked the trial court to recharacterize the petition as a postconviction petition. The appellate court found, inter alia, that by appointing counsel to represent defendant and ordering counsel to file a Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 651(c) certificate, the trial court was treating defendant's pleading as a postconviction petition. While defendant's claims were subject to dismissal under § 2-1401, they were appropriately considered in a postconviction petition. Accordingly, the trial court abused its discretion by failing to recharacterize defendant's petition under § 5/122-1.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the cause was remanded with directions to recharacterize defendant's petition as a postconviction petition.

Jaason v. Sullivan


No. 1-08-1254


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


389 Ill. App. 3d 376; 906 N.E.2d 125; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 177; 329 Ill. Dec. 280



March 31, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 11, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Jaason v. Barbara J. Sullivan & B.J. Sullivan & Assocs., 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 1733 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Apr. 29, 2009)
Appeal denied by Jaason v. Sullivan, 233 Ill. 2d 560, 919 N.E.2d 353, 2009 Ill. LEXIS 1789, 335 Ill. Dec. 634 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. No. 07 L 013513. HONORABLE JAMES D. EGAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a beneficiary under a will, appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found that his legal malpractice action against defendants, an attorney and her law firm, were time barred and dismissed the action on that basis.


OVERVIEW: The beneficiary's action was based on the failure of a bequest to him due to defendants negligence in drafting the decedent's will. Defendants argued that the action was time barred pursuant to 735 ILCS 5/13-214.3(d) (1994). Under the statute, the beneficiary's action had to be filed within the time for filing a petition contesting the validity of the will or the time for filing claims against the estate, whichever was later. The deadline for contesting the validity of the will had passed by the time the malpractice action was filed. However, the action was filed before the time for filing claims against the estate had elapsed. Contrary to defendants assertion, 755 ILCS 5/18-3(a) (2006) allowed for more than one deadline for filing such claims. Separate deadlines could exist for claims by unknown creditors and known creditors. In the instant case, while the time in which unknown creditors could file claims had elapsed, the time for known creditors to file claims had not elapsed on the date the malpractice action was filed. Thus, the malpractice action was timely under § 13-214.3(d).


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

Knaus v. Guidry


No. 1-07-3509


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


389 Ill. App. 3d 804; 906 N.E.2d 644; 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 143; 329 Ill. Dec. 446



March 27, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 11, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. County Department, Law Division. Honorable Dennis J. Burke, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an attorney and his firm, challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that denied their motion to dismiss a complaint filed by appellees, residents of Florida and Missouri, for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The complaint alleged fraud, a violation of the Illinois Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act (815 ILCS 505/1 et seq. (2002)), conspiracy, breach of fiduciary duty, and conversion.


OVERVIEW: The attorney claimed that he and his firm had insufficient contacts with Illinois to be subject to long-arm jurisdiction under 735 ILCS 5/2-209(a) (2006). The sole issue was whether it was error to conclude that Illinois courts could exercise jurisdiction over appellants, who were Texas residents. Appellees conceded that appellants had not had continuous and systematic contact with Illinois so as to subject them to general personal jurisdiction, nor were appellants subject to specific personal jurisdiction. Appellees did not show that appellants purposefully directed their conduct towards Illinois so as to have an effect there. The purpose of the alleged conspiracy was to secure the money of the residents of Florida and Missouri through fraud. Any injury suffered by appellees was suffered in their home states, not in Illinois. Appellants' actions in furtherance of the conspiracy, including the attorney's transfer of funds allegedly stolen from appellees to an entity in Illinois, were not purposely directed towards Illinois. Appellants' activities did not meet the Rudzewicz test so as to subject them to in personam jurisdiction, even if the conspiracy theory of jurisdiction applied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order.
